1001 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Howard


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 1064; 435 N.Y.S.2d 399; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9987



January 22, 1981 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the County Court of Schenectady County (New York), which convicted defendant, upon a verdict, of two counts of assault in the second degree and one count of unlawful imprisonment in the first degree. Defendant assigned error in the denial of his motions to dismiss the admission of hospital records over his objection, and alleged a denial of constitutional right to assistance of counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was indicted on two counts of first-degree assault, first-degree unlawful imprisonment, and first-degree coercion. The trial court assigned counsel to defendant. Four months later, defendant requested and received a change of assigned counsel. Five months later, defendant again requested new counsel. The trial court refused the request and the second assigned counsel drew the jury. Defendant later appeared with retained counsel and the trial court permitted substitution. Defendant was convicted of assault and unlawful imprisonment. The court affirmed the convictions. The court held that complainant's hospital records indicating the extent of injuries were properly received under the business records rule. The court also held that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel because the retained trial lawyer did not select the jury. The court found that defendant freely chose to continue with retained counsel, although defendant was warned that retained counsel might not be as effective because it had not drawn the jury. The court also held that victim's loss of two front teeth was a permanent and serious injury under N.Y. Penal Law § 120.05(1).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for assault and unlawful imprisonment. The court held that complainant's hospital records indicating the extent of injuries were properly received under the business records rule and that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel. The court also held that complainant's loss of two front teeth was a permanent and serious injury under N.Y. penal law.

 

1002 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Slewett & Farber v. Board of Assessors


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


78 A.D.2d 403; 435 N.Y.S.2d 313; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9650



January 21, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Nassau County, entered January 31, 1979, affirmed insofar as appealed from, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners and respondents, County Board of Assessors and Board of Assessment, challenged a judgment from the Supreme Court at Special Term, Nassau County (New York), which had declared the latter three subdivisions of N.Y. Real Prop. Tax Law § 307 unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: At principal issue on these cross appeals were the validity and effect of certain legislative enactments, which retroactively altered the means and standards by which aggrieved taxpayers could establish inequality of assessed valuations of real property. The underlying controversy involved the rates at which real property in the county were assessed; the appellate questions pertained to the constitutionality of laws, which would nullify petitioners' judicial success in establishing those rates as identical to the equalization rates fixed for Nassau County by the State Board of Equalization and Assessment, which the trial court found to be unconstitutional. The court affirmed. Petitioners, who owned a large commercial parcel, instituted proceedings to review its assessment, alleging that for the years in issue their property was assessed at a higher ratio to fair market value than other property in the county. They could not claim an unequal assessment as compared to all other taxpayers or seek to recover a refund because a tax levy had cast on him an unequal share of the total burden of all taxpayers.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment from the trial court that the latter three subdivisions of a portion of the New York Real Property Tax Law were unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Assessment

Subdivisions 3, 4 and 5 of former section 307 of the Real Property Tax Law, which require inequality petitions to allege that the challenged assessments were made at a higher proportionate ratio to value than that of other property of the same major type, as defined by the State Board of Equalization and Assessment, and to offer evidence to such effect, are unconstitutional since although section 307 gives the appearance of merely regulating pleadings in tax review proceedings, it actually accomplishes a substantive remodeling of established law governing the imposition of taxes without further enabling legislation as to requisite details. Section 307 requires proof of inequality predicated upon comparison to a particular class of property rather than all property within the district, and because its provisions were made applicable to all pending causes of action, the ultimate effect [***3] of the section is to increase or decrease the amount at which property could be initially assessed; accordingly, the statute has the effect of retrospectively sanctioning a tax on real property by class or type, which renders it unconstitutional as applied to tax years prior to its effective date. The prospective operation of the same subdivisions suffers from similar fatal deficiencies since the class system of taxation set forth in subdivision 3 of section 307 is not imposed uniformly against all taxpayers of the varying classes in the taxing district, but only upon those who have pursued a judicial remedy against the sovereign, and nowhere in the entire structure of the 1978 legislation can there be found statutory authority for the tax assessor to assess classes of property at varying rates.

 

1003 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


First Broadcasting Corp. v. Syracuse


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


78 A.D.2d 490; 435 N.Y.S.2d 194; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9663



January 16, 1981 



DISPOSITION: Determination unanimously confirmed without costs and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner sought review of a determination by the Commissioner of Public Works of the City of Syracuse, which recommended the condemnation of an avigation easement above the owner's property as requested by respondent city.


OVERVIEW: The city began condemnation proceedings for the purpose of eliminating the aviation hazard to the airport caused by the property owner's radio towers. The commissioner found that the taking was for a public use and recommended the condemnation of the avigation easement. The property owner petitioned for review. The court held that (1) the property owner was not denied procedural due process during the hearing, (2) N.Y. Em. Dom. Proc. Law did not violate substantive due process, (3) N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law. § 355 gave the city the authority to condemn the right to unobstructed use of the airspace within 3,000 feet of a municipal airport, (4) the removal of the towers would have no environmental impact, (5) the determination and findings of the commissioner amply demonstrated that a public use would be served by the condemnation of the property owner's towers.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the determination and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Eminent Domain -- Avigation Easement

1. The determination and findings of the Commissioner of Public Works of the respondent city, which recommended the condemnation of an avigation easement above petitioner's property due to the presence of radio towers located near the municipal airport, are proper where they were made in accordance with EDPL article 2. The EDPL does not violate procedural due process inasmuch as the statute provides for a uniform procedure and requires public hearings, notice, publication of determinations and findings, and judicial review; the statute does not violate substantive due process since there is an applicable standard regarding the condemnation of property, i.e., land may only be taken for a public use.

Eminent Domain -- Avigation Easement

2. A municipality has the authority to condemn an interest in land outside its boundaries pursuant to section 355 of the General Municipal Law where such interest involves flight hazards which [***2] lie within 3,000 feet of a municipal airport or within such greater distance as the Federal Civil Aeronautics Administration or its successor may declare to be necessary; section 355 also permits the municipality to condemn the right to unobstructed use of the airspace within the same distance.

Eminent Domain -- Avigation Easement

3. In a proceeding concerning the condemnation of an avigation easement due to the presence of radio towers located near a municipal airport, the hearing officer made proper findings in regard to the environmental impact of the removal of the towers where such removal would have no environmental impact; furthermore, the hearing officer followed the requirement of EDPL 204 and stated the public use to be served by the easement.

Eminent Domain -- Avigation Easement

4. The determination and findings of the hearing officer, which recommended the condemnation of an avigation easement above petitioner's property due to the presence of radio towers located near a municipal airport, are proper where they amply demonstrate that a public use will be served by the condemnation; the determination of whether a taking of property is for a public [***3] use is a judicial question and the condemnation of land for an airport is for a public use.

People v. Boyd


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 975; 437 N.Y.S.2d 928; 1981 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9858



January 5, 1981 

 

1005 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Town of Olive v. Martins


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 822; 435 N.Y.S.2d 153; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14224



December 31, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowner appealed and plaintiff town cross-appealed from an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which denied the landowner's motion for summary judgment and partially granted the town's motion for summary judgment in an action brought by the town claiming the landowner violated its subdivision regulations.


OVERVIEW: The landowner acquired title to land on both sides of a public highway. The landowner's deed described the land in separate parcel descriptions although all of it was contiguous except as bisected by the highway. The parcel on the northerly side of the road was divided into five lots, four being sold and the fifth being retained by the landowner. The town contended the division violated the subdivision regulations of the town. The landowner contended that the use of the word "parcel" as the description of land subject to subdivision was either too vague to encompass lands separately described in a deed or did not, as a matter of law, apply to her. The parties cross-appealed from the trial court's order and the court held that the words "parcel of land" were sufficient to convey the meaning of a contiguous area being subject to encompassment in a singular description of the land referred to at the time it is divided into five lots by its owner. The court held that the town was entitled to summary judgment declaring the regulations constitutional because the definition of a subdivision was not unconstitutionally vague as applied to the landowner.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order of the trial court by granting the town's motion for summary judgment. The court affirmed the order of the trial court as modified and remitted the matter to the trial court for further proceedings.

 

1006 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Polli v. Connelie


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


78 A.D.2d 151; 435 N.Y.S.2d 363; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13400



December 24, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, and petition dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent applicants sought to take a competitive written examination for the position of New York State trooper. Appellant, Superintendent of the New York State Police, refused to permit them to take the exam, relying on N.Y. Exec. Law § 215, subdiv. 3. The Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York) directed that the applicants be permitted to take the examination. The superintendent sought review.


OVERVIEW: The superintendent refused to permit the applicants to take the examination because they were over the age limit specified in § 215, subdiv. 3. In addition, none of the applicants claimed any previous military duty that would extend the § 215, subdiv. 3 age limit. The lower court ruled that in the absence of appropriate standards, the discretion conferred on the superintendent violated the equal protection clause of N.Y. Const. art. I, § 11. The court rejected this ruling and reversed the lower court's judgment. The court held that the applicants did not ask the superintendent to invoke his powers of discretion in their favor and that even if § 215, subdiv. 3 represented an unlawful delegation of lawmaking power, the claimed deficiency would not benefit the applicants. Section 215, subdiv. 3 specified that no one over age 29 was eligible for appointment unless the superintendent, in the exercise of discretion, decided to extend that primary limitation. Because a declaration striking down this flexibility as unconstitutional would leave a proper maximum age limitation of 29 years fully intact, the court held that the applicants would still be ineligible for the examination.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's judgment and dismissed the petition.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- State Police -- Examinations -- Age Limitations for State Troopers

Where petitioners, all of whom are well under 35 years of age, but two of whom were born more than 29 years before the date of a scheduled competitive examination for the position of State trooper, and one of whom would have become 29 prior to the expected appointment date, were not permitted to take the examination, and thereafter challenged subdivision 3 of section 215 of the Executive Law which provides that no person shall be appointed to the New York State Police force unless he is between the ages of 21 and 29 years except that the superintendent, in his discretion, may extend the maximum age to 35 years, the petition is dimissed;  [***2] the maximum age limitation of 29 years is valid (see Matter of Figueroa v Bronstein, 38 NY2d 533, app dsmd 429 U.S. 806), and even if the discretionary provision allowing the superintendent to extend the maximum age to 35 were constitutionally invalid, the 29-year limitation would be left intact.

 

1007 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Mansell


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FIRST DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 582; 434 N.Y.S.2d 352; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13911



December 23, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which convicted him of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the first degree under former N.Y. Penal Law § 220.21 and imposed an indeterminate sentence of two years to life.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant of the A-I felony of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the first degree under former N.Y. Penal Law § 220.21, and imposed an indeterminate sentence of two years to life. Defendant sought review of the trial court's decision. On appeal, the court modified the trial court's judgment by vacating the sentence, finding that the sentencing of defendant for an A-I felony conviction to an indeterminate term of two years to life violated N.Y. Penal Law § 70.00(3)(a)(1) because § 70.00(3)(a)(1) required a minimum sentence of not less than 15 years. The court affirmed the trial court's decision as modified and remanded the case to the trial court for resentencing.


OUTCOME: The court modified the trial court's decision that had convicted defendant of criminal possession of a controlled substance in the first degree and had imposed a sentence of two years to life by vacating the sentence, affirmed the trial court's decision as modified, and remanded the case for resentencing.

 

1008 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Caso v. New York State Public High School Athletic Asso.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


78 A.D.2d 41; 434 N.Y.S.2d 60; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13405



December 12, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant parent sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court of Onondaga County (New York), which, in a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding, denied the parent's motion to overrule a determination of respondent public high school athletic association (athletic association), that prohibited the parent's son from participating in high school interscholastic athletics due to a violation of eligibility rules.


OVERVIEW: The parent's son participated in an international gymnastic competition in violation of the athletic association's interscholastic sports rules and was declared ineligible to participate in the sport for the remainder of the season. The parent argued that the athletic association's actions stigmatized his son's reputation, thereby jeopardizing his liberty interests under the Due Process clause. The court affirmed, holding that participation in interscholastic high school competitions was not considered a substantial right unless the athletic association's denial of that right was based on an abuse of the son's fundamental rights or predicated on a suspect basis, e.g. religion or race. The court found that the denial was based on the son's violation of the athletic association's unambiguous rule. The athletic association did not act arbitrarily and capriciously because the son had participated in outside competition in violation of the athletic association's rule that prescribed a loss of eligibility, and no hearing was required on the part of the athletic association to find either a violation of the rule or to fix a sanction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the supreme court which denied the parent's motion to overrule the athletic association's determination prohibiting the parent's son from participating in high school interscholastic athletics due to the son's violation of the athletic association's eligibility rules.


HEADNOTES

Appeal -- Academic and Moot Questions

1. Although a proceeding concerns a denial of eligibility to a high school student to participate in athletic events already concluded, the issue is not moot where the case is one in which the underlying questions are of general interest, have substantial public importance and are likely to recur.

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- When Remedy Appropriate -- Exhausting Administrative Remedies

2. A CPLR article 78 proceeding is the appropriate remedy to compel private corporations to fulfill obligations imposed upon them by statute as well as by their internal rules. The general rule is that one must exhaust available administrative remedies prior to seeking relief from a court of law; however, the exhaustion [***2] rule is not inflexible and need not follow when the action is challenged as either unconstitutional or outside of a grant of power, when resort to an administrative remedy would be futile or when its pursuit would cause irreparable injury.

Schools -- Participation of Students in Interscholastic Athletics

3. Although an athletic association's actions may be deemed State action and cause injury to a student athlete, participation in interscholastic high school competitions is not a substantial right, and thus there is no violation of due process, unless denial of participation is based on an abuse of a student's fundamental rights or predicated on a suspect basis; a student athlete is not denied due process by having his good name and reputation jeopardized due to his being declared ineligible from participating in interscholastic sports where he waived his right to a factual hearing, neither presenting proof of harm, if any, nor utilizing the opportunity to purge any alleged stain on his name, and the athletic association provided a vehicle to review all questions of eligibility.

Schools -- Participation of Students in Interscholastic Athletics

4. A student [***3] athlete who had his privilege to participate in high school interscholastic athletics withdrawn due to a violation of an eligibility rule is not denied equal protection where the classifications in the rule are neither inherently suspect nor a violation of a fundamental right, but rather are grounded in and reasonably related to legitimate State interests.

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- When Remedy Appropriate

5. A determination by respondent athletic association, which withdrew a student's privilege to participate in high school interscholastic athletics due to a violation of eligibility rules, does not come within CPLR 7803 (subd 3) where there is no showing that respondent violated lawful procedure, was affected by an error of law, acted arbitrarily and capriciously, abused its discretion or inflicted an unwarranted measure or mode of penalty.

Schools -- Jurisdiction of Athletic Associations

6. An athletic association has jurisdiction to withdraw a student's privilege to participate in high school interscholastic athletics due to a violation of eligibility rules inasmuch as the association controls certain interscholastic sports competitions and [***4] if an individual wishes to participate in those events, then he comes under the jurisdiction of the association; he has no inherent right to participate otherwise.

 

1009 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Camardo v. Board of Education


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, FOURTH DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 864; 434 N.Y.S.2d 514; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14280



December 12, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowners sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court of New York, Monroe County, which declared that defendants' school reorganization plan was not a contract impairment or unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendants created a school reorganization plan. The homeowners filed an action against defendants alleging that: (1) earlier legislation created a contract which promised them the right to maintain their own school districts and the right to attend city schools tuition free; and (2) the contract could not be repudiated by subsequent legislation. The trial court granted defendants' motion for a declaratory judgment. It determined that the reorganization plan was not a contract impairment or unconstitutional. The homeowners appealed. The court affirmed the judgment because the homeowners failed to prove the elements necessary to a contractual relation and their constitutional challenges were without merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the declaratory judgment in favor of defendants.

 

1010 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Adoption of XX


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


77 A.D.2d 381; 434 N.Y.S.2d 772; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13387



December 11, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father sought review of the decision of the Family Court, Ulster County (New York), which denied the father's motion to open, vacate and/or set aside an order of adoption entered by the trial court under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111-a.


OVERVIEW: The mother and the father lived together for approximately two years prior to the birth of the child. The father claimed that the mother disappeared, taking the baby with her. The mother and the stepfather married, and a year later the mother and the stepfather commenced adoption proceedings. Approximately 26 months after the birth of the child, although he had never supported the child, filed a paternity petition. The trial court signed the adoption order and subsequently denied the father's motion to vacate the adoption order. The court affirmed and held that the father could have insured his right to notice of the adoption proceeding by signing the putative father registry created by § 111-a and N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 372-c. He failed to do so. Further, although N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111-a was declared unconstitutional after the adoption proceeding was closed, the decision was not entitled to retroactive effect in view of the well-settled legal doctrine that final dispositions should not be disturbed by a subsequent change in the decisional law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of the father's motion to vacate the adoption order.


HEADNOTES

Adoption -- Notice to Putative Father

Petitioner's motion to have an adoption order vacated on the ground that he is the natural father of the child and, as such, should have received notice of the adoption proceeding and been afforded an opportunity to be heard, was properly denied, where he did not comply with the requirements of section 111-a of the Domestic Relations Law, which provides that notice of an adoption proceeding must be given the father of a child born out of wedlock in certain situations; said statute is not constitutionally infirm, and, further, a United States Supreme Court decision handed down six weeks after the adoption order was granted, holding that an unwed father, like an unwed mother, may now veto an adoption of his child merely by refusing to give his consent, absent a showing of abandonment, neglect or surrender ( Caban v Mohammed, 441 U.S. 380), is not entitled to retroactive [***2] effect in view of the well-settled legal doctrine that final dispositions should not be disturbed by a subsequent change in decisional law.

Wilson v. Levitt


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 742; 434 N.Y.S.2d 815; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14146



December 11, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant former employee sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), which dismissed the former employee's application, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, to review a determination by respondent Comptroller of the State of New York, which disapproved the former employee's application for ordinary disability retirement benefits.


OVERVIEW: While at home, the former employee fell and sustained a fractured hip. The injury and its debilitating residual effects ultimately caused the employee's termination. The employee applied to the Comptroller for an ordinary disability retirement allowance, but his application was disapproved because he was not actually in service at the time the application was filed. On review, the court affirmed. The court found that the former employee was not "in service" at the time his application was filed. The former employee's assertion of a denial of equal protection was unavailing because he was not a member of a protected class.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissal of the former employee's application to review a determination by the Comptroller.

Cooper v. Tully


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 757; 434 N.Y.S.2d 794; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14157



December 11, 1980 

 

1013 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Ranz v. Sposato


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


77 A.D.2d 408; 435 N.Y.S.2d 723; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13358



December 9, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on April 22, 1980, affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.

[See 79 AD2d 594.] 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant out-of-state insurer sought review of an order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which denied its motion for summary judgment in the action by plaintiff administratrix against defendant insured for the death of the deceased in an automobile accident. The administratrix had obtained an order attaching the contractual obligation of the insurer to appear, defend, and to pay any judgment to the limits of the policy.


OVERVIEW: No motion was made by the insurer to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction nor was the jurisdictional issue preserved by a responsive pleading as permitted by N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211(e). The insurer contended that subject matter jurisdiction could not be conferred upon the court even by consent or stipulation and was subject to attack at any time. The court affirmed, finding that the jurisdiction was personal and that the insurer, by its failure to raise the issue either by motion or by answer, waived the initial defect in jurisdiction under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211(e). Hence, the insurer had no right to file a motion to dismiss. It was plain that the purpose of the amendment to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 320(c) was not to alter the nature of the jurisdiction obtained, but rather to limit the liability flowing from an unconditional appearance in response to a warrant of attachment. Notwithstanding the limitation of liability to the face amount of the policy, the underlying jurisdiction remained personal because the appearance by the insurer was unconditional. The court granted leave for a certified question to be presented to the court of appeals in order to facilitate a speedy final disposition.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying the motion filed by the out-of-state insurer and the insured for summary judgment and dismissal of the administratrix's complaint for lack of jurisdiction.


HEADNOTES

Attachment -- Insurance Policy of Nonresident

In an action commenced after plaintiff's intestate, a New York resident, died as a consequence of an accident in Pennsylvania involving a vehicle owned and operated by defendants, Pennsylvania residents, defendants' motion for summary judgment is denied, jurisdiction having been obtained by attachment of the contractual obligation of defendants' insurer to appear, defend and pay any judgment procured to the limits of the policy; following joinder of issue, no motion was made by defendants to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction nor was the jurisdictional issue preserved by the responsive pleading ( CPLR 3211, subds [a], [e]), and the jurisdiction involved is personal jurisdiction rather than subject matter jurisdiction; accordingly, defendants have waived the initial defect in jurisdiction [***2] by their failure to raise the issue either by motion or by answer, and the right to move vanished.

 

1014 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rosenfeld v. Isaacs


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 630; 433 N.Y.S.2d 623; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13983



December 8, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff administrator sought review of an order from the Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York), which granted defendant tortfeasors' motion for partial summary judgment, dismissing the cause of action for punitive damages in the administrator's action to recover damages for the wrongful death and conscious pain and suffering of the administrator's decedent.


OVERVIEW: The administrator brought an action against the tortfeasors, seeking to recover damages for the wrongful death and conscious pain and suffering of the administrator's decedent and claimed that punitive damages were recoverable because of the allegedly egregious manner in which the decedent died. The tortfeasors filed a motion for partial summary judgment and the trial court granted it, dismissing the administrator's cause of action for punitive damages. The administrator appealed and the court affirmed, holding that because actions to recover damages for wrongful death and conscious pain and suffering did not exist at common law and were created by legislative enactments, such enactments pre-empted the area, and as the rights accorded by statute were in derogation of the common law, the right to sue for injury sustained due to the death of another were founded in statutory authority. The court determined it was not free to consider the relative merits of arguments in favor of, or against, the limitations of damage recovery because the legislature had "struck a balance" for the court. The court concluded that the administrator's arguments were solely for the legislature's ears.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order, with costs and disbursements, granting the tortfeasors' motion for partial summary judgment and thereby dismissing the administrator's cause of action for punitive damages in his action against the tortfeasors to recover damages for the wrongful death and conscious pain and suffering of the administrator's decedent.

 

1015 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Aurnou v. Leggett


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, SECOND DEPARTMENT


79 A.D.2d 623; 433 N.Y.S.2d 811; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13972



December 5, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, counsel for defendant in a criminal proceeding, filed a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to prohibit respondent judge of the County Court of Westchester County (New York) from enforcing an order requiring counsel to produce certain material for an in camera inspection so that its discoverability by the People under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 240.40(1) could be assessed. The People sought to dismiss the proceeding.


OVERVIEW: The trial court ordered counsel to produce certain material for the trial court's in camera inspection in connection with claims by the People that the material was discoverable under Here, the trial court ordered that certain material be produced by defendant for an in camera inspection, in order to assist the court in determining whether the material was discoverable by the People under § 240.40(1). The court granted the People's motion to dismiss the petition. It held that the trial court's order did not represent such a serious excess of power so vitally different from other trial rulings of constitutional import as to warrant the court's interference with the trial. Noting its concern about establishing a significant precedent under which collateral proceedings are permitted to interrupt ongoing criminal trials, the court held that the constitutional issues urged by defendant was not so critical that it justified special treatment being meted out by the court during an ongoing criminal trial. The court thereupon granted the People's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court granted the People's motion to dismiss defense counsel's petition for review of the county court's order requiring production of materials for an in camera inspection to determine discoverability.

 

1016 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Guardianship of Victory


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


78 A.D.2d 843; 433 N.Y.S.2d 445; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13529



November 25, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant father challenged an order of the Family Court, New York County (New York), which excluded him from participating in a fact-finding hearing that was brought by respondent hospital to obtain guardianship and custody of the father's child who was born out of wedlock and to free him for adoption and which allowed the father to participate in the dispositional hearing.


OVERVIEW: The child was placed with the hospital after his mother, who was now dead, attempted suicide. The father, who had spent time in mental hospitals, was employed and manifested a desire for custody of his child or to have custody turned over to the maternal grandmother. The father was excluded from the fact-finding hearing on the ground that only the parents whose consent to adoption under N.Y. Dom. Rel. Law § 111 was required were entitled to have been heard. Although § 111(1)(c) stated that only the consent of the mother was required for adoption when the child was born out of wedlock, a recent decision held that § 111(1)(c) was unconstitutional because it was a denial of equal protection. Thus, the father's exclusion from the fact-finding hearing was improper. Although the hearing was held prior to the recent decision, the court applied the decision retroactively because no reliance interest existed. No adoption had taken place. No familial or financial interests were jeopardized. All that was at stake was the father's right to participate in and to have been heard at all stages of a proceeding that might have led to the adoption of his child. Thus, the court reversed the judgment.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the family court's decision, which excluded the father from participating in a fact-finding hearing that was brought by the hospital to obtain guardianship and custody of the father's child and to free him for adoption. The court remanded for a new hearing.

 

1017 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Holmes v. Planning Bd. of New Castle


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


78 A.D.2d 1; 433 N.Y.S.2d 587; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13403



November 17, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Westchester County, dated February 28, 1978, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, and matter remitted to the Planning Board of the Town of New Castle for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owners sought approval of respondent planning board for a proposed addition to an office building on their property. The board conditioned approval of the owners' site plan upon their consent to an easement burdening their property. The Supreme Court in Westchester County (New York) determined that this was within the planning board's power. Petitioners appealed from that judgment.


OVERVIEW: The board had the responsibility of site plan review and conditioned its approval of the owner's proposed addition to their office space on the owners' consent to an easement. The court rejected the owners' argument that the board imposed an arbitrary condition upon them in their efforts to curb traffic congestion or that the condition constituted a compensable taking. The court found that 1) the board was authorized to approve the petitioners' site plan conditionally, and that the traffic congestion was a proper subject for the board's concern; 2) a police power reasonable relationship test had to be applied when scrutinizing the condition with respect to its effects upon the application for proposed development; 3) there was a reasonable relationship between the problem that would result from the effectuation of the application's proposed development and the conditional solution designed to alleviate it; and 4) the burdened property was capable of a reasonable return; however, the board's concept did not specify the means by which the intended result was to be achieved, which defeated the plan and consequently, the condition based thereon was vague and also had to be stricken.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court finding that the board had the power to condition approval of the owners site plan on their consent to an easement. The court remanded the matter for the articulation of an implementation plan so that the owners had the possibility to discover the full extent of the participation required from them and the benefits and burdens they would have incurred incur under the plan.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Planning Board -- Conditional Approval of Site Plan

A condition imposed by respondent town planning board as a requisite of its approval of a site plan submitted by petitioners property owners, which condition requires petitioners' consent to grants of reciprocal access easements with all other property owners encompassed by a limited goal plan adopted by the board that is intended to provide a partial solution to the problem of traffic congestion on a small section of the main east-west artery within the town business district by using [***2] interconnected parking lots and common access drives as the relief mechanisms, but which is a conceptual, rather than a specific plan, is impermissibly vague and must be stricken; although the condition imposed is a reasonable exercise of the planning board's authority (Town Law, § 274-a) and is constitutionally valid as it is in furtherance of the public health, safety and welfare and there is a reasonable relationship between the problem and the solution proposed to alleviate it, which is internally consistent, is compatible with regional and State planning goals and is not inherently confiscatory, the matter must be remanded to the planning board for a more complete formulation of the underlying plan, inasmuch as the final effects of the condition on petitioners' property cannot be determined by reference to said amorphous plan, e.g., whether apparently similar bordering properties not included in the plan will be similarly burdened and whether petitioners' projected loss of parking spaces under the plan will result in a reduction of their investment in the property.

1019 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Legal Aid Soc. v. Schenectady


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


78 A.D.2d 933; 433 N.Y.S.2d 234; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13699



November 13, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner property owner instituted the instant proceeding pursuant to N.Y. Em. Dom. Proc. Law § 207, to review the determination and findings made by respondent city relative to the acquisition of certain real property owned by the property owner.


OVERVIEW: In an effort to provide free off-street parking in the downtown district, the city proposed to acquire the property owner's property. The property owner contended that the city failed to give the required statutory notice pursuant to N.Y. Em. Dom. Proc. Law § 202; that the notice provision of § 202 was unconstitutional as a violation of due process; that the public hearing was improperly conducted and contrary to N.Y. Em. Dom. Proc. Law § 203; that the property owner was not given adequate notice of the city's final determinations; and that the findings of fact were insufficient to support the conclusions. The court found all the arguments without merit, concluding that the city's findings and the determination for acquiring the property were duly published pursuant to N.Y. Em. Dom. Proc. Law §§ 202-204, and moreover, the content of the notice, although brief, was sufficient in that the purpose, the location, and the general effect of the proposed project were all contained therein. The court therefore confirmed the city's determination and denied the property owner's motion for an order directing the city to file a further record pursuant to N.Y. Em. Dom. Proc. Law § 207.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the city's findings regarding the notice provided to the property owner in connection with the acquisition of its property for the purpose of providing off-street downtown parking.
