1043 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Cintron


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


74 A.D.2d 457; 428 N.Y.S.2d 267; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10858



May 27, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Kings County, rendered January 18, 1977 and amended on January 31, 1977, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the Kings County Supreme Court (New York), entered upon a jury verdict, convicting him of second-degree murder and criminal possession of a weapon after the trial court, inter alia, failed to sua sponte charge the jury on a potential defense of intoxication, following testimony that defendant, on the night in question, had consumed approximately 40 alcoholic drinks.


OVERVIEW: At defendant's murder trial, two prosecution witnesses testified that they saw defendant carefully shoot the victim several times in an occupied drinking establishment and then bury the body in the cellar of the bar. Defendant testified that he was not involved. Although he claimed he had consumed about 40 alcoholic drinks that night, he further testified he was not drunk. Defendant requested a manslaughter instruction, but he did not request a jury instruction on an intoxication defense. Neither instruction was given, and he was convicted. Defendant appealed, claiming, inter alia, that the failure of the trial court to charge the jury on an intoxication defense was reversible error. In affirming, the court rejected defendant's argument and ruled that defendant could not interject hindsight into the proceedings to upset a properly obtained conviction. Defendant had made a reasoned decision not to pursue an intoxication defense in favor of an absolute denial, so presenting the intoxication issue to the jury was not justified. However, even if the jury had been so instructed, intoxication did not necessarily negate the ability of defendant to form the intent to kill.


OUTCOME: The convictions were affirmed because defendant did not request an intoxication instruction and hindsight could not be interjected into the appeal to upset a properly obtained conviction. The court held that the positions taken by defendant at trial did not justify the presentation of an intoxication factor to the jury since he had made a reasoned decision not to pursue that course.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Instructions -- Intoxication

Upon a trial for murder, the trial court was not, sua sponte, obligated to charge the jury on the potential defense of intoxication as it related to the issue of intent where the defendant, at the time he took the stand, chose to deny any involvement in the crime, as opposed to asserting a claim of diminished capacity, and there was not even a scintilla of objective or subjective proof prior to defendant testifying which in any way indicated intoxication; there is a subjective element of intoxication and even an inebriated individual may be capable of forming an intent.

 

1044 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Central Buffalo Project Corp. v. Buffalo


Appeal Nos. 1, 2


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


74 A.D.2d 336; 428 N.Y.S.2d 102; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10841



May 23, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Appeal No. 1. -- Order unanimously reversed, with costs to plaintiff, and motion for summary judgment granted. Appeal No. 2 -- Appeal unanimously dismissed as moot.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed from the decision of the Supreme Court, Erie County (New York), which denied its motion for summary judgment in its action against defendant city constitutionally challenging the amount of taxes collected by the city.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer brought an action for refunds for taxes illegally collected by the city in excess of its constitutional limits. The taxpayer brought a motion for summary judgment, which was denied by the trial court. The basis for denial was that the taxes had not been shown to be collected illegally inasmuch as the statute that authorized collection of the taxes, 1976 N.Y. Laws ch. 349, 484, had not been explicitly declared unconstitutional. On appeal, the court reversed. The issue involved a complicated tax assessment ratio. The court concluded that the burden to establish the constitutionality of the ratios should not be on the taxpayer. To find the city had established a question of fact created a monumental burden of proof requiring the taxpayer to prove the full value of all property in Buffalo during the years 1970-1977. Such a trial would consume enormous resources from both of the parties and the trial court without producing an appreciable gain in the accuracy of the ratios established. It imposed no undue hardship upon the city to require it to do what the taxpayer could not do and challenge the ratios directly in an administrative proceeding created for that very purpose.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and granted the summary judgment motion brought by the taxpayer in its refund action against the city.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Constitutional Limitation on Real Property Taxes

Summary judgment is granted to plaintiff taxpayer in an action to recover refunds of real property taxes illegally collected by a municipality in excess of its constitutional limits when the city exceeded its maximum taxing power by excluding pension and retirement benefits from the computation (see Bethlehem Steel Corp. v Board of Educ., 61 AD2d 147, affd 44 NY2d 831; Hurd v City of Buffalo, 34 NY2d 628); furthermore, the municipality is bound by the equalization ratios upon which it relied and is estopped from denying the validity of the ratios, since it failed to challenge [***2] the ratios before the State Board of Equalization and Assessment.

 

1045 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Martin v. Martin


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


74 A.D.2d 419; 427 N.Y.S.2d 1002; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10852



May 23, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously modified, on the law and facts, and, as modified, affirmed, without costs, in accordance with opinion by Simons, J. P.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The New York Supreme Court (New York) granted plaintiff husband a divorce and custody of the children. In a countersuit resolved in the same judgment, the wife was granted a divorce and the trial court found the separation agreement between the parties unfair. The husband appealed from so much of the judgment as voided the separation agreement and ordered him to pay his wife's counsel fees.


OVERVIEW: The husband filed a petition for divorce on the grounds of adultery and cruel and inhuman treatment. The wife filed her own petition for divorce in a countersuit on the grounds of the husband's cruel treatment. The trial court granted the wife's petition and voided the separation agreement between the parties, finding that it was unfair. The husband appealed, and the court modified and affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The court applied the best interest test and affirmed the trial court's determination that the children should be with the husband. The court also affirmed the trial court's award of attorney fees to the wife, rejecting the husband's argument that the statutory provision for attorney fees was discriminatory against men. The court modified the trial court's judgment, however, in that it voided the separation agreement. The court held that the agreement was the subject of extensive bargaining between the parties in which the wife had the advice of her minister and lawyer.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court voiding the couple's separation agreement and awarding the wife counsel fees was modified and affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Husband and Wife -- Separation Agreement

1. A husband's failure or refusal to disclose his financial circumstances when he executes a separation agreement with his wife is not sufficient to void an agreement fair on its face, particularly when the wife was represented by counsel during the negotiations and execution. Accordingly, the court erred in granting defendant wife's application to rescind a provision in a separation agreement as unconscionable based on the disparity between the consideration paid to her to convey her interest in the marital home and the value of her share of the equity, which disparity was allegedly the product of her husband's overreaching through nondisclosure, where the agreement was the subject of [***2] extensive negotiation during conferences in which defendant had the advice of her minister and her lawyer, she complied with its terms for almost a year, she knew the original cost of the house as well as the approximate value of the house when the agreement was drawn, she knew of her husband's general financial condition and the agreement as a whole represents a bargain which someone in her position might reasonably accept in an effort to resolve her marital difficulties, since, even if it could be said that the husband failed in some duty of good faith, his wife was not misled and did not rely upon his misconduct.

Parent and Child -- Custody

2. In a proceeding involving two natural parents, custody is to be determined solely by what is in the best interest of the child and the disposition of the trial court should not be reversed in the absence of manifest error or an abuse of discretion. Accordingly, although generally when children have been living with one parent for a long period of time and the parties have previously agreed that custody shall remain in that parent, their agreement should prevail and custody should be continued unless it is demonstrated that the [***3] custodial parent is unfit or perhaps less fit, where the parents' separation agreement did not address or resolve long-term custody of the children, Trial Term proceeded correctly when it declined to give controlling weight to the provisions of the separation agreement giving custody to the mother or to the fact that the children had previously lived with their mother after their father moved out of the house and, applying the best interests of the child test, awarded custody to the father.

Parent and Child -- Custody

3. A wife's adultery does not, ipso facto, warrant her loss of custody of the parties' children.

Husband and Wife -- Divorce -- Counsel Fees

4. The United States Supreme Court decision declaring an Alabama statute similar to section 237 of the Domestic Relations Law, which authorizes the award of counsel fees in an action for annulment, separation or divorce only in favor of the wife, to be unconstitutional because it violates the equal protection clause, is binding on the New York courts and shall be applied prospectively; moreover, a husband who did not challenge the constitutionality of section 237 at trial has standing to raise the issue [***4] on appeal. However, section 237 is construed to be gender neutral, authorizing relief to either spouse when appropriate, and, accordingly, an award of counsel fees to the wife under section 237 is upheld on a finding that, on the evidence, the statute was not unconstitutionally applied.

 

1046 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thomas


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


74 A.D.2d 317; 428 N.Y.S.2d 20; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10839



May 19, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Kings County, rendered September 5, 1978, reversed, on the law, plea vacated, and matter remitted to Criminal Term for further proceedings consistent with the opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the decision of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which convicted defendant, upon a conditional guilty plea, of reckless endangerment in the first degree and criminal possession of two weapons. Defendant contended that the evidence was insufficient to establish the elements of reckless endangerment and that N.Y. Penal Law § 265.15(3)'s statutory presumption was unconstitutional as applied to his case.


OVERVIEW: Although defendant admitted the facts underlying the charges against him during the allocution, defendant's guilty plea was conditioned upon his ability to raise two issues on appeal. Defendant asked the court to determine whether the requisite elements of reckless endangerment in the first degree were satisfied by the proof available to the prosecution and whether § 265.15(3)'s statutory presumption of weapons possession was constitutional as applied to the facts of his case. The court reversed and remanded to give defendant an opportunity to plead again finding that the issues were not reviewable. The court determined that defendant's appeal sought review of issues of factual guilt, which was inconsistent with his admission of factual guilt. Therefore, the court found that his appeal was not logically or legally consistent with his guilty plea. The court also concluded that the limited plea record was insufficient for the court to determine whether § 265.15(3)'s statutory presumption was unconstitutional as applied. The factual issues regarding the location of defendant's guns in the car and his ability to reach them from the driver's seat required resolution at a trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction and remanded to give defendant the opportunity to plead anew because he was foreclosed from raising factual issues of guilt on appeal and because his conditional guilty plea was given in reliance on his ability to pursue the appellate remedy that he attempted to preserve.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Plea of Guilty -- Appeal

1. Where a defendant, pursuant to an agreement with the District Attorney, entered a conditional plea of guilty to several counts of an indictment against him and preserved for appeal issues as to the sufficiency of the facts alleged to constitute one of the charges against him and the constitutionality of the presumption of possession of weapons in subdivision 3 of section 265.15 of the Penal Law as applied to the facts in the case, the judgment of conviction is reversed and the matter remanded to give defendant the opportunity to plead anew as the appeal is not properly before the Appellate Division; conditional [***2] pleas which attempt to preserve issues which lose their relevancy once the defendant has asserted his factual guilt are precluded, and the State's statutory scheme has provided an expansive approach to appealability by preserving the right to raise postplea objection where suppression motions asserting claims of illegally obtained or improperly tainted evidence have been denied. Defendant is seeking a review of issues of factual guilt following an admission of factual guilt and the appeal is not logically or legally consistent with the plea; on the limited record it could not be determined whether the statutory presumption was unconstitutional as applied.

Crimes -- Plea of Guilty -- Appeal

2. As a general rule, a plea of guilty, intelligently and voluntarily entered, operates as a waiver of certain fundamental constitutional defects and bars the later assertion of constitutional challenges to pretrial proceedings; therefore, only those issues fully disclosed in the record which relate either to the exercise of jurisdiction by the court or to the voluntary and knowing nature of the plea are appealable after a plea of guilty. Since a guilty plea is not merely a confession [***3] but is itself a "conviction", objections which go to the factual finding of guilt and not either to the right of the People to prosecute or to the validity of the plea itself are deemed waived by such a plea.

 

1047 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Darienzo v. Wise Shoe Stores, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


74 A.D.2d 342; 427 N.Y.S.2d 831; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10842



May 12, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Appeal from an order of the Supreme Court, Kings County, dated October 23, 1978, dismissed as academic. That order was superseded by the order of resettlement dated February 15, 1979.

Order of the same court, dated February 15, 1979 affirmed.

Respondents are awarded one bill of costs payable by appellant.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant manufacturer sought review of the judgment from the Supreme Court Kings County (New York), which denied the manufacturer's motions to dismiss, for lack of in personam jurisdiction, the third party complaints brought by respondents, retailer and distributor, in the customer's action to recover personal injury damages.


OVERVIEW: The customer was injured when a defect in her shoe caused her to fall. The customer sought personal injury damages from the retailer and the distributor. The retailer and the distributor brought third party complaints against the manufacturer. The trial court denied the manufacturer's motion to dismiss. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that N.Y. C.P.L.R. 302(a)(3)(ii) allowed the trial court to exercise personal jurisdiction over the manufacturer. Under their business arrangement, the distributor solicited the sale from the retailer and then contracted with the manufacturer for the shoes. The manufacturer had no sales department and only manufactured those shoes that were ordered by the distributor. The court found that the manufacturer relied on this relationship in order to insulate itself from in personam jurisdiction in the state. The evidence established that the manufacturer had ties to interstate commerce with the reasonable expectation of forum consequences in the state resulting from the anticipated and intended sale of its products to consumers within the state. Therefore the due process requirements of minimum contacts and substantial fairness were satisfied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of the manufacture's motions to dismiss the third party complaints brought by the retailer and distributor in the customer's personal injury action.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- Jurisdiction -- Long-Arm Jurisdiction

1. In an action for negligence and breach of warranty concerning personal injuries sustained by plaintiff when the heel of her shoe separated from the shank causing her to fall from the platform of an elevated train station into the tracks below, a denial of motions by third-party defendant,  [***2] a New Hampshire corporation, to dismiss third-party complaints against it for lack of in personam jurisdiction is proper where the corporation derived substantial revenue from interstate commerce and had a reasonable expectation of forum consequences in New York resulting from the anticipated and intended sale of its shoes to New York consumers ( CPLR 302, subd [a], par 3, cl [ii]), inasmuch as these circumstances establish sufficient forum ties and satisfy the due process requirements of minimum contacts and substantial fairness; despite a technical intermediate sale by third-party defendant to another New Hampshire corporation, which shares common officers and appears to have virtual identity of shareholders, it is apparent that third-party defendant's existence was entirely dependent upon interstate commerce since it packaged the shoes for interstate shipment and directly delivered them to a common carrier.

Constitutional Law -- Due Process of Law -- In Personam Jurisdiction

2. Due process requires that a defendant may not be subject to the in personam jurisdiction of a State court unless that defendant has certain minimal contacts, ties or relations with the forum [***3] State.

 

1048 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


J. Beres & Sons Dairy, Inc. v. Barber


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


75 A.D.2d 930; 427 N.Y.S.2d 522; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11584



 May 8, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner milk dealer sought the review of the judgment of respondent Commissioner of Agriculture and Markets of the State of New York (Commissioner) which conditionally revoked the milk dealer's license and imposed a penalty against the dealer. The Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York) transferred the matter to the court.


OVERVIEW: The milk dealer argued that its sale of milk to a market, for which he was punished, was not a sale to an unlicensed milk dealer, but, rather, was a sale to an exempt store under N.Y. Agric. & Mkts. Law § 257(3). By statutory definition, if the market purchased, handled, or sold milk, it was a milk dealer under the law. The market picked up milk at the milk dealer's premises and transported it back to its store for resale and did not qualify for the exemption from licensing because it transported milk to a store. Nevertheless, the market was exempt and, therefore, the milk dealer did not commit an unauthorized sale. The milk dealer also contended § 257(3) was unconstitutional on its face and in its enforcement arguing that there was no rational basis for its limitations and no public interest being served by so restricting the sale of milk to a retailer for subsequent sale at its own store, and further, that the section was unconstitutionally vague. The court found that the statute was unambiguous and clearly constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court annulled the finding of the Commissioner that the milk dealer was guilty of making sales to an unlicensed dealer and remitted the matter to the Commissioner.

 

1049 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re P.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


74 A.D.2d 403; 427 N.Y.S.2d 447; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10851



May 5, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Appeal from an order of the Family Court, Rockland County, dated September 14, 1978, dismissed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county attorney's office (county) challenged a dispositional order of the Family Court, Rockland County (New York), which adjudicated respondent juvenile as a delinquent and placed him on probation for one year. The county alleged that the dispositional order was not supported by a preponderance of the evidence and that the evidence supported placement in a residential treatment center.


OVERVIEW: The family court adjudicated the juvenile as a delinquent and placed him on probation for one year. The county appealed, claiming that the dispositional order was not supported by a preponderance of the evidence and that the evidence supported placement in a residential treatment center. The court dismissed the appeal. At the time of the appeal, the term of probation had expired. The court held that to permit the county to appeal an enforceable dispositional order of the family court for the purpose of having the severity of the order increased, would violate the Double Jeopardy clause of U.S. Const. amend. V. The court noted that the juvenile had already fully suffered one of the alternative punishments for his offense and held that the courts had no power to punish him further. Even in the absence of a fully executed dispositional order, the court held that an appeal by the county challenging the leniency of an order of disposition was barred by the double jeopardy clause, at least in the absence of a statute expressly providing for such a right as an adjunct to an appeal by the juvenile contesting the propriety of the dispositional order.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the county's appeal challenging a dispositional order adjudicating the juvenile as a delinquent and placing him on probation.


HEADNOTES

Infants -- Juvenile Delinquents -- Double Jeopardy

It would be violative of the constitutional prohibition against double jeopardy to permit the petitioner in a juvenile delinquency proceeding to appeal an enforceable dispositional order of the Family Court for the purpose of having the severity of the order increased, whether on appeal or following a remand to the Family Court, inasmuch as respondent would be exposed to the risk of a harsher disposition.

 

1050 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rodriguez


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


75 A.D.2d 730; 427 N.Y.S.2d 418; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11260



 May 1, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed the order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), that set aside a jury verdict that had convicted defendant of criminal possession of a weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged, along with co-defendant, with criminal possession of a weapon. Co-defendant denied any knowledge of a gun and testified that he had been riding with defendant and had stopped to pick-up defendant's friend. The friend rode for a time and then he and defendant left the car briefly. Defendant returned shortly thereafter, alone. The jury received the case against both on a charge of the presumption of possession found in N.Y. Penal Law § 265.15(3), acquitted co-defendant, but convicted defendant. The court set aside the verdict. The State appealed the judgment setting aside the verdict was reversed. The court held that it was error to rely on a case that had since been overturned to declare the statutory presumption unconstitutional. It also held there was sufficient evidence to support the verdict, and that the split verdict was not inconsistent because co-defendant had given an exculpatory explanation that was sufficient to rebut the presumption against him.


OUTCOME: The judgment setting aside the conviction was reversed, and the conviction reinstated, because it was error for the trial court to declare the statute in question unconstitutional. Also, there was sufficient evidence to support the verdict, and the split verdict was not inconsistent because the co-defendant gave an adequate exculpatory explanation.

In re John AA.


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


75 A.D.2d 910; 427 N.Y.S.2d 319; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11563



 May 1, 1980 

 

1052 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Warder v. Board of Regents


SUPREME COURT OF NEW YORK, APPELLATE DIVISION, THIRD DEPARTMENT


75 A.D.2d 666; 426 N.Y.S.2d 849; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11138



 April 10, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In related cases, petitioners, the proposed trustees of a theological seminar, appealed judgments of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York). The county court dismissed their application to compel respondent State Board of Regents to rule on their application for a provisional charter to operate an academic institution and dismissed their application to annul a finding that they were not entitled to a provisional charter.


OVERVIEW: In the first action, the trustees claimed that the Board took too long to rule on the application. In the second action, filed before the Board ruled in the first case, they claimed that the charter was wrongly denied. The court rejected all of the trustees' claims. It found that the delay raised in the first case was mooted by the Board's later issuance of a ruling; that the reasonableness of the delay was properly preserved in the second case; and that the first case was properly dismissed. The court also found that the Board had a rational basis for denying the charter. It noted that financial issues were raised only because the trustees did not inform the Board in a timely manner as to certain transactions and later refused to provide a proper financial statement; that the trustees did not show that the Board violated any statutory or constitutional rights by denying the charter; and that no violations of the Open Meetings Law occurred. The court held that the charter application was thoroughly and properly investigated and that the application was rightly denied because the seminary failed to meet the academic and financial requirements essential for the issuance of a charter.


OUTCOME: The court upheld the determinations of the Board denying a charter for the proposed theological seminary and dismissed the trustees' challenges thereto.

 

1053 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Estate of Schneier


Appeal Nos. 1, 2


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


74 A.D.2d 22; 426 N.Y.S.2d 624; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10077



April 8, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Appeal No. 1 -- Order unanimously modified, and, as modified, affirmed, with costs to petitioner, in accordance with opinion by Witmer, J. Appeal No. 2 -- Order unanimously reversed and motion denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner estate appealed an order of the Onondaga County Surrogate's Court (New York) denying its demand for a jury trial in a replevin action to recover stock certificates and assets held by respondent executor. The estate cross-appealed from an order partially granting the executor's motion for a protective order preventing one deposition. The executor cross-appealed from the same order permitted the depositions of two other individuals.


OVERVIEW: The estate brought a replevin action to recover corporate stock certificates and other assets formerly possessed by the testator and now held by the executor. On appeal, the court held that the estate was entitled to a jury trial of the issues raised by the executor's answer. The estate was entitled to a jury trial with respect to the issue of title in a proceeding under N.Y. Surr. Ct. Proc. Act § 2105, consistent with N.Y. Surr. Ct. Proc. Act § 501 and the constitution. The estate made a timely demand for a jury trial, pursuant to N.Y. Surr. Ct. Proc. Act § 502, within six days after the service of the answer to the amended petition following a stay. The amended petition, served by leave of the court after discovery, was not a subterfuge to reinstate the running of the statute of limitations. The surrogate court abused its discretion by not denying the motion to strike the demand because there was no showing of prejudice to the executor. The surrogate court erred in not allowing an examination before trial of one individual by the estate, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3101, because the essential issue upon which he was previously examined was different.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting the motion to strike the demand for a jury trial in the replevin action and denied the motion. The court modified the order with respect to the motion for a protective order against the estate's demand for an examination before trial and reversed it in so far as it granted the motion concerned one individual and, otherwise, affirmed the motion.


HEADNOTES

Trial -- Right to Jury Trial -- Proceeding in Surrogate's Court

1. A petitioner who, pursuant to SCPA 2105, instituted a proceeding in Surrogate's Court in the nature of a replevin action to recover specific certificates of corporate stock and other assets, formerly possessed by the testator and now in the hands of respondent as executor, is entitled to a jury trial of the issues raised in respondent's answer.

 [***2] Trial -- Right to Jury Trial -- Proceeding in Surrogate's Court

2. Petitioner, who instituted a proceeding in Surrogate's Court in the nature of a replevin action to recover specific certificates of corporate stock and other assets, formerly possessed by the testator and now in the hands of respondent as executor, made a timely demand for a jury trial where he was granted leave to serve an amended petition after his discovery proceedings gave him fuller knowledge of the items of assets which he claimed and he made the demand within six days after service of the answer to that petition (SCPA 502, subd 2, par [a]); moreover, lacking any showing of prejudice to the respondent, under the circumstances of the case, the trial court abused its discretion under CPLR 4102 (subd [e]) in not denying the motion to strike the demand.

Disclosure -- Examination before Trial

3. A demand for an examination before trial of three individuals by petitioner, who instituted a proceeding in Surrogate's Court in the nature of a replevin action to recover specific certificates of corporate stock and other assets, formerly possessed by the testator and now in the hands of respondent as [***3] executor, should be granted where all three were employees and officers of respondent bank through whom respondent acted; the fact that petitioner had already examined one of the individuals should not prohibit a second examination where the essential issue upon which that individual was questioned is different from the one now presented.

 

1054 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Kay-Fries, Inc. v. Martino


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


73 A.D.2d 342; 426 N.Y.S.2d 304; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10056



March 31, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Appeals from (1) a judgment of the Supreme Court, Rockland County, entered August 23, 1979, and (2) an order of the same court, entered November 13, 1979, dismissed, without costs or disbursements (see CPLR 5517; Matter of Aho, 39 NY2d 241, 248).

Resettled judgment of the same court, entered November 14, 1979, modified, on the law, (1) by deleting the ninth decretal paragraph thereof, (2) by deleting from the tenth decretal paragraph thereof the limitation on the number of persons in the location identified as the "tent" area, and (3) by adding thereto a provision that the injunction shall remain in effect for no more than six months [***2] from the date of the signing of the original judgment, August 23, 1979, unless extended pursuant to paragraph 8 of subdivision 1 of section 807 of the Labor Law. As so modified, resettled judgment affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, union members and officials, appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court (New York), which granted injunctive relief in favor of plaintiff employer in a labor dispute. The employer had sought to restrain the members and officials from obstructing egress and ingress into its plant.


OVERVIEW: The uncontradicted testimony of the employer's witnesses was replete with instances of unlawful acts such as rock throwing, tire puncturing, and tire slashing by the union members during a labor dispute. The union members and officials appealed the grant of injunctive relief, assigning as error the trial court's jurisdiction, the extent of the restraints, and the finding that the union members and officials were responsible for the acts complained of. The court affirmed, with minor modification. The court held that the record amply justified relief. The trial court's recitation of facts did not pose a jurisdictional problem under N.Y. Lab. Law § 807(1) because the trial court's power to render a judgment on the merits was unaffected by its failure to comply with the statute. The record was sufficiently complete to permit the court to make the necessary findings of fact. The court modified the restraints ordered with respect to the number of persons allowed at a tent area and the length of the injunction. Finally, the record supported the trial court's findings that the union, its officers, and members had engaged in the unlawful acts.


OUTCOME: The court dismissed the appeals by the union members and officials, without costs or disbursements. The court resettled the judgment below and modified, on the law, by deleting two paragraphs and by adding a provision that the injunction was to remain in effect for no more than six months from the date of the signing of the original judgment. As so modified, the resettled judgment was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Courts -- Jurisdiction -- Injunctive Relief in Labor Disputes

1. Upon an action for an injunction in a labor dispute, the Supreme Court's failure to comply with subdivision 1 of section 807 of the Labor Law, which directs that findings of fact be filed in the record of a case, is not a jurisdictional defect and the court has the power to render a judgment on the merits; however, the requirement of subdivision 1 of section 807 is important for enlightenment of the parties and for effective review on appeal. Furthermore, the Appellate Division has the power to make any necessary findings if the record of the case is complete, even if the trial court failed to state the essential facts.

Appeal -- Matters Appealable -- Findings of Fact by Appellate Division

2. An appeal lies from a denial of a motion which sought to modify the recital portion of a resettled judgment, and while the granting of plaintiff's motion to resettle in [***3] its entirety would have aided the Appellate Division in determining if the essential facts found by the trial court support the relief granted, where the record is sufficiently complete the Appellate Division can make the necessary findings of fact and, therefore, reversing an order denying specific fact finding and resettlement would serve no purpose.

Judgments -- Correction

3. A motion to resettle a judgment is not untimely under CPLR 4405 as a posttrial motion under CPLR 4404 (subd [b]) to make new findings of facts or render a new decision where the defect was not substantive since the motion is more properly characterized as a motion to correct an irregularity pursuant to CPLR 5019 (subd [a]).

Courts -- Jurisdiction -- Injunctive Relief in Labor Disputes

4. Although certain labor union activities are protected by Federal law, the State has the power to enjoin breaches of the peace and threats to public safety; accordingly, a trial court's jurisdiction in an action for an injunction in a labor dispute involving acts of violence is limited by section 807 of the Labor Law.

Labor -- Injunctions in Labor Disputes

5. The restraints imposed by [***4] the trial court, i.e., that only five pickets could be stationed at a site near the entrance to the employer's plant and that these pickets had to move to the roadside upon the approach of vehicular traffic absent a voluntary stop by the driver of a vehicle to inquire about the strike, were reasonable considering the terms of the injunction, which prohibited the pickets from hindering the ingress to or egress from the employer's plant, the threatening or committing of violence upon plant employees or guests, and the committing of any property destruction, with specific reference to the throwing of objects and the placing of nails so as to damage tires, and given the traffic-stopping tactics of the pickets and the expressed safety concerns of local police authorities about tie-ups at the intersection.

Labor -- Injunctions in Labor Disputes

6. A modification of a judgment is required where it does not conform with the requirement of subdivision 8 of section 807 of the Labor Law, which provides that no permanent injunction issued in a labor dispute shall remain in force for more than six months from the date on which the judgment is signed; the purpose of the limitation is [***5] to assure that restraints are made only after a recent hearing.

 

1055 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Pacheco


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


73 A.D.2d 370; 426 N.Y.S.2d 57; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10059



March 24, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Resentence and order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the sentence imposed by the Supreme Court in Kings County (New York) upon defendant as a second felony offender and of the trial court's order denying defendant's motion to set aside the sentence, contending that N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06 was unconstitutional on equal protection grounds.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of the felony of attempted criminal possession of a dangerous drug in the fourth degree. Thereafter, defendant entered a guilty plea to the felony of criminal sale of a controlled substance in the fifth degree, with an agreed-sentence. The trial court sentenced defendant as a predicate felon under N.Y. Penal Law § 70.06, to the agreed-upon term. Defendant filed a motion to set aside his sentence insofar as he was sentenced as a predicate felon. The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the court affirmed the sentence and the order. The court held that § 70.06 was rationally related to a legitimate legislative purpose. The statute worked a harsher result on those with a prior state felony conviction than those who previously carried out their illicit conduct elsewhere, but the legislature could have determined within acceptable constitutional dimensions that it wished to be more severe with those who consistently violated the laws of the state. All those with a prior state felony conviction were treated equally.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's sentence of defendant as a predicate felon and the trial court's order denying defendant's to set aside the sentence imposed on defendant after he pled guilty to criminal sale of a controlled substance in the fifth degree.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Sentence -- Second Felony Offender

Section 70.06 (subd 1, par [b], cl [i]) of the Penal Law, which concerns sentence of imprisonment for second felony offenders, is not unconstitutional on equal protection grounds, despite the differing treatment of those individuals who have been convicted of a prior felony in New York and those individuals who have an out-of-State conviction, the former not being afforded the benefit of any downgrading of the acts constituting the earlier crime while the latter are, inasmuch as the statute is rationally related to a legitimate legislative purpose; all individuals with a prior New York conviction are treated equally and while the statute concededly works a harsher result on those with a prior New York felony conviction, the Legislature [***2] could determine within acceptable constitutional dimensions that it wishes to be more severe with those who have consistently violated the laws of this State since an individual with a history of violating our laws may be viewed as a greater threat to the peace and tranquility of the residents of New York than one who has previously carried on his illicit conduct elsewhere.

 

1056 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


North Hempstead v. Exxon Corp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


73 A.D.2d 377; 425 N.Y.S.2d 995; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10060



March 24, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil companies sought review of judgments of the Supreme Court in Nassau County (New York), which determined, in two consolidated actions, that appellee town's ordinance, which prohibited the installation and use of self-service gasoline stations anywhere in the town, was a valid constitutional exercise of police power.


OVERVIEW: Two oil companies owned and operated self-service gasoline stations in the town, which complied with all applicable safety regulations. The town board enacted an ordinance that prohibited the installation and use of self-service gasoline stations anywhere in the town. The town brought an action against one oil company to enjoin its operation of a self-service station, and the other oil company brought an action against the town to challenge the constitutionality of the ordinance. The actions were consolidated for trial. The trial court upheld the validity of the ordinance and the oil companies sought review. The court held that: (1) legislative enactments were presumed to be constitutional, and while the presumption was rebuttable, unconstitutionality had to be demonstrated beyond a reasonable doubt; (2) an ordinance was required to be reasonably related to some manifest evil which need only be reasonably apprehended; (3) the town was entitled to regulate the use of flammable substances, N.Y. Town Law § 130(5); and (4) the ordinance was not reasonably related to safety because self-service stations were not an increased safety risk.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgments for the town against the oil companies because the town ordinance was unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Regulation of Self-Service Gasoline Stations

1. A local law prohibiting the installation and use of self-service gasoline stations in a town is unconstitutional, as an unlawful exercise of the town's police power, since it does not bear a rational relation to the goal of preventing fires and other casualties at gasoline stations, i.e., the undisputed empirical proof demonstrates that any manifest evil associated with the dispensing of gasoline is not increased by the advent of self-service.

Statutes -- Presumption of Constitutionality

2. All legislative enactments are entitled to a presumption of constitutionality.

 

1057 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Schermerhorn v. Rosenberg


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


73 A.D.2d 276; 426 N.Y.S.2d 274; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10048; 6 Media L. Rep. 1376



March 17, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Orange County, entered June 30, 1978, modified, on the law, by deleting therefrom the amount attributable to the recovery on the fourth cause of action and adding thereto a provision dismissing that cause of action. As so modified, judgment affirmed, with costs to plaintiff, and action remitted to Trial Term for entry of an appropriate amended judgment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state senator filed an action for libel and slander against defendants, a newspaper reporter and newspaper. The Supreme Court, Orange County (New York), entered judgment in favor of the senator. The reporter and the paper appealed.


OVERVIEW: The senator contended that the verdicts were consistent with the law and the evidence and must be sustained. The reporter sought to overturn the verdicts as inconsistent with the First Amendment's guarantee of freedom of the press. The court held that the issue of whether the headline was defamatory was properly submitted to the jury. The court held that the verdict against the reporter carried the implicit finding that he had played some part in the formulation of the headline, and the court could not say that that finding was without support in the record. The evidence was sufficient to sustain the jury's determination that the reporter acted as the agent of the paper and within the scope of his employment, had composed a defamatory headline with actual knowledge that the matter asserted therein was false. The court held that the publication of the reading of the article on the senate floor was protected by a principle of overriding importance embodied in New York statutory law as an expression of the state's public policy. The court held that the public's right to know outweighed the individual rights of the senator, with the result that the article was absolutely privileged.


OUTCOME: The court modified the judgment of the trial court by deleting therefrom the amount attributable to the recovery on the cause of action regarding reporting that the article in question was read on the senate floor. The court dismissed that cause of action. As so modified, the trial court's judgment in favor of the senator was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Libel and Slander -- Actionable Words -- Public Figure

1. In an action based on libel and slander, the court is not bound to search out and apply any possible innocent construction of the words alleged to be defamatory inasmuch as the function of the court in matters such as these is twofold: first, it must determine whether the statement complained of reasonably permits the construction urged by the plaintiff and, if it does, then it is for the jury to decide whether that was the sense in which the statement was likely to be understood by the ordinary and average reader; and [***2] second, the court must determine whether there is a reasonable basis to find that the meaning ascribed to the statement is actionable. Finally, where the plaintiff is a public official, he must bear the additional burden of demonstrating by proof of convincing clarity that the defamatory matter was published with malice.

Libel and Slander -- Public Figure

2. A verdict in favor of plaintiff State Senator upon a cause of action for libel regarding a false headline appearing in defendant newspaper from which the jury could reasonably conclude that plaintiff believed blacks ought to be excluded from participating in the administration of an important urban renewal project should be sustained where there was evidence that the headline was published with malice inasmuch as a legislator's reputation and standing in the community could be seriously damaged by such a suggestion.

Libel and Slander -- Libelous Headline

3. In an action for an allegedly libelous headline appearing in a newspaper, whether such headline constitutes a statement of fact or opinion is a question of law to be determined by the court; accordingly, where a headline plainly purports to state a fact,  [***3] not an opinion, the trial court should have so ruled as a matter of law, but its failure to do so does not warrant reversal of a verdict for plaintiff since that failure actually redounded to the defendants' benefit by permitting the jury to find that the headline represented a protected opinion.

Libel and Slander -- Libelous Headline -- Actionable Words

4. In an action regarding allegedly libelous headlines, the trial court should charge the jury that defamatory headlines are actionable though the matter following is not, unless they fairly indicate the substance of the matter to which they refer, and unless they are a fair index of the matter contained in a truthful report; if the headline is a fair index of an accurate article, it is not actionable and if it is not a fair index, then the headline must be examined independently to determine whether it is actionable under general principles of libel; that the defamatory meaning of the headline may be dispelled by a reading of the entire article is of no avail to the publisher inasmuch as a headline is often all that is read by the casual reader.

Libel and Slander -- Public Figure

5. A verdict in favor of a [***4] public figure upon a cause of action for slander, regarding a newspaper reporter's telephone conversation with two of plaintiff's colleagues, must be upheld where the evidence at trial was sufficient to sustain the jury's determination that the reporter made the statement, that it was defamatory, and that it was made with actual knowledge that it was untrue.

Libel and Slander -- Privilege

6. A verdict in favor of a State Senator upon a cause of action for slander, regarding a newspaper's accurate report of an accusation by one of his colleagues, who stated that he had access to tape recordings of plaintiff making racial and ethnic slurs, should be upheld where the substance of the accusation was concocted and disseminated by the newspaper's reporter inasmuch as a newspaper simply may not shield itself from a libel action by reporting the utterance of a false and defamatory accusation of which it was the source.

Libel and Slander -- Privilege -- Reports of Legislative Proceedings

7. A verdict on a cause of action for libel based upon the publication of the fact that an earlier defamatory headline, written by defendant reporter and printed by defendant newspaper,  [***5] had been read in the course of a floor debate in the State Senate, must be set aside and the cause of action dismissed since the publication accurately reported the proceedings of the Legislature and, accordingly, is protected by the absolute privilege contained in section 74 of the Civil Rights Law, which provides that a civil action cannot be maintained against any person, firm or corporation, for the publication of a fair and true report of any legislative proceeding.

 

1058 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


First Colonie Co. v. Lyons


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


74 A.D.2d 696; 425 N.Y.S.2d 667; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10383



February 21, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a declaratory judgment action, plaintiff inn owner appealed a decision of the Supreme Court, Special Term (New York), which granted summary judgment to defendant, the Commissioner of the Albany County Department of Health. The special term declared that provisions of the New York State Sanitary Code requiring fencing for swimming pools, N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10 §§ 6.9(a)(3), 6.16, 14-1.32(b)(3), were valid and applied to the inn.


OVERVIEW: The Department approved the inn's plans and specifications for an unfenced indoor swimming pool but later advised the inn that the State Sanitary Code would require the pool to be fenced. On appeal from summary judgment in favor of the Department, the court reviewed the decision to require fencing an indoor swimming pool. In reversing, the court noted the rule under N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 10 § 6.9(a)(3), 6.16, which provided that artificial swimming pools had to be protected by a fence, wall, building, enclosure or solid wall of durable material. The court concluded that the rule did not require the inn's indoor pool to be fenced. The pool was protected by the building in which it was located, and that protection complied with the language of the statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the summary judgment in favor of the Department, without costs, granted judgment in favor of the inn, and declared that the State Sanitary Code did not require the indoor pool to be protected by a fence.

 

1059 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Angelone v. Rochester


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


72 A.D.2d 445; 424 N.Y.S.2d 933; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9701



February 20, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged the judgment of Supreme Court (New York) that declared unconstitutional an ordinance providing for the levy of a special tax and the repayment of an unconstitutional tax in plaintiff taxpayers' action for a refund.


OVERVIEW: The city imposed a tax that was later found illegal because it exceeded the two-percent cap found in the state constitution. The city was ordered to pay refunds to those taxpayers who had paid the tax under protest. Instead, the city passed Rochester, N.Y., Ordinance 97-307, which granted refunds to all taxpayers, imposed a special levy to pay the refund, and showed the refund as a credit of the levy amount. The taxpayers sought a refund of the unconstitutional taxes and protested the scheme of the ordinance. The trial court granted summary judgment to the taxpayers and held the ordinance unconstitutional. The court affirmed, holding that the refunds were only allowed to be paid to those who had overpaid the tax in the earlier tax year, not to taxpayers in the year of the special levy. The computation of the levy never actually resulted in a return of the illegal tax but was a refund of the levy itself. In addition, the levy was subject to the two-percent limitation, which it exceeded, and the city was only authorized to collect funds by special levy to pay particular claims or judgments, not those of the city's taxpayers at large.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision in favor of the taxpayers in their action for a refund against the city.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Repayment of Real Property Taxes Collected in Excess of Constitutional Limitation

An ordinance of a municipality, which collected real property taxes in excess of its constitutional limitation and was directed by court order to make refunds to people who paid them under protest, is unconstitutional where, pursuant to a repayment plan by which the city would give tax refunds to the people who paid them under protest as well as to the people who did not, the ordinance gave the refund to all property holders on the tax rolls in one particular year and did not determine the people who actually paid the excess assessments; furthermore, the ordinance is unconstitutional since the entire repayment plan was nothing more than a fiction inasmuch as no money was ever returned to the taxpayers, the "refund", which was credited to the taxpayer's [***2] tax bill, was precisely the same amount stated on the bill due the city as a result of the extra levy to fund the plan. Accordingly, plaintiffs, who paid their real property taxes under protest, are entitled to refunds in the amount of the excess for the years during which the city collected taxes in excess of its constitutional limitation.

 

1060 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Dozier


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


72 A.D.2d 478; 424 N.Y.S.2d 1010; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9706



February 14, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, Bronx County, rendered on June 22, 1978, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought relief from a judgment of the Supreme Court, Bronx County (New York), which found him guilty of rape in the third degree in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 130.25(2).


OVERVIEW: Appellant plead guilty to rape in the third degree under N.Y. Penal Law § 130.25(2). The charge was based on sexual intercourse with a female less than 17 years of age. Appellant contended that the statute was violative of due process and equal protection, because it did not permit ignorance or mistake as to the female's age to be asserted as a defense. Appellant further contended that the statute arbitrarily and capriciously fixed the age at which a female may consent to sexual intercourse at 17 years. The court held that strict scrutiny standard of review did not apply, because age was not a suspect classification, and that the state had a legitimate concern in protecting females 16 years and younger. In addition, the statute was malum prohibitum rather than malum in se; therefore, honest intent or no intent at all was not a factor that would invalidate the statute. Thus, the court upheld the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court upheld appellant's rape conviction and held that the strict scrutiny standard of review did not apply, because age was not a suspect classification and the state had a legitimate concern in protecting females 16 years and younger.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Rape

1. Subdivision 2 of section 130.25 of the Penal Law, which provides that a male is guilty of rape in the third degree when, being 21 years old or more, he engages in sexual intercourse with a female less than 17 years old, is not violative of equal protection since the statute serves a significant State interest in that it protects a certain class of minors from any adverse consequences of sexual intercourse, even if consensual; the State's interests involve the problems of adolescent pregnancy, due to the attendant psychological, medical, sociological and moral questions, including questions of whether to have an abortion or to bear the child, and the prevention of injuries uniquely suffered by young females resulting from sexual intercourse.

Crimes -- Rape

2. Subdivision 2 of section 130.25 of the Penal Law, which provides that a male is guilty of [***2] rape in the third degree when, being 21 years old or more, he engages in sexual intercourse with a female less than 17 years old, does not violate due process by its failure to permit ignorance, fraud or mistake as to the female's age to be asserted as a defense inasmuch as there is no constitutional prohibition against imposing criminal liability for conduct in which mens rea is not an element of the offense, it being an established principle of law that public policy may require that in the prohibition or punishment of particular acts it may be provided that he who shall do them shall do them at his peril and will not be heard to plead in defense good faith or ignorance.

Redding v. Board of Regents


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


74 A.D.2d 671; 424 N.Y.S.2d 796; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10358



February 14, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner chiropractor initiated a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. Educ. Law § 6510(4) to annul a determination of respondent Commissioner of Education, which imposed a penalty of censure and reprimand on petitioner for practicing beyond the scope of his chiropractic license and for unprofessional conduct.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner, as a former president of the state chiropractic association, was dissatisfied with the provisions of N.Y. Educ. Law § 6551, subd. 2, para. a, cl. (3), prohibiting chiropractors from X-raying below the level of the top of the first lumbar vertebra. In an effort to invalidate that portion of the statute, petitioner decided to make himself a test case and intentionally violated its provisions by extending X-rays for certain patients beyond the permissible limitation. Petitioner readily admitted his guilt of violating the statute before the hearing panel but urged its unconstitutionality. The court held that petitioner admittedly and deliberately violated the provisions of § 6551, in order to contest the constitutionality of that statute in a disciplinary proceeding held pursuant to § 6510. The court held that an action for a declaratory judgment was the appropriate vehicle for the relief requested. However, the determination of the Commissioner was supported by substantial evidence and had a rational basis.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the determination and dismissed the petition.

Reid v. Ambach


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


74 A.D.2d 671; 424 N.Y.S.2d 793; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10359



February 14, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner land surveyor initiated proceedings pursuant to N.Y. Educ. Law § 6510(4) to annul a determination of respondent, the Commissioner of Education of the State of New York, which suspended the surveyor's license to practice land surveying and thereby effectuated an action by the board of regents that adopted the regents committee's finding of guilt but modified a suspension recommended by the state board for land surveying.


OVERVIEW: A land developer hired the surveyor to update the survey from another firm, the latter refusing to do the update because of unpaid fees. The surveyor made the update over the other firm's objections. The surveyor was charged and found guilty of unprofessional conduct in practicing the profession of land surveying using the designation of "Civil Engineers and City Surveyors" when there was, in fact, no professional engineers connected with his firm; in affixing his professional seal to a survey, certifying same as true and accurate, when he had substantially copied the survey from the work of another without verifying the accuracy thereof; and in affixing his professional seal to the aforementioned survey without placing a notation to reflect the fact that the survey was copied from a prior survey made by another. The court affirmed and held that the board of regents was authorized to promulgate rules as to what constituted unprofessional conduct. Administrative rule interpretations and factual determinations would not be reversed absent an abuse of discretion. Here, the findings of the commissioner were reasonable and supported by substantial evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commissioner's determination to suspend the surveyor's license to practice land surveying.

Brennan v. New York City Housing Authority


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


72 A.D.2d 410; 424 N.Y.S.2d 687; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9696



February 7, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on July 3, 1979, modified, on the law, to the extent of declaring that Police Officers of the Housing Authority of the City of New York are public officers within the meaning of section 30 of the Public Officers Law and subject to the residency requirements therein, but defendants are equitably estopped from imposing these requirements on plaintiffs, and, as so modified, the order is affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant housing authority appealed from an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term, New York County (New York), which granted plaintiff housing authority police officers' motion for a preliminary injunction, and plaintiffs cross appealed from so much of said order as denied plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment in plaintiffs' declaratory judgment action.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff housing authority police officers brought a declaratory judgment that the provisions of N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 30, which required public officers to be state residents, were inapplicable to plaintiffs and that memoranda issued by the chief of the housing authority police department in enforcement of this residency requirement was unconstitutional. The court ruled that defendant housing authority was equitably estopped from enforcing this mandate. The court held that the imposition of equitable estoppel would not work a serious injustice nor unduly damage public policy, and its application to these plaintiffs was limited and would prevent a "manifest injustice." The lower court's order, granting plaintiffs' application for a preliminary injunction and denying plaintiffs' cross motion for summary judgment as premature, was modified to the extent of declaring that plaintiffs were public officers within the meaning of § 30 and subject to the residency requirements therein, but defendants were equitably estopped from imposing these requirements on plaintiffs.


OUTCOME: The lower court's order was modified to the extent of declaring plaintiff public housing police officers were public officers within the meaning of the Public Officers Law and subject to the residency requirements therein, but defendants were equitably estopped from imposing these requirements on plaintiffs, and, as so modified, the order was affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


HEADNOTES

Public Officers -- In-State Residence Requirement

The in-State residence requirement for public officers set out in section 30 of the Public Officers Law was not enforced against 36 plaintiffs, New York City Housing Authority police officers who reside in New Jersey and Connecticut.

 

1064 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


State Board of Equalization & Assessment v. Kerwick


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


72 A.D.2d 292; 425 N.Y.S.2d 640; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9684



January 31, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, entered July 14, 1977, affirmed, without costs.

Judgment, entered April 25, 1978, reversed, on the law, and petition dismissed, without costs.

Judgment, entered July 14, 1978, modified, on the law, to the extent that the petition is dismissed as moot, without costs.

Judgment, entered March 23, 1979, reversed, on the law, and complaint and petition dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner State Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA) initiated actions under N.Y. Real Prop. Tax. Law §§ 202(1)(g) and 216(2) to force respondent local tax assessors to place upon the tax rolls real property which the local tax assessors had exempted. The Supreme Court at Special Term (New York) dismissed two of the SBEA's actions, but granted a motion for declaratory judgment that directed placing the real properties on the tax rolls.


OVERVIEW: The SBEA in its first action initially commenced it under § 202(1)(g) which provided that the SBEA could furnish the local tax assessors with information and instruction necessary for them to perform their duties, which had to have been followed, and compliance which could have been compelled by the SBEA. The court read § 202(1)(g) together with § 216(2) which set forth the particular procedures the SBEA was to have followed when confronted with recalcitrant assessors. The court held that latter section provided the exclusive procedures for enforcement of SBEA rules, regulations, and orders. The next action was initiated pursuant to § 216(2) to enforce an SBEA order that directed that certain exempted real properties be placed back on the tax rolls. The court held that the SBEA lacked such authority because it had procedural oversight authority only, and no right to actively participate in the local assessment process because those power were specifically reserved to the local tax assessors. Finally, the SBEA's motion for declaratory judgment could not have been treated as a summary judgment under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3211, because it was an inappropriate procedure.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the dismissals of the SBEA's orders directing the local tax assessors to place certain real property on the tax rolls. The court reversed an order that granted the SBEA's motion for declaratory judgment and that had directed the local tax assessors to place certain real property on the tax rolls.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Assessment -- Powers of Board of Equalization and Assessment

1. The sole and exclusive procedures for enforcement of rules, regulations and orders of the State Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA)  [***4] are those provided by subdivision 2 of section 216 of the Real Property Tax Law, which states that when a public officer whose duties relate to assessments has failed to comply with a law, rule or regulation relating to such duties, the SBEA may, after a hearing, direct such officer to comply, and if such employee neglects or refuses to comply, the SBEA may apply to the Supreme Court for a summary order compelling compliance; accordingly, lacking any standing as an aggrieved taxpayer (Real Property Tax Law, § 704) and without statutory authority to obtain the relief sought, under section 202 (subd 1, par [g]) of the Real Property Tax Law, which provides that the SBEA shall provide assessors with information and instruction in making assessments, which instructions shall be followed and compliance with which may be enforced by the SBEA, a petition brought by the SBEA in a proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78 seeking to void a tentative assessment roll, enjoin proceedings on grievance day, direct a return of the tax rolls to assessors, and place properties exempted from taxation through property owners' membership in the Universal Life Church upon the tax rolls, is dismissed.

 [***5] Administrative Law -- Agency's Construction of Statute

2. The interpretation of a statute by the agency charged with its administration must be given judicial deference, but such an interpretation must be rational and reasonable and not one which would render a specific statutory provision meaningless.

Taxation -- Assessment -- Powers of Board of Equalization and Assessment

3. A petition brought by the State Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA), seeking an order directing compliance with orders of the SBEA made after hearings (see Real Property Tax Law, § 216, subd 2) directing correction of a final assessment roll by removal of property which had been granted a tax exemption due to the owners' membership in the Universal Life Church from the exempt portion of the assessment roll, with directions that they be restored to the taxable portion thereof and that future assessments reflect the full value of those parcels, is dismissed, since the SBEA does not have authority to issue an order which directs a particular assessment of an individual parcel of real property, and since the hearings were fatally flawed by the SBEA's failure to comply with the statutory [***6] mandates contained in the State Administrative Procedure Act in that the town's assessors were denied proper notice of the hearing and its purposes (State Administrative Procedure Act, § 301, subd 2), in some instances their counsel was denied the right to cross-examine certain witnesses (State Administrative Procedure Act, § 306, subd 3), and the ultimate decision of the SBEA following the hearing did not contain the necessary findings of fact or a concise statement of the underlying facts supporting its findings (State Administrative Procedure Act, § 307, subd 1).

Declaratory Judgments -- When Relief Appropriate

4. In a proceeding commenced by the State Board of Equalization and Assessment (SBEA) and the State of New York after respondent assessors successfully circumvented a judgment directing them to place previously exempted properties on their town assessment rolls by first placing the omitted properties on the assessment rolls for the year 1977 and then contemporaneously removing the same properties from the 1978 rolls, in which plaintiffs moved for mandatory relief seeking an order directing that the exempt property be placed on the taxable rolls for the years [***7] 1977 and 1978 and that the defendant assessors be restrained from exempting these properties for the taxable year 1979, the Supreme Court reasoned that it had before it both a declaratory judgment action and a CPLR article 78 proceeding, and although it had the power to treat the motion as one for summary judgment ( CPLR 3211, subd [c]), it improperly granted declaratory relief since the court did not notify the parties of its intention to make a summary determination, thus enabling them to submit additional proof in support of their positions ( CPLR 3211, subd [c]); moreover, the relief granted in the article 78 proceeding was not procedurally appropriate since the SBEA has no powers beyond those statutorily granted (Real Property Tax Law, § 216), and since the State's exclusive remedy is pursuant to article 7 of the Real Property Tax Law. Accordingly, the complaint and petition are dismissed.

People ex rel. Van Fossen v. Dillon


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


72 A.D.2d 166; 424 N.Y.S.2d 550; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9663



January 24, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, entered in Onondaga County (New York), that denied his application for a writ of habeas corpus, denied his application for restoration to his former parole status, and ruled that his final revocation hearing should be expedited.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner instituted a habeas corpus proceeding to prevent the revocation of his parole. He alleged the denial of his constitutional rights and denial of due process of law at the preliminary hearing due to 1) continued interrogation after he requested an attorney and informed the officers that he did not wish to speak to them; 2) the refusal of his request for a breathalyzer test for alcohol following his arrest, and; 3) the limitation of the scope of his cross-examination of a witness presented against him. The writ was denied, and petitioner appealed. On appeal, the court noted that habeas corpus is the proper remedy for review of parole revocation proceedings. The court also found that the evidence before the hearing officer was sufficient to permit a finding that petitioner had violated the terms of his conditional release by using alcohol. With respect to the cross-examination claim, the court recognized the rule that the Parole Board may limit any cross-examination to the precise factual issue of the stated violation.


OUTCOME: The judgment below was affirmed because there was sufficient evidence to support a finding of probable cause of a parole violation by the use of alcohol.


HEADNOTES

Habeas Corpus -- When Remedy Appropriate

1. Habeas corpus is a proper remedy for review of parole revocation proceedings.

Parole -- Revocation Hearing

2. Actions of the Parole Board are judicial functions and are not reviewable if performed in accordance with law (Executive Law, § 259-i); accordingly, upon finding that there was evidence at a preliminary parole violation hearing which, if believed, was sufficient to support a finding of probable cause and that required procedural rules were followed, the court's power to review is exhausted and it must dismiss a writ of habeas corpus.

Parole -- Revocation Hearing -- Scope of Cross-Examination

3. The Parole Board may limit any cross-examination at a parole revocation hearing to the precise factual issue [***2] of the stated violation.
