People v. Onofre


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


72 A.D.2d 268; 424 N.Y.S.2d 566; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9681



January 24, 1980 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, and indictment dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the Onondaga County Court (New York) for consensual sodomy in violation of N.Y. Penal Law § 130.38, challenging the constitutionality of the statute.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an adult male, was charged with the crime of consensual sodomy in violation of § 130.38 after admitting to engaging, by mutual consent, in proscribed sexual conduct with another adult male in the privacy of his home. After the trial court denied defendant's motion to dismiss on the grounds that the statute was unconstitutional, defendant entered a plea of guilty. On appeal, defendant again challenged the constitutionality of the statute. The court reasoned that although curtailing conduct that offended the public was a legitimate state interest, sexual conduct engaged in by mutually consenting adults in private had little likelihood of offending a public not embarked on eavesdropping. The court ruled that because the statute's purpose would be achieved by means that were unduly broad and that invaded the area of protected freedoms, the statute impermissibly interfered with defendant's constitutional right to privacy and violated the due process and equal protection clauses of the United States Constitution and the due process clause of N.Y. Const. art. I, § 6.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for consensual sodomy and dismissed the indictment, declaring the statute under which defendant was convicted to be unconstitutional.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Appeal

1. Defendant, who pleaded guilty to the crime of consensual sodomy in violation of section 130.38 of the Penal Law after the trial court denied his motion to dismiss the charge on the ground that the statute is unconstitutional on its face, can appeal that conviction by again challenging the constitutionality of the statute.

Crimes -- Sodomy

2. Section 130.38 of the Penal Law is an unconstitutional exercise of State power insofar as it prohibits voluntary sexual conduct between consenting adults in private inasmuch as the State's interest in regulating such conduct is insufficient to prevent the statute from running afoul of the constitutional right to privacy, the equal protection and due process clauses of the Fourteenth Amendment of the United States Constitution, and the due process clause of section 6 article I of the New York Constitution. 

 

1067 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Wittmann


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


73 A.D.2d 1053; 425 N.Y.S.2d 416; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10018



January 24, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction in the Erie County Court (New York) for driving while intoxicated.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was arrested for driving while intoxicated, arraigned, and released on bail, but did not hear anything more about the charge for 16 months, when he was questioned about it while applying for a driver's license. He was indicted 18 months after his arraignment. The reviewing court found that his conviction was improper. The delay by the prosecution was without excuse and violated his right to a speedy trial under N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 30.30.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction for driving while intoxicated was reversed because he was denied his right to a speedy trial.

 

1068 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Neiss


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


73 A.D.2d 938; 423 N.Y.S.2d 942; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9851



January 14, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Criminal defendant appealed a decision from the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which convicted him, upon his plea of guilty, of grand larceny in the third degree and theft of services, on the grounds that the statutory presumption contained in the "theft-of-services" statute, N.Y. Penal Law § 165.15(6), was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Criminal defendant pleaded guilty to the crimes of grand larceny in the third degree and theft of services in connection with the illegal appropriation of natural gas. On appeal, defendant challenged the constitutionality of the statutory presumption in N.Y. Penal Law § 165.15(6). The appellate court held that there was no viable constitutional challenge in the absence of a factual record that indicated to what extent, if any, the presumption was relied upon by plaintiff state in prosecuting defendant. However, the court then found that the interest of justice required a reversal of the lower court's judgment and vacated the guilty plea, noting that the record unequivocally showed that defendant entered a guilty plea upon the assurance of plaintiff that defendant had preserved his right to challenge the evidentiary presumption on appeal.


OUTCOME: The court reversed criminal defendant's convictions and vacated defendant's guilty plea, finding that although defendant had not preserved his right to challenge the constitutionality of the evidentiary presumption under the "theft-of-services" statute, the record was unequivocally clear that defendant had pleaded guilty upon assurances from plaintiff prosecution that his plea would not prevent him from appealing on that issue.

 

1069 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Brewer Funeral Home, Inc. v. Axelrod


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


73 A.D.2d 991; 423 N.Y.S.2d 570; 1980 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9937



January 10, 1980 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner funeral director instituted an action against respondent department of health, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, which challenged the decision from the department of health that found that the funeral director had violated N.Y. Pub. Health Law art. 34.


OVERVIEW: The funeral director was charged with 22 violations of N.Y. Pub. Health Law art. 34. The department of health determined that the funeral director had violated three provisions and issued a fine. The court annulled the violations that the funeral director failed to provide an itemized list because there was evidence that a complete list had been provided to the customers before the date of the funeral and the determination that the funeral director had engaged in misconduct for high pressure sales tactics because at the time of the violation there were no rules that defined misconduct so that the statute was unconstitutionally vague. The court affirmed the determination that the funeral director had misrepresented expenses that it incurred on behalf of customers and remanded the determination for a reconsideration of the fine.


OUTCOME: The court modified the determination by the department of health by annulling the determination of failing to provide a complete itemized list of services and merchandise and misconduct in the use of high pressure sales tactics, and remitted for reconsideration of the appropriate penalty to be imposed upon petitioners for one proven violation.

 

1070 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Klimek v. Ghent


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


71 A.D.2d 359; 423 N.Y.S.2d 517; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13483



December 27, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order reversed, on the law, without costs, the affirmative defense reinstated, and matter remitted for further proceedings not inconsistent herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant town sought review of an order from the Supreme Court at Special Term, Columbia County (New York), which dismissed an affirmative defense pleaded by the town in a personal injury action brought against it by respondent father on behalf of his minor son and himself.


OVERVIEW: Respondent initiated a personal injury action against the town alleging that the minor sustained injuries as a result of the town's negligent construction of a road. The town asserted as an affirmative defense that it was not liable to respondent because there had been no compliance with a local law barring it from liability for injuries resulting from any of its property being defective, out of repair, unsafe, dangerous or obstructed unless, before the occurrence of the injuries, the town was given notice of the defect and failed to repair it. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's decision and found that the local law was not unconstitutional. The court noted that the local law was not inconsistent with N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 50-e because § 50-e expressly stated that it did not serve to dispense with any notice requirement relative to unsafe conditions that were otherwise be required by law. The town could constitutionally make prior written notice of the condition complained of a condition precedent to the maintenance of an action and to extend the written notice requirement to the dangerous condition of any property owned, operated, or maintained by the town.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order granting respondent's motion to dismiss affirmative defense raised by the town, reinstated the affirmative defense, and remitted the matter for further proceedings.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Prior Written Notice of Defective Condition

There is an exceedingly strong presumption of constitutionality that attaches even to local laws and a local law, which provides that no civil action shall be maintained against a town for injuries resulting from any property of the town being unsafe unless, prior to the occurrence of the injuries, the town shall have been given actual written notice of the condition complained of and shall have failed or neglected within a reasonable time to repair or remove the condition, is not unconstitutional due to any inconsistency with section 50-e of the General Municipal Law, inasmuch as such statute does not serve to dispense with any notice requirement relative to unsafe conditions [***2] which may otherwise be required by law, and plainly passes constitutional muster even though the superseded section 65-a of the Town Law related only to specified property, i.e., unsafe highways, bridges and culverts for which constructive notice was sufficient, since each town is expressly authorized to adopt local laws amending or superseding provisions of the Town Law relating to the property, affairs or government of the individual town unless the Legislature shall have expressly prohibited the adoption of such a local law. (Municipal Home Rule Law, § 10, subd 1, par [ii], cl d, subcl [3].) Accordingly, an order of Special Term, which dismissed the defendant town's affirmative defense that it could not be liable to plaintiff in an action based on personal injuries allegedly sustained as a result of the town's negligence in the construction and maintenance of a road because there had been no compliance with the local law in question, should be reversed, on the law, and the affirmative defense reinstated.

 

1071 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Whidden


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


71 A.D.2d 367; 423 N.Y.S.2d 512; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13486



December 27, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the Washington County Court (New York), entering a judgment of conviction for two counts of rape in the third degree.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, convicted of violation of the statutory rape statutes, N.Y. Penal Law §§ 130.25, 130.30(2), challenged the statutes as violative of equal protection on appeal. The court affirmed his convictions. The statutes' gender-based classifications served important governmental objectives because they prevented early pregnancy and physical and psychological harm. The statutes were also substantially related to the achievement of those objectives.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction; the statutes prevented pregnancy and injury to women and thus served important governmental interests.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Rape

 Section 130.30 of the Penal Law, which provides that a male is guilty of rape in the second degree when, being 18 years old or more, he engages in sexual intercourse with a female less than 14 years old, and subdivision 2 of section 130.25, which provides that a male is guilty of rape in the third degree when, being 21 years old or more, he engages in sexual intercourse with a female less than 17 years old, are not violative of the equal protection clauses of the State and Federal Constitutions despite the fact that only males can be convicted of these crimes inasmuch as the gender-based classifications contained in these statutes serve important governmental objectives regarding uniquely female concerns, e.g., there are greater incidents of female victims, young female victims are more prone to physical injury than males and only the female can become pregnant with possible physical and psychological problems [***2] resulting, and the statutes are substantially related to the achievement of those objectives; furthermore, great deference should be given to legislative judgments concerning problems with which the State is confronted, and particularly to those involving the health, welfare and morale of infants.

 

1072 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Commissioner of Social Services v. G.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


72 A.D.2d 9; 423 N.Y.S.2d 155; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13843



December 27, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order, Family Court, New York County, entered on January 18, 1979, unanimously modified, on the law, to the extent of remanding the proceeding to the Family Court with a direction to include in its support order an income deduction provision pursuant to section 49-b (subd 1, par [b]) and otherwise affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Commissioner of Social Services of the City of New York, citing N.Y. Pers. Prop. Law § 49-b(1)(b), sought review of a decision of the Family Court, New York County (New York), which issued a support order in a child support proceeding that failed to include a payroll deduction order upon the employer of respondent husband.


OVERVIEW: The family court had concluded that issuance and enforcement of a conditional payroll deduction order under N.Y. Pers. Prop. Law § 49-b(1)(b) would constitute taking of property without due process of law and would deny the father the equal protection of the law. The court modified the order with directions to enter an income deduction order. The court stated that the provision for a payroll deduction order to be included in support orders whenever the court directed payments to be made to a support collection unit was a postjudgment collection remedy, intended to enforce judicially established obligations, and did not violate due process. The court determined that because of the state's strong interest in reducing the expense and increasing the effectiveness of its child support enforcement programs, there was no denial of the equal protection of the laws with respect to the father or others similarly situated. The court determined that there was no basis for the family court's conclusion that the requirement for a mandatory conditional payroll deduction order unlawfully interfered with judicial discretion and made the courts a rubber stamp for administrative recommendations.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order of the family court by remanding the proceeding to the family court with a direction to include in its support order an income deduction provision. The court otherwise affirmed the order.


HEADNOTES

Social Services -- Child Support Enforcement Program -- Automatic Entry of Payroll Deduction Order after Default

1. The automatic entry of a payroll deduction order after a specified number of defaults in court-ordered support payments by a respondent whose family is receiving public assistance, as authorized by section 49-b of the Personal Property Law, is not violative of due process of law, by virtue of the fact that service of a payroll deduction order might jeopardize respondent's employment, inasmuch as the compelling interest of the Federal, State [***2] and local governments, acting through the Commissioner of Social Services, in partially recouping welfare payments made to those in need from those obligated to support them outweighs respondent's significant interest in not having his wages garnisheed. Furthermore, a respondent is given an opportunity for notice and hearing at the initial support hearing to determine the extent of his obligation based upon his earnings and responsibilities, and afterwards upon notification of a determination of default, respondent is afforded an opportunity to make up the delinquency as prescribed in the statute; the provision for a payroll deduction order to be included in support orders whenever the court directs payments to a support collection unit is a postjudgment collection remedy intended to enforce judicially established obligations and does not violate due process.

Social Services -- Child Support Enforcement Program -- Automatic Entry of Payroll Deduction Order after Default

2. The automatic entry of a payroll deduction order after a specified number of defaults in court-ordered support payments by a respondent whose family is receiving public assistance, as authorized by section [***3] 49-b of the Personal Property Law, does not deny respondent equal protection of the law, by virtue of the fact that the statute requires such orders only where support is required to be made to a support collection unit and not where the payments are to be made directly to the spouse and/or children, since recipients of State aid, as such, do not constitute a suspect classification and speculation that there might be an unlawful termination of employment by a recalcitrant employer ( CPLR 5252) is hardly a ground for rejecting the classification as unconstitutional in the face of the family's need for support and the right of the State to recoup the support advanced from a respondent responsible for the family's support; furthermore, the distinction between those respondents required to make payments to a support collection unit and those respondents required to make the payments directly does not deny equal protection of the law inasmuch as a classification based upon social and economic considerations is not unconstitutional if it has a rational basis and the State's strong interest in reducing the expense and increasing the effectiveness of its child support enforcement programs warrants [***4] the distinction.

Social Services -- Child Support Enforcement Program -- Automatic Entry of Payroll Deduction Order after Default

3. The automatic entry of a payroll deduction order after a specified number of defaults in court-ordered support payments by a respondent whose family is receiving public assistance, as authorized by section 49-b of the Personal Property Law, does not unlawfully interfere with and infringe upon the authority of the judiciary by precluding the exercise of judicial discretion in determining whether a payroll deduction should be issued since the court's discretion is exercised when the hearing is held to determine the amount of support and the number of defaults required to trigger service of the order on the employer, and there is further opportunity for judicial discretion regarding the 15-day notice provision whereby the respondent is afforded an opportunity to prevent the order from being served by paying the delinquency or applying to the court for a stay.

 

1073 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Greschler v. Greschler


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


71 A.D.2d 322; 422 N.Y.S.2d 718; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13477



December 10, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Kings County, dated March 14, 1979, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, motion granted and complaint dismissed, with leave to plaintiff to serve an amended complaint, if she be so advised, within 20 days after service upon her of a copy of the order to be entered hereon, together with notice of entry thereof.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant ex-husband sought review of the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which denied his motion to dismiss the plaintiff ex-wife's complaint for failure to state a cause of action, pursuant to N.Y.C.P.L.R. 3211.


OVERVIEW: The ex-husband and the ex-wife were married and had three children. They later entered into a separation agreement. Subsequently, the ex-wife executed a power of attorney to enable the ex-husband to obtain a divorce in a foreign country. The divorce was obtained and the decree provided for the survival of the separation agreement. The agreement provided that the ex-husband would support the unemancipated children, but not the ex-wife. The ex-wife sought to have the separation agreement declared void and the marriage reinstated. The court reversed the judgment that denied the ex-husband's motion to dismiss the ex-wife's complaint, holding that her first cause of action that alleged fraud and misrepresentation of his financial circumstances should have been dismissed because her pleadings did not give the trial court or the ex-husband notice of what she intended to prove, pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 3013, 3016(b). The court further held that the complaint should have been dismissed because N.Y. Gen. Oblig. Law § 5-311, was unconstitutionally disparate because it improperly stated that a husband and wife could not contract to relieve the husband from liability to support the wife.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment, which denied the ex-husband's motion to dismiss the ex-wife's complaint for failure to state a cause of action, because the pleadings did not give the trial court nor the ex-husband notice of what she intended to prove and the relevant statute was unconstitutionally disparate.


HEADNOTES

Husband and Wife -- Support

1. Section 5-311 of the General Obligations Law is unconstitutional insofar as it denies husbands and wives the right to contract to relieve the husband of his liability to support his wife, but does not forbid them to contract to relieve the wife of her duty to support her husband unless he is or is likely to become a public charge inasmuch as the statute does not treat men and women equally and this gender-based classification serves no legitimate governmental objective; the statute should not be read expansively to extend its protection to husbands as well as wives since this [***2] would mean depriving husbands of a right to contract which they previously enjoyed and, furthermore, such an extension should be done by the Legislature. Accordingly, a cause of action by plaintiff wife alleging that a part of her separation agreement, in which she waived all claims to support from her husband, is void as against public policy is properly dismissed.

Pleading -- Sufficiency of Pleading

2. A cause of action by plaintiff wife, sounding in fraud, alleging that defendant husband knowingly misrepresented his financial circumstances to induce her to execute a separation agreement and to later obtain a divorce, fails to meet the minimum requirements of CPLR 3013 and 3016 (subd [b]), which concern the particularity of statements contained in pleadings regarding this type of action, and cannot withstand defendant's motion to dismiss where the complaint contains bare conclusory allegations giving neither the court nor the defendant adequate notice of what she intends to prove inasmuch as the essential material must appear on the face of the complaint; furthermore, in answering the defendant's motion to dismiss, the plaintiff offered no satisfactory explanation [***3] for her failure to set forth her husband's representations with particularity and has failed to explain why her pleadings are so general.

 

1074 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Thomas


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


71 A.D.2d 280; 422 N.Y.S.2d 394; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13469



December 6, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, Bronx County, rendered on December 15, 1977, reversed, on the law, and the matter remanded for a new trial.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Supreme Court (New York) convicted defendant of three counts of murder in the second degree. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant confessed to stabbing and killing his girlfriend and her two young children in a fit of jealousy but latter recanted and claimed the confession was the product of police coercion and duress. The victims were found stabbed multiple times and all died shortly thereafter from the brutal beatings sustained. The trial court offered a second degree murder instruction which indicated that "a person is presumed to intend that which he actually does." On appeal, the court recognized that the instruction was errant, and that the trial court should have explained that the presumption of intent was permissive, not mandatory, and, in any event, rebuttable. The court also found that the error here was of constitutional dimension and harmful per se where it shifted the state's burden of proof as to an element of the crime, defendant's intent to kill. The convictions were reversed and the matter remanded for a new trial accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court convictions on the law and remanded the matter for a new trial.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Instructions

1. A conviction of defendant on three counts of murder in the second degree is reversed, on the law, and remanded for a new trial where the trial court's instructions to the jury, in effect, directed them to find an intent to kill because defendant's acts caused death; the court should have explained to the jury that the presumption of intent, i.e., a person is presumed to intend the natural and probable consequences of his act, is permissive, not mandatory and, in any event, rebuttable. The error cannot be deemed harmless since it absolved the People of the duty to prove an essential element of murder in the second degree, the intent to kill; moreover, having recognized the existence of a reasonable view of the evidence to justify the submission of manslaughter in the first degree as a lesser included [***2] offense, the court's charge removed the lesser offense from the jury's consideration by precluding a finding that defendant acted with any intent other than to kill.

Crimes -- Appeal

2. A failure by defendant to take an appropriate exception to a trial court's charge to the jury does not mean that any error therein is not preserved for appellate review where the error was of a constitutional dimension in that it involved a shifting of the People's burden of proof as to the elements of a crime inasmuch as no exception is necessary to preserve for appellate review a deprivation of a fundamental constitutional right.

 

1075 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Pratt v. Melton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


72 A.D.2d 887; 422 N.Y.S.2d 169; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14178



November 29, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent, the Commissioner of the Department of Motor Vehicles of the State of New York, sought review of a judgment from the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which granted petitioner's application to annul a determination of respondent suspending petitioner's driver's license, and which denied respondent's motion to transfer the proceeding to the appellate division.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner stuck and killed a pedestrian in the crosswalk of a public highway. A referee determined that petitioner was not paying attention to the traffic pattern in violation of N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Laws § 1154, and suspended his driver's license. Petitioner appealed the decision to the supreme court, claiming that the notice he received informing him of the referee's hearing was inadequate, misleading and unconstitutionally vague. Petitioner's appeal was heard initially by the supreme court. On appeal, the court found that the supreme court improperly retained jurisdiction of the case instead of transferring the matter to the appellate division. Respondent then appealed, but the court elected to treat the matter as if it had never been considered by the supreme court. The court found petitioner's claims to be without merit, and that the referee's findings were supported by ample evidence. Accordingly, the court reversed the supreme court's judgment that dismissed petitioner's case.


OUTCOME: The court found that the supreme court had improperly retained jurisdiction over the matter. The court reversed the decision and dismissed the petition after concluding that there was ample evidence in the record to support a finding that petitioner was in violation of applicable provisions of the vehicle and traffic law.

Press v. County of Monroe


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


72 A.D.2d 915; 422 N.Y.S.2d 195; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14219



November 16, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owners of 135 apartments filed an action against defendants, a sewer district and others, seeking a declaratory judgment in the Supreme Court, Monroe County (New York). Plaintiffs challenged the validity of the sewer assessments adopted pursuant to N.Y. County Law § 271 as applied to the apartments they owned in three specific years. Defendants sought review of the trial court's denial of their motion to dismiss.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs attacked the assessments as discriminatory and unconstitutional in that residential structures containing four or more dwelling units were assessed, without a rational basis, at a higher and more burdensome rate than residential structures containing one, two, or three dwelling units. The sewer district argued that plaintiffs' sole remedy was by way of a certiorari proceeding commenced under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 that had to have been filed within four months after the adoption of the assessment rolls for the years in question pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 217. The court held that plaintiffs' proper course was first to exhaust their administrative remedies by seeking a change or amendment in the assessment rolls prior to the final adoption of the questioned assessment pursuant to N.Y. County Law § 271. Plaintiffs had to appear and object at the public hearings and, if not successful, they were then able to commence a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78 to review the actions of the sewer district in each year.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's order and dismissed the complaint.

Roosevelt & Cross, Inc. v. County of Albany


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


72 A.D.2d 855; 421 N.Y.S.2d 682; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14139



November 8, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff underwriters appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court in Albany County (New York), which granted a motion by defendant county for summary judgment dismissing the underwriters' breach of contract complaint.


OVERVIEW: The county published a notice of sale inviting sealed bids for the purchase of general obligation bonds. The notice stated that as a condition precedent to the consideration of any bid, each bidder was to place a deposit of a designated amount, all bids were publicly opened and announced, the bonds would be delivered and would be legal and binding. The underwriters placed a bid and deposit and the bid was awarded to the underwriters. Thereafter, a third party commenced an action against the county and the county notified the underwriters by submitting an addendum to the underlying agreement. The underwriters refused to accept the bonds and demanded the return of their deposit. The county refused to return the deposit and the underwriters commenced a breach of contract action. The trial court granted the county's motion for summary judgment, the underwriters appealed, and the court upheld the judgment. The court held that the county did not alter the terms of the contract, they merely supplemented the information provided to the underwriters. Additionally, the court held that the underwriters failed to show that the county breached the contract in any way.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment granting summary judgment in the county's favor.

 

1079 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Morgan v. New York Racing Asso.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


72 A.D.2d 740; 421 N.Y.S.2d 249; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13956



November 5, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner horse owner appealed a judgment from the Supreme Court, Nassau County (New York), which dismissed the petition as to respondents, racing board and racing association, as premature, and directed respondent club to hold a hearing with respect to the horse owner's request to reregister the horse.


OVERVIEW: The racing board and racing association rejected the horse owner's application to race its horse on the ground that it was not properly registered with the club, pursuant to N.Y. Comp. Codes R. & Regs. tit. 9, § 4024.1(a). The horse owner commenced the proceeding to compel the club to accept a new registration for the horse under its true name and to permit it to race in the state. The trial court dismissed the petition against the racing board and racing association as premature, and directed the club to hold a hearing on the horse owner's request to reregister the horse. The trial court's judgment was affirmed. The club refused to register the horse and § 4024.1 provided that no horse was allowed to start in any race unless registered and named in the registry office of the club. Thus, the court held that it was proper to have dismissed the petition as to the racing board and racing association. Further, the club had procedures for internal review of its decisions, which the horse owner failed to exhaust before seeking redress from the court, and the court properly ordered the horse owner to pursue the review procedures available from the club.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment, which dismissed the petition to the racing board and racing association as premature, and directed the club to hold a hearing with respect to the horse owner's request to reregister the horse.

 

1080 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Mitchell


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


70 A.D.2d 367; 421 N.Y.S.2d 443; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12724



November 2, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously reversed, without costs, and matter remitted to Onondaga County Family Court for further proceedings in accordance with opinion by Callahan, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner father sought review of a judgment from the Family Court, Onondaga County (New York), which denied the father's petition for habeas corpus and ordered that adoption proceedings of the infant be facilitated in the best interest of the child. The father had brought the habeas corpus action to require respondent department of social services to show cause why the child should not be released to the father's custody.


OVERVIEW: The father, who was 19 years of age and unwed, filed a habeas corpus petition seeking to require the department of social services to show cause why his child should not be released to the father's custody. The child's mother had put him up for adoption. The trial court denied the father's petition and ordered that adoption proceedings be facilitated in the best interest of the child. The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the case. The court held that: (1) it was clear that the father had not surrendered the child, nor was there a finding of abandonment, persistent neglect, or unfitness; (2) absent findings of surrender, abandonment, persistent neglect, or unfitness, the court could not permanently sever all parental ties; (3) the matter should be remitted to the trial court for an immediate hearing and decision in accordance with existing law; (4) the record should be supplemented to include appropriate social investigation, interviews, and reports; (5) the father should not be precluded from presenting all relative and material proof from witnesses on his behalf.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which had denied the father's habeas corpus petition, and remanded the case to the trial court.


HEADNOTES

Appeal -- Law Governing at Time of Appeal

1. An appellate court must decide a case on the basis of the law as it exists at the time of judicial review.

Adoption -- Consent of Natural Father

2. The parental rights of the father of a child born out of wedlock may not be terminated by ordering that adoption proceedings of the child be facilitated in the best interests of the child, without a finding of abandonment, surrender or unfitness, in view of Caban v Mohammed (441 U.S. 380), which declared section 111 (subd 1, par [c]) of the Domestic Relations Law, requiring consent to the adoption of a child born out of wedlock to be given only by the mother, unconstitutional as a violation of the equal protection [***2] clause.

Parent and Child -- Custody -- Rights of Natural Father

3. A natural parent has a right to the care and custody of his child superior to all others and this right can be dissolved only by abandonment, surrender or unfitness; furthermore, the natural father of an illegitimate child possesses this right no less than the father of a child born in wedlock

 

1081 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Ziecker v. Orchard Park


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


70 A.D.2d 422; 421 N.Y.S.2d 447; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12732



November 2, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order unanimously affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant municipalities appealed from an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term in Erie County (New York), which granted an application by plaintiff child to file a late notice of claim against the municipalities and determined that, by reason of the infancy and disability of the child, N.Y. C.P.L.R. 208 authorized an extension of time under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 50-e(5).


OVERVIEW: The child was seriously injured when he dived headfirst into shallow water at a municipal park and was hospitalized for more than a year. After the child was released from the hospital, the child and his father filed motions for an order pursuant to N.Y. Gen. Law § 50-e(5) for leave to file a late notice of claim against the municipalities. The trial court granted the child's motion and held that, under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 208, the child's infancy and disability tolled the period for filing a claim. The trial court denied the father's motion and held that the derivative claim of the child's father was not tolled. The municipalities appealed from so much of the order as granted the application of the child. The court affirmed and held that N.Y. Gen. Law § 50-e(5) conferred upon the trial court broad discretion to extend the time to file a notice of claim beyond the prescribed time limit and that the tolling provisions of N.Y. C.P.L.R. 208 applied. The court further found that the municipalities were not prejudiced by the extension of time because they had actual notice of the accident as shown by their immediate investigation of the accident.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order granting the child leave to file a late claim against the municipalities.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Notice of Claim

Under subdivision 5 of section 50-e of the General Municipal Law, as amended effective September 1, 1976, the period of one year and 90 days within which a court of competent jurisdiction may extend the time for a notice of claim to be served upon a public corporation may be tolled by infancy under CPLR 208, since it was the intent of the Legislature to extend significantly the discretion of the court to grant leave to file a notice of claim, and consideration of infancy is warranted even though the disability may not have been the reason for the failure to serve a late notice; accordingly, an infant injured less than two months before the amendment may, some 17 months after the accident, file a late notice of claim against [***2] the town and village allegedly responsible for his injuries, since the amendment has been given a modified retroactive effect to claimants whose causes of action accrued within the prescribed one-year period preceding the effective amendatory date, and since the defendant municipalities not only had notice of plaintiff's injuries on the day it occurred, but actually investigated it that day. A just claim for damages for a serious injury should not be forfeited for failure to give notice where the basic purpose of the statute is not offended and where no substantial prejudice exists.

 

1082 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Long Island Oil Terminals Asso. v. Commissioner of New York State Dep't of Transp.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


70 A.D.2d 303; 421 N.Y.S.2d 405; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12712; 13 ERC (BNA) 1953



October 25, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff trade association appealed an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which denied its motion for a preliminary injunction enjoining defendant state enforcement departments, their agents and employees, pendente lite, from enforcing certain provisions of N.Y. Nav. Law art. 12 in the association's action for a declaratory judgment that art. 12 was unconstitutional, and seeking the injunction.


OVERVIEW: The trade association's members owned and operated oil storage terminals that were "major facilities" as defined in N.Y. Nav. Law § 172(11). New York's Oil Spill Prevention and Compensation Act, 1977 N.Y. Laws 845, which enacted N.Y. Nav. Law art. 12, required each such operator to get a license and pay a license fee until the New York Environmental and Spill Compensation Fund reached $ 25 million. The fund was to be used to pay for cleanup of oil and property damage, and major facility operators were required to reimburse the fund for amounts expended as a result of their discharges. The association brought an action seeking a declaration that art. 12 violated the import-export, commerce, equal protection, and due process clauses of the United States Constitution, and for a preliminary injunction. The trial court denied the injunction. On appeal, the court affirmed, concluding that the association failed to meet its burden to show it had a clear right to ultimate victory or that art. 12 was unconstitutional, where the license fee was on the transfer of oil rather than the oil itself, and there was no factual basis for the claim that the fees were excessive.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying the association's motion for a preliminary injunction against enforcement of provisions of New York's Oil Spill Prevention and Compensation Act.


HEADNOTES

Injunctions -- Preliminary Injunction

1. A motion for a preliminary injunction is addressed to the discretion of the trial court, and the decision of the trial court on such a motion will not be disturbed on appeal, unless there is a showing of abuse of discretion, and an order denying a motion for a preliminary injunction will be reversed only in an exceptional case.

Injunctions -- Preliminary Injunction

2. One seeking a preliminary injunction has the heavy burden of showing that he has a clear right to ultimate victory on the merits and that he will suffer immediate and irreparable harm if the preliminary injunction is denied.

Statutes -- Presumption of Constitutionality

3. A strong presumption [***2] of validity attaches to legislative enactments and a party who is attacking the constitutionality of a statute bears the heavy burden of establishing unconstitutionality beyond a reasonable doubt.

Environmental Conservation -- Oil Spill Prevention, Control and Compensation Act -- License Fee

4. Article 12 of the Navigation Law, the Oil Spill Prevention, Control and Compensation Act, which requires each operator of a major facility (Navigation Law, § 172, subd 11) to obtain a license from the Department of Transportation (Navigation Law, § 174, subds 1, 2, 3), and pay a license fee of 1 cent per barrel transferred until the balance in the New York Environmental and Spill Compensation Fund equals or exceeds $ 25 million (Navigation Law, § 174, subd 4), which fund provides a source of payment for expenses incurred by the State for cleanup and removal of petroleum and property damage caused by oil discharges (Navigation Law, § 176), is not unconstitutional in that the fee is an impost and duty on imports in violation of clause 2 of section 10 of article I of the United States Constitution, since the license fee is imposed on the transfer of petroleum and not on the petroleum [***3] itself, and the license fee does not discriminate against interstate commerce, since the fee is not imposed only on those New York transfers where petroleum enters the State, but rather, the statute focuses on New York major facility transfers without reference to where the petroleum was produced; accordingly, in an action for a judgment declaring that article 12 is unconstitutional and to enjoin the enforcement of the provisions of article 12, plaintiff, a trade association whose members own and operate oil storage terminals, has failed to establish a clear right to ultimate success or that article 12 is unconstitutional beyond a reasonable doubt, and a motion for a preliminary injunction was properly denied.

 

1083 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Koffler


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


70 A.D.2d 252; 420 N.Y.S.2d 560; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12704



October 1, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner the Joint Bar Association Grievance Committee for the Tenth Judicial District (New York) sought confirmation of their report holding that respondent attorneys were in violation of N.Y. Jud. Law § 479 and N.Y. Code of Prof'l Responsibility DR 2-103(A) for their mass mailings to real estate brokers and prospective clients to establish attorney-client relationships and solicit retainers.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner grievance committee held respondent attorneys in violation of N.Y. Jud. Law § 479 and N.Y. Code of Prof'l Responsibility DR 2-103(A) for mass mailings to real estate brokers and prospective clients to establish attorney-client relationships and solicit retainers. The court confirmed the report holding that the mailings exceeded the bounds of permissible commercial speech because they constituted solicitations rather than advertising where they did not merely advise the public of the availability of legal services, but sought out particular individuals believed to be interested in a particular transaction, and urged them to retain respondents. The court held that § 479 and DR 2-103(A) were constitutional insofar as the ban on solicitations by mail or in person was a "reasonable restriction" on the "manner of advertising." The important governmental interest in prohibiting such solicitation stemmed from the potential for abuse including the possible conflict of interest in this case to the detriment of the property sellers. Because respondents' letters were apparently sent in good faith reliance on precedent, the court found disbarment, suspension, or censure unnecessary.


OUTCOME: The report of petitioner grievance committee was confirmed because respondent attorneys' mass mailings constituted solicitations in violation of professional rules rather than permissible advertising, and the rules against such solicitation were constitutional as "reasonable restrictions" on the "manner of advertising" allowed by attorneys licensed by the state.


HEADNOTES

Attorney and Client -- Disciplinary Proceedings

1. An attorney's mailing of letters to individuals identified as prospective clients and to real estate brokers for the purpose of establishing an attorney-client relationship and soliciting a retainer in the identified transaction for the attorney's pecuniary gain exceeds the bounds of permissible commercial speech and is properly proscribed by section 479 of the Judiciary Law, which makes unlawful the soliciting either directly or indirectly of legal business, and DR 2-103 (A) of the Code of Professional Responsibility, which essentially is a duplicate of the statute, as adopted by the New York State Bar Association; section 479 of the Judiciary Law and DR 2-103 (A) of the Code of Professional [***2] Responsibility are constitutional insofar as they ban solicitation of legal business by mail as well as in person.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Regulation of Commercial Speech

2. Although commercial speech is not wholly outside the protection of the First Amendment, it is distinguishable from other forms of speech and holds a subordinate position in the scale of First Amendment values; particularly, there is a "common-sense" distinction between speech proposing a commercial transaction which occurs in an area traditionally subject to government regulation and other varieties of speech, and the State has a special interest in regulating members of a profession it licenses, and who serve as officers of its courts. Therefore, modes of regulation that might be impermissible in the realm of noncommercial expression may be applied to forms of commercial speech, and although some forms of commercial speech regulation are surely permissible, the State may not completely prevent the dissemination, by commercial speech, of the price of professional services.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Regulation of Commercial Speech

3. The State may promulgate [***3] a reasonable regulation of the manner in which commercial advertising may be distributed and, in particular, may restrict advertising that is related to activities which the State may legitimately regulate.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Advertising by Attorneys

4. Advertising by attorneys may not be subjected to blanket suppression because the State's interest in maintaining high standards for the professions licensed by it may not be enforced by keeping the public in ignorance of the entirely lawful terms that competing licensed professionals are offering; specifically, the State may not prevent the publication in a newspaper of an attorney's truthful advertisement concerning the availability and terms of routine legal services, but nevertheless, the State may restrict the manner of advertising professional services provided that restrictions of that kind are justified without reference to the content of the regulated speech, that they serve a significant governmental interest, and that in so doing they leave open ample alternative channels for communication of the information.

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Speech -- Solicitation by Attorneys

 [***4] 5. Solicitation by a lawyer of remunerative employment is a business transaction in which speech is an essential but subordinate component so that the banning thereof is subjected to a lower level of an appropriate judicial scrutiny than would be the case if it did not involve a business transaction, and the protection of the public from aspects of solicitation which involve "vexatious conduct", is a legitimate and important State interest; the State has the right to take measures to regulate substantive evils, including invasion of privacy, that potentially are present in solicitation of prospective clients by lawyers. Moreover, the State has an interest in minimizing commercialization of the legal profession and considerations of undue commercialization of the legal profession are more than of marginal force where the solicitation is for pecuniary gain; the State is free to fashion reasonable restrictions with respect to the manner of solicitation by members of its Bar, and the State may apply narrowly drawn rules to proscribe solicitation that in fact is overbearing.

 

1084 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Cohen v. Pearl River Union Free School Dist.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


70 A.D.2d 94; 419 N.Y.S.2d 998; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12306



August 27, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Rockland County, dated September 22, 1978, reversed insofar as appealed from, on the law, without costs or disbursements, and, upon reargument, application to file a late notice of claim on behalf of the infant petitioner against the Pearl River Union Free School District is denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent school district appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Rockland County (New York), which, upon reargument, granted the application of petitioner infant for leave to serve a late notice of claim against the school district. The infant had been injured while participating in a school soccer game.


OVERVIEW: While participating in a school soccer game at the school district's field, the infant allegedly sustained an injury to his foot when it struck a hidden object protruding from the ground. The application for leave to file a late claim on behalf of the infant was filed 26 months after the accident. The lower court initially denied the application, but, after a reargument, the motion was granted. The school district appealed and the court reversed. The court held that the legislature never intended that the limitation of one year and 90 days in which a court could exercise its discretion to grant late filing, based on the disability of infancy, would have been automatically extended by the disability itself. The court held that because the lower court had lacked the power to grant an extension for filing of the notice of claim beyond the period of one year and 90 days after the date of the accident on which the claim was based, the order was to be reversed and the application denied.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order of the lower court, which granted the application to file a late notice of claim on behalf of the infant against the school district.


HEADNOTES

Schools -- Notice of Claim

1. Under subdivision 5 of section 50-e of the General Municipal Law, as amended September 1, 1976, the period of one year and 90 days within which a court may exercise its discretion to grant an extension for late filing of a notice of claim to be served upon a public corporation is not tolled by the disability of infancy under CPLR 208; accordingly, an application for leave to file a late claim on behalf of an infant made 15 months after the effective date of the amendment to [***2] section 50-e and some 26 months after the accident, should be denied.

Statutes -- Notice of Claim Statutes

2. Whether regarded as permissible qualifications upon a legislatively created right or as reasonable conditions for the exercise of a common-law right, the recognized purposes of a notice of claim statute are, inter alia, to afford a local government the opportunity to fully investigate a claim against it, and, if regarded as appropriate, to settle claims without the expense and hazards of litigation. Though notice of claim provisions also benefit claimants by assuring earlier processing and consideration of their claims, they are enacted primarily for the benefit of the government agencies to which they apply.

 

1085 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Rosano


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


69 A.D.2d 643; 419 N.Y.S.2d 543; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11843



August 6, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Four judgments of the Supreme Court, Queens County, all rendered May 23, 1978, modified, on the law, by (1) reversing the convictions of all defendants under counts 213, 214, 215 and 216, and the sentences imposed thereon, and the said counts are dismissed and (2) reversing the conviction of defendant Naples under count 222, and the sentence imposed thereon, and said count dismissed as to Naples. As so modified, judgments affirmed, and case remitted to the Supreme Court, Queens County, for further proceedings pursuant to CPL 460.50 (subd 5).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, who were developers, appealed judgments from the Supreme Court, Queens County, (New York) convicting defendants of larceny in violation of N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a and perjury in violation in N.Y. Penal Law § 210.35.


OVERVIEW: Defendants developed a condominium project. Each was convicted in relation to criminal misconduct related to the project. Defendants contended that the evidence was insufficient to sustain their convictions had the trial court not mistakenly treated their repayment defense to larceny as an affirmative defense, that N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a was unconstitutional, and that they did not have the requisite intent to sustain the perjury conviction under N.Y. Penal Law § 210.35. The court disagreed on the larceny charge but agreed as to the perjury conviction. N.Y. Lien Law § 79-a was determined to be constitutional, and, although the court agreed that it was an ordinary defense, defendants failed to raise the defense within the limits imposed by the legislature. As to the perjury convictions, the court determined that defendants lacked the required culpable intent required.


OUTCOME: Defendants' convictions relating to the larceny charge were affirmed. However, the convictions for perjury were reversed because the People failed to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that defendants made apparently false statements.


HEADNOTES

Crimes -- Larceny -- Misappropriation of Trust Funds

1. Judgments convicting the defendants, a corporate builder and three corporate principals, of larceny under section 79-a of the Lien Law in that they [***4] disbursed for nontrust purposes building loan contract funds and funds advanced by contract vendees to two of the corporate principals or to other corporations controlled by them, are affirmed, where the disbursements were made as repayments for the acquisition of land, since the defense of repayment (Lien Law, § 79-a, subd 2) which provides a trustee with a defense to the charge of larceny where his application of trust funds for a nontrust purpose is a repayment of an advance actually applied for a trust purpose, was not available, because the purpose of the trust is that the trust assets of which an owner is trustee shall be held and applied for payment of the cost of improvement and the purchase of land is not a "cost of improvement", and even if the separate existence of the individual defendants' various business entities is ignored and the expenditures are categorized as repayments by the trustee to itself, the payments would not qualify as a cost of improvement even if they were within the definition in subdivision 5 of section 2 of the Lien Law, which provides that reimbursement of an owner for payments made for improvements prior to the date of an initial advance under a [***5] building loan mortgage are deemed a cost of improvement only if such payments are itemized in the building loan contract; since the payments alleged were not made for trust purposes and were not listed in the construction loan contract, any suggestion that the lending institution agreed that trust funds could be so diverted would constitute a charge that it too violated the Lien Law and would not constitute a legal defense. Moreover, defendants did not succeed in raising the defense of repayment because they did not come forward with sufficient evidence to impose the burden of disproving it on the People.

Courts -- Stare Decisis -- Dicta

2. The rule of stare decisis does not apply to dicta.

Crimes -- Larceny -- Misappropriation of Trust Funds -- Defense of Repayment

3. The repayment defense contained in subdivision 2 of section 79-a of the Lien Law was intended to be an ordinary rather than an affirmative defense.

Crimes -- Larceny -- Misappropriation of Trust Funds -- Presumption of Wrongful Diversion of Funds

4. The presumption in subdivision 3 of section 79-a of the Lien Law, which provides that a trustee's failure to keep required books [***6] or records shall be presumptive evidence of wrongful diversion of trust funds, furnishes reasonable protection to those entitled to payment for improvement of property for which the contractor has been paid, and it places no unreasonable burden upon the contractor; a statutory presumption of guilt arising from unexplained and willful failure to comply with the provisions of the statute rests upon a sound foundation and does not violate any provision of the Constitution of the State of New York or of the United States.

Statutes -- Presumptions

5. The controlling test for determining the validity of a statutory presumption is that there be a rational connection between the fact proved and the fact presumed; it must be shown that the presumed fact is more likely than not to flow from the proved facts on which it is made to depend.

Crimes -- Larceny -- Misappropriation of Trust Funds -- Liability of Individual Defendant

6. Three individual defendants, corporate principals, were properly convicted of larceny under section 79-a of the Lien Law in that they disbursed for nontrust purposes building loan contract funds and funds advanced by contract vendees to two of [***7] the corporate principals or to other corporations controlled by them, since section 79-a provides for individual liability for a corporate trustee's diversion of trust funds in that it applies to any trustee of a trust and any officer, director or agent of such trustee, and there was evidence that the defendants actively participated in the wrong of the corporation or had knowledge of use of trust funds in the corporate business.

Crimes -- Making Apparently Sworn False Statements -- Intent

7. Judgments convicting defendants, a corporate builder and three corporate principals, of making apparently sworn false statements in the second degree (Penal Law, § 210.35) in that one of the defendants subscribed affidavits upon which construction loan advances were made which contained a declaration that all bills due to the date of the advance were paid despite the fact that there were unpaid bills at the time the affidavits were executed, are reversed, since the requisite intent that the statement be uttered or published as true, was not established; the lending institution was aware of the existence of unpaid bills when it made advances under the construction loan agreement and [***8] that the advances were made for the purpose of enabling the sponsor to pay the accrued bills, and it was not shown that the defendants deliberately concealed the existence of unpaid contractors or that they delivered the affidavits with the intent that they be published as true.

Crimes -- False Representations in Offering Statements

8. The evidence was sufficient to sustain convictions of a corporate builder and two corporate principals of violating sections 352-c, 352-e and 359-g of the General Business Law insofar as an offering statement falsely represented that the defendants would hold in trust moneys received from purchasers of condominium homes and insofar as the offering statement omitted the material fact that sewer approval had been revoked; however, since the trial court found a third corporate principal not guilty insofar as the statement omitted that fact that sewer approval had been revoked on the ground that there was no evidence connecting him to the preparation, filing or amendment of the offering statement, his conviction insofar as the statement falsely represented that the defendants would hold in trust moneys received from purchasers of condominium [***9] homes is reversed. Additionally, defendants' convictions of violating sections 352-h and 359-g of the General Business Law in that they misappropriated moneys received from purchasers of condominium units were supported by the evidence.

 

1086 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Greenberg v. CBS, Inc.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


69 A.D.2d 693; 419 N.Y.S.2d 988; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11846; 5 Media L. Rep. 1470



August 6, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Nassau County, dated July 26, 1978, affirmed, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff physician and defendants, television network, program producer, and correspondent, challenged a decision of the Supreme Court of New York , Appellate Division, which denied both parties' motions for summary judgment in the physician's libel action.


OVERVIEW: The television network broadcast a program seen by millions of people that dealt with amphetamine abuse. In the program, a patient made comments that the physician prescribed certain amphetamine substitutes for her, and she alleged that taking these medications did harm to her daughter, who was born with birth defects. The physician alleged that this was defamatory, and the network argued that the statements were true. The court found that the physician was not a limited issue public figure because he did not thrust himself into the public controversy over amphetamines, especially in light of the fact that he had last treated the patient more than 10 years prior to the broadcast. Regarding the media's duty of care, the court found that the patient's statements were not confirmed for accuracy, and that the network relied on undisclosed sources for verification. Overall, the court found that a trial was required to evaluate the actions of the network in its investigative reporting that allegedly defamed the doctor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of summary judgment to all parties in the physician's libel action.


HEADNOTES

Constitutional Law -- Freedom of Press

1. While there is no privilege having a greater right to, or need for, protection, than that of freedom of the press, the judicial policy against inhibition of the vigorous and fruitful exercise of First Amendment freedoms by the media is not the equivalent of insurance against all risks. Accordingly, since the reputation and privacy of the individual or individuals discussed is also at stake in the course of disseminating information in the public domain, "hit and run" journalism is no more protected under the First Amendment than speeding on a crowded sidewalk is permitted under a valid driver's license.

Libel and Slander -- Summary Judgment

2. If a material, triable issue of fact exists in a libel action, summary judgment must be denied, since, although motions for summary judgment in defamation actions [***4] are invaluable devices to insure the free and uninhibited debate of matters of public concern by obviating the necessity for protracted and expensive litigation where there are no factual issues, solicitude for First Amendment freedoms was not intended to abrogate the fundamental rules governing the administration of summary judgment. Accordingly, the Appellate Division affirmed Special Term's denial of cross motions for summary judgment in a libel action on the ground that issues of fact existed relative to the falsity of statements and the degree of care exercised by a television network and individual defendants in confirming their accuracy, employing a two-pronged analysis to ascertain if factual questions existed: the form, content, effect, and falsity of the allegedly defamatory statements were first examined, since the plaintiff bears the burden of showing that the statements are in fact libelous, and then the First Amendment limitations on recovery were applied, since the burden of defeating constitutionally mandated privileges raised by defendants is also on the plaintiff; in making such two-pronged analysis, the following issues were considered: the libelous nature of the [***5] statements; whether the status of plaintiff, a doctor who was the subject of a televised program on amphetamine abuse, was that of a "limited issue" public figure; and the telecasters' duty of care in assessing the accuracy of comments made during a taped interview, which was included in the broadcast, by a former patient of plaintiff doctor concerning the amount and nature of medication he prescribed for her.

Libel and Slander -- Actionable Words -- Context

3. An allegedly libelous statement must be understood in the context in which it is heard. Accordingly, where the whole thrust of a television report on amphetamine abuse was not only that the prescribing of amphetamines and amphetamine substitutes for obesity, which a doctor named in the broadcast allegedly did in excess, was bad medical practice, but that such practice was illegal and carried criminal sanctions that were difficult to enforce, the defamatory nature of the statements made about him was reinforced both by the context of the telecast and the setting in which the statements were made.

Libel and Slander -- Actionable Words -- Requirement of Falsity

4. There can be no recovery in a defamation [***6] action unless the statements which are the subject of the action are false.

Libel and Slander -- Expression of Opinion

5. Opinions are constitutionally protected and may not be the subject of defamation actions, provided that the facts supporting the opinions are set forth as its bases; however, if the facts are false, or they are not stated, the opinion is actionable.

Libel and Slander -- Expression of Opinion -- Context

6. Whether an allegedly defamatory statement constitutes fact or opinion is a question of law, which distinction is frequently a difficult one, since what constitutes a statement of fact in one context may be treated as a statement of opinion in another, in light of the nature and content of the communication taken as a whole; opinions which label people or things generally employ terms which are loose and figurative, rather than a precise designation which is subject to rigorous examination for its truth or falsity. Accordingly, a statement by plaintiff doctor's former patient that he had prescribed "amphetamine-type" drugs for her is not a statement of opinion.

Libel and Slander -- "Limited Issue" Public Figure

7. Whether an [***7] individual is a "limited issue" public figure so as to give rise to protection against liability for defamatory statements concerning him is a question of law in which the nature and extent of his participation in the particular controversy giving rise to the defamation are the essential issues; in the absence of an allegation that the plaintiff in a defamation action has acted to generate the dispute, a finding that a public controversy existed at the time plaintiff acted is a prerequisite to a finding that he voluntarily acted to produce a specific outcome and, even if a continuing controversy is shown, his actions must constitute significant participation in the controversy which actions invite or attempt to attract public attention, in order to confer such status on him. Accordingly, a doctor who may have prescribed amphetamines for a patient, whom he treated for obesity for a short time more than 10 years prior to a telecast report on amphetamine abuse, in which broadcast he was named and allegedly defamed, and who treated her at a time in which no public debate regarding the use of such drugs to combat obesity is suggested in the record, is not a "limited issue" public figure,  [***8] since the nature of his actions was not then controversial and, even assuming an on-going controversy, his involvement in it was not significant; nor is the fact that he had, over a period of years, published articles in scientific books and journals, which were intended for a scholarly audience rather than a mass market, enough to make him a "limited issue" public figure where the articles did not involve the subject matter of the telecast or attract public attention, since it is the breadth of the audience coupled with the appeal of the topic upon which emphasis should be placed, not the extensiveness of the publishing activities.

Libel and Slander -- "Limited Issue" Public Figure

8. Those charged with defamation cannot, by their own conduct, create their own defense by making the plaintiff a public figure. Accordingly, where defendant television reporter attempted to foist "limited issue" public figure status on plaintiff doctor by asking him for an interview in which he would comment, generally, as a practitioner in the treatment of obesity, on the abuse of amphetamines and their substitutes, but failed to confront plaintiff in any way with specific charges of such [***9] abuse which had been made against him by a former patient, defendants' contention that the plaintiff should not be permitted to avoid the status of a "limited issue" public figure by using an "ostrich" approach to the controversy by refusing to be interviewed is specious.

Libel and Slander -- Public Figure

9. Absent clear evidence of general fame or notoriety in the community and pervasive involvement in the affairs of society, an individual should not be deemed a public personality for all aspects of his life; it is preferable to reduce the public figure question to a more meaningful context by looking to the nature and extent of an individual's participation in the particular controversy giving rise to the defamation. Accordingly, even where an individual consents to be interviewed by the media, the interview does not necessarily insure public figure status.

Libel and Slander -- Actionable Words

10. The States are free to define their own standards of liability for the actionable defamation of a private individual by a news publisher or broadcaster.

Libel and Slander -- News Publisher or Broadcaster -- Gross Negligence Standard

11. Where the content [***10] of a news article is arguably within the sphere of legitimate public concern, which is reasonably related to matters warranting public exposition, a private individual defamed therein may recover for such defamation if he establishes, by a preponderance of the evidence, that the publisher or broadcaster acted in a grossly irresponsible manner, without due consideration for the standards of information gathering and dissemination ordinarily followed by reasonable parties. Accordingly, although a telecast report on the topic of amphetamine abuse is within the sphere of public concern and the personal experience of an individual who was interviewed on the program regarding such abuse is reasonably related to matters warranting public exposition, an attempt by defendant newsperson to interview plaintiff doctor, as a practitioner in the treatment of obesity, on the abuse of amphetamines and their substitutes, cannot be equated to any confrontation to determine the accuracy of charges concerning the way in which he prescribed such drugs, made against him on the program by a former patient, and is not sufficient to support a finding that defendants acted responsibly as a matter of law.

 [***11] Libel and Slander -- Defense of Verification -- Newspersons' "Shield Law" Privilege

12. In a defamation action by a private individual against a newsperson, no consideration will be given, on appeal, to the defense of verification, where it is based on confidential material covered by the newspersons' privilege under the "Shield Law" (Civil Rights Law, § 79-h), which privilege protects both the identity of the source and the information obtained, vests the media with the option to disclose or to refuse to disclose such sources and information, and does not include a divestiture procedure. Accordingly, where defendants newspersons rely on undisclosed sources and confidential information for verification of allegedly false and defamatory telecast material and offer this verification as "proof" of their responsibility in gathering and disseminating the report, thus putting in issue the very privilege upon which they rely, such exploitation of the statute will not be permitted, since it vitiates the limited right to recovery that the plaintiff has as a private individual, which use is not mandated by the First Amendment, nor was it intended by the Legislature.

Libel and  [***12] Slander -- Defense of Verification -- Newspersons' "Shield Law" Privilege

13. Evidentiary privileges in litigation are not favored, and even those rooted in the Constitution must give way in proper circumstances. Accordingly, at the trial of a defamation action by a private individual against newspersons, if defendants opt to rely on the newspersons' privilege of confidentiality under the "Shield Law" (Civil Rights Law, § 79-h), they will be precluded from any use of those confidential sources and information as proof of verification of the material or evidence of responsible journalism; if they choose to fully disclose their investigation, no limitation of the defense will occur.

Libel and Slander -- News Publisher -- Gross Negligence Standard

14. In Chapadeau v Utica Observer-Dispatch (38 NY2d 196), the Court of Appeals fashioned a gross negligence standard, defining actionable defamation of a private individual by the media, to balance the need for free debate against the right of the individual to be secure in his reputation, which, like the concept of malice, is a legal measure, designed to be applied in a wide range of circumstances and evaluated by the [***13] reasonable individual; these standards are not professional journalistic principles. Accordingly, in such a defamation action, affidavits of expert journalists regarding responsible publishing standards are not required on a motion for summary judgment.

 

1087 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Gershowitz v. Planning Bd. of Brookhaven


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


69 A.D.2d 460; 419 N.Y.S.2d 976; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11826



July 30, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Suffolk County, entered August 24, 1978, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, the matter is remitted to the Zoning Board of Appeals of the Town of Brookhaven for further proceedings in accordance with the opinion herein, and the declaratory judgment action is dismissed, without prejudice to renewal, in accordance with the opinion herein.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant planning board sought review of a decision from the Special Term of the Supreme Court in Suffolk County (New York), which annulled appellant's approval of petitioner junk dealer's site plan and declared the operation of an automobile shredder on petitioner's premises to be a permitted use. Appellant asserted that the trial court erred in its finding that operation of a shredder was a permitted use.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner junk dealer submitted an application to the building department for a shredder plan for automobiles but the application was disapproved.
