International Tel. & Tel. Corp. v. State Tax Com.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


70 A.D.2d 700; 416 N.Y.S.2d 387; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 12184



May 10, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner corporation initiated a tax refund action against respondent, State Tax Commission, challenging the Commission's determination that the corporation was not entitled to a refund of the use tax it paid pursuant to N.Y. Tax Law § 1110.


OVERVIEW: The corporation was headquartered in New York City and purchased three airplanes out of state. The corporation paid state use taxes on all three planes pursuant to § 1110 and parked them at a New York airport. The corporation requested a refund of the use taxes on the grounds that the use tax violated the Commerce Clause and the Equal Protection Clause and there was not a taxable event in the state. The Commission denied the application. The corporation initiated a refund action. In affirming the Commission's decision, the court found that since the corporation did not pay a sales tax upon the purchase of the planes, the use tax was properly imposed by statute. The planes were used solely for the corporation's benefit and were subject to its direction in the state, so there was taxable event. The statute did not violate the Commerce Clause or the Equal Protection Clause because the planes were not engaged in interstate commerce at the taxable moments and there was no unequalization of class that would void the tax.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's determination.

 

1107 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Cook v. Binghamton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


67 A.D.2d 469; 416 N.Y.S.2d 349; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10132



May 3, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment modified, on the law, by reversing so much thereof as declared chapter 965 of the Laws of 1977 unconstitutional as applied to plaintiffs and permanently enjoined defendants from reducing the level of payments which plaintiffs are to receive thereunder, and by declaring chapter 965 of the Laws of 1977 constitutional and, as so modified, affirmed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants, a city and a police department, appealed a decision from the Supreme Court in Broome County (New York) declaring 1977 N.Y. Laws ch. 965 unconstitutional and enjoining defendants from reducing the level of payments that plaintiff disabled firemen were entitled to recover under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 270-a.


OVERVIEW: The disabled firemen were receiving benefits under § 207-a. The benefits included their full regular salaries and free medical care until their disabilities ceased. The legislature then enacted 1977 N.Y. Laws ch. 965, which gave disabled firemen their full salaries until they reached their mandatory retirement age and then they would receive reduced retirement benefits. The firemen initiated an action against defendants alleging that ch. 965 was unconstitutional. The trial court entered judgment for the firemen, finding that ch. 965 improperly abrogated the disable fireman's rights to receive benefits and enjoined defendants from reducing the benefits. In modifying the decision, the court reversed the finding of unconstitutionality and declared the statute constitutional. The court found that ch. 965 was intended as a remedial statute to alleviate the excessive costs of N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 207-a. It therefore could be given retrospective application and did not impair vested rights. The court concluded that the terms and conditions of the disabled firemen's employment were at issue, rather than their retirement or pension benefits.


OUTCOME: The court modified the decision by reversing that portion that declared 1977 N.Y. Laws ch. 965 unconstitutional and enjoined defendants from reducing the disabled firemen's payments. The court declared the statute constitutional.


HEADNOTES

Municipal Corporations -- Firemen -- Payments to Disabled Firemen

Chapter 965 of the Laws of 1977, which amended section 207-a of the General Municipal Law by providing, inter alia, that a fireman who became disabled because of injury or illness incurred as a result of the performance of his duties is no longer entitled to receive the full amount of [***2] his regular salary or wages until his disability has ceased but shall receive instead his regular salary or wages only until he reaches his mandatory retirement age or attains the age or performs the period of service specified by applicable law for the termination of his service, is constitutional inasmuch as it was enacted as a remedial statute to alleviate what were deemed to be the excessively costly and undesirable effects of section 207-a, and, as a remedial statute, it can be given retrospective application to the extent that it does not impair vested rights; accordingly, plaintiffs, disabled firemen receiving benefits pursuant to section 207-a prior to the amendment, may be required to accept the reduced retirement benefits upon their reaching retirement age or the termination of their service inasmuch as the Legislature, in providing for the retirement or termination from service of disabled firemen upon the happening of certain specified events and for the consequent reduction in the payments which they as retirees will receive, was not impairing any vested right of said firemen, whether contractual or otherwise, but rather was merely altering the terms and conditions of [***3] the firemen's employment, an action which was clearly within its power.

 

1108 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Society for Ethical Culture v. Spatt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


68 A.D.2d 112; 416 N.Y.S.2d 246; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10527



May 3, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, New York, entered on January 15, 1976, reversed, on the law, without costs and without disbursements, the judgment vacated and the designation of petitioner's Meeting House as a New York City landmark declared valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant Landmarks Preservation Commission challenged the order of the Supreme Court, New York County (New York), which permanently enjoined it from interfering with respondent society's use of its building and the land upon which it was situated.


OVERVIEW: The society challenged the landmark designation applied by the commission to one of its buildings. The trial court annulled the designation on the basis that the restrictions flowing from the landmark designation interfered with the religious, educational, and charitable purposes of the society. The commission appealed and the court reversed. The court observed that landmark regulation inevitably had a restricting or adverse effect on property, charitable or otherwise. The court also observed that, although religious structures enjoyed a constitutionally protected status that curtailed the permissible extent of governmental regulation, the power of regulation was not eliminated. The court found that the landmark designation did not interfere with the society's use of the building or with the society's charitable or religious activities. The court noted that the landmark designation did pose the possibility of future restrictions regarding any alteration or demolition of the building but that any future "hardship" was speculative and would have to be judged on the basis of the society's needs at that time.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court, annulling the commission's designation of the society's building as a landmark, was reversed and the designation was declared valid.


HEADNOTES

Administrative Law -- Judicial Review of Administrative Action -- Substantial Evidence

1. Appellate courts may not upset the determination of an administrative tribunal, where a hearing has been held, if there is substantial evidence to support the finding; the courts cannot interfere unless there is no rational basis for the exercise of discretion or the action complained of is arbitrary and capricious.

Constitutional Law -- Landmarks Preservation Law

2. There was a rational basis for the designation of the Meeting House of the Society for Ethical Culture in New York City as a landmark since it was found [***2] that the building was a rare, fine and irreplaceable example of art nouveau architecture and that it had served as the meeting house of the society since 1910, a period well over half of the society's existence, and maintenance of the meeting house as a landmark would not seriously interfere with the society carrying out its charitable purpose since the society's proposals for use of the property were to develop commercially the site for financial gain; although any owner is free to develop his property, all property owners, commercial or charitable, are subject to governmental land use regulation, including regulation which may deprive the owner of the full exploitation value of his property, and the fact that an ordinance deprives property of its most beneficial use does not render it unconstitutional. Although the society's claim of hardship is not premature to the extent that the designation impairs the value of the property, the designation does not constitute an undue interference with the free exercise of religion in violation of the First Amendment of the United States Constitution since a large part of the contemplated use is wholly unrelated to the exercise of religion,  [***3] except for the tangential benefit of raising revenue through development.

 

1109 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Maplecrest Sausage Co. v. Tully


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


67 A.D.2d 329; 415 N.Y.S.2d 311; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10113



April 19, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, and petition dismissed, without [***2] costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On transfer from the Supreme Court at Special Term in Albany County (New York), petitioner taxpayer challenged an assessment of additional sales and use tax on its hot dog manufacture by respondent, President of the New York State Tax Commission. The taxpayer argued that the assessment was untimely, the hot dog casings were exempt from taxation, there was no taxable event in the state, and that the tax was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayer manufactured hot dogs. The casings of the hot dogs were removed from the finished product and disposed of prior to their shipment for retail sale. The taxpayer received a notice of determination and demand for payment of an additional sales and use tax assessment and filed an action to review the determination. The Commission sustained the assessment. The taxpayer appealed, and the lower court transferred the proceeding to the court. The court sustained the assessment, holding that the assessment was not time barred under N.Y. Tax Law § 1147 because the uncontroverted facts supported the Commission's finding that the assessment was timely. The Commission was justified in concluding that the hot dog casings did not constitute cartons for the purpose of the exemptions in N.Y. Tax Law §§ 1115(a)(19), 1118(4). The Commission correctly determined that there was a taxable event in the state because the delivery truck was used solely for the taxpayer's benefit and was subject to its direction and control, and it travelled at least 300 miles per week on New York State roads. New York's sales and use tax was not an unconstitutional burden on interstate commerce.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's assessment of additional sales and use tax on the taxpayer.


HEADNOTES

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes -- Timeliness of Assessment of Additional Taxes

1. There was substantial evidence to support a finding that an assessment of additional sales and use taxes was timely; petitioner had signed an agreement extending the period of limitations to December 20, 1975 and a notice of taxes due dated December 18, 1975 was sent to petitioner; assuming that no assessment within the meaning of subdivision (b) of section 1147 of the Tax Law could have been made until the notice was given, the determinative date pursuant to subdivision (a) of section 1147 is the date of mailing and not the date of receipt, the notice assertedly not having been received until substantially after December 18.

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes

2. Casings used by petitioner in its manufacture of hot dogs, which casings are removed from the finished product and disposed of prior to their shipment for retail sale, do not constitute cartons, containers and wrapping and packing material actually transferred by petitioner to the purchaser (Tax Law, § 1115, subd [a],par [19]) or property converted into a component part of petitioner's product (§ 1118, subd [***3] [4]) and, therefore, the purchase of said casings is not exempt from sales and use taxes.

Taxation -- Sales and Use Taxes

3. A sales and use tax was properly imposed on the lease of a truck owned by one of petitioner's employees which truck was used exclusively for the transportation of petitioner's products to and from its processing plant in New York; the truck is used solely for petitioner's benefit and is subject to its direction and control. Accordingly, a finding that there has been a taxable event in New York State must be sustained.

Constitutional Law -- Interstate Commerce

4. New York's sales and use taxes are not an unconstitutional burden on interstate commerce and since the Tax Law allows reciprocal credit for taxes paid in other States, any possibility of multiple State taxation has been eliminated.

 

1110 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Fairbank Farms, Inc. v. Kasza


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


69 A.D.2d 1001; 416 N.Y.S.2d 141; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11780



April 13, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, state sales tax examiners, sought review of the judgment of the Erie Supreme Court (New York), which prohibited them from determining that respondent corporation was subject to assessment of sales tax arising from certain transactions. The trial court also prohibited the examiners from taking any departmental action in furtherance of their determination that the sales tax was due.


OVERVIEW: Respondent accountant, who worked for the corporation, inquired by letter to the Instructions and Interpretations Unit of the New York State Department of Taxation and Finance as to the taxability of an accounting method proposed by the corporation. The Unit replied that the method would not result in additional sales tax liability. Therefore, the corporation implemented the method. The examiners then proposed to assess an additional sales tax, and a hearing officer upheld the proposed assessment. The corporation and the accountant filed the N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding. The examiners contended that the corporation and accountant failed to exhaust their administrative remedies under N.Y. Tax Law §§ 1138, 1140. On appeal, the court agreed. The corporation and accountant had to comply with the method of review found in N.Y. Tax Law because they were not challenging the taxing authority's jurisdiction on the ground that the statute was unconstitutional or inapplicable. Therefore, because no final determination was reached by the Tax Commission, the 90-day period in which the corporation and accountant had to apply for a hearing under N.Y. Tax Law § 1138 had not begun to run.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment, which prohibited the examiners from determining that the corporation was subject to assessment of sales tax and from taking any departmental action in furtherance of that proposed determination that the sales tax was due. The court then dismissed the petition.

 

1111 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Harding v. Melton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


67 A.D.2d 242; 415 N.Y.S.2d 286; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10099



April 12, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, with costs, and judgment directed to be entered in favor of the appellants declaring that subdivision 4-a of section 510 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law is constitutional and that form MV-1160 is not unconstitutional or illegal. Settle order on notice.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles of the State of New York, challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Albany County (New York), which declared N.Y. Veh. & Traf. Law § 510(4-a) and form MV-1160 to be unconstitutional, and vacated the order of the Commissioner suspending the driver's license of petitioner licensee.


OVERVIEW: The Department of Motor Vehicles issued a notice to the licensee that his license was being suspended, effective 30 days from the date of the notice, for his failure to answer summonses for traffic violations. On appeal, the court reversed and directed entry of a judgment declaring that § 510(4-a) was constitutional and that form MV-1160 was not unconstitutional or illegal. Section 510(4-a) was not unconstitutionally vague as to a definite date for suspension or as to proper notice because it expressly provided that there must be a minimum period of 30 days from the date of the notice of suspension, was expressly limited to last no longer than the failure of a licensee to appear after such notice was given, and expressly required that notice to the licensee be given. Form MV-1160 was not a rule which had to be filed with the Secretary of State and it was not unconstitutionally vague because the department was empowered to reserve the right to take whatever action it was authorized to take upon a review of the licensee's record. The lack of a pre-suspension hearing did not violate the licensee's due process rights.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court, which was in favor of the licensee.


HEADNOTES

Declaratory Judgments -- When Remedy Appropriate

1. Where petitioner challenges the suspension of his driver's license pursuant to subdivision 4-a of section 510 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law and alleges that the statute is unconstitutionally vague in a proceeding pursuant to CPLR article 78, the appropriate procedure is to convert [***4] the matter to a declaratory judgment action and meet the constitutional issues.

Motor Vehicles -- Revocation or Suspension of Operator's License

2. Subdivision 4-a of section 510 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, which provides that the Commissioner of Motor Vehicles may suspend the driver's license of a person who has failed to appear within three months of the return date or new subsequent adjourned date pursuant to an appearance ticket, pending receipt of notice that the person has appeared and that the suspension shall take effect no less than 30 days from the day upon which notice thereof is sent to the person, is not unconstitutionally vague as to a definite date for suspension or as to proper notice, since it expressly provides that there must be a minimum period of 30 days from the date of the notice of suspension, is expressly limited to last no longer than the failure of a licensee to appear after such notice is given, and expressly requires that notice to the licensee be given; additionally, the form used by the Department of Motor Vehicles to notify licensees of suspension is not a rule which must be filed with the Secretray of State since the statute expressly [***5] requires that notice be given to motorists and the form is nothing more or less than the transmittal of notice, and is not unconstitutionally vague in that it provides that it will become effective 30 days from the date of the notice unless there is notification from the court that the summons has been answered or indication that other action is necessary, since the Department of Motor Vehicles is empowered to reserve the right to take whatever action it might be authorized to take upon a review of the licensee's record.

Motor Vehicles -- Revocation or Suspension of Operator's License -- Presuspension Hearing

3. Where a driver's license is suspended pursuant to subdivision 4-a of section 510 of the Vehicle and Traffic Law, the lack of a presuspension hearing does not violate the licensee's due process rights, since the State's interest is in keeping reckless drivers off the road and under such circumstances, the available review pursuant to CPLR article 78 is sufficient protection.

 

1112 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Economico v. Pelham


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


67 A.D.2d 272; 415 N.Y.S.2d 239; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10104



April 9, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Westchester County entered March 27, 1978, reversed, on the law, with $ 50 costs and disbursements, and proceeding dismissed on the merits. Cross appeal dismissed as academic, without costs or disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employee filed an action against respondent employer for unlawful dismissal in violation of a collective bargaining agreement and the due process requirements of the civil service law. The Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), declared that the employee's dismissal was null and void, but failed to direct that he receive full compensation for the period of his improper dismissal. Both parties filed cross-appeals of the decision.


OVERVIEW: An employee was placed on sick leave, with pay, after suffering injuries in an automobile accident not related to his employment. He was ordered to report back to work but he refused to comply, claiming that he was still physically unfit for duty. The employee was terminated by a city resolution predicated upon his continuing non-service connected disability. The employee contended that he had been denied due process in that he had not been afforded a hearing prior to his dismissal and, that he was entitled to unlimited sick leave under a collective bargaining agreement. The trial court ruled that the employee had been improperly dismissed. On appeal, the court reversed the decision because the employer was not required to provide a judgmental ruling in absence of any claim by the employee that he was not in fact incapacitated. The court determined that the employer's resolution was purely an administrative determination and was neither a judicial nor quasi-judicial decision requiring due process. The court also rejected the employee's claim that he was entitled to unlimited sick leave because the collective bargaining agreement was in direct conflict with public policy.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment in favor of the employee and dismissed the employer's cross appeal.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Dismissal -- Nonservice Related Disability

1. It is not a denial of due process for a village to dismiss a petitioner pursuant to section 73 of the Civil Service Law, without a hearing, after he had been continuously absent from his position for a period in excess of 18 months as a result of a nonservice related disability in that the full panoply of due process protection mandating a pretermination hearing does not apply since the village made a [***2] purely administrative determination, petitioner making no claim that he was not absent from duty for more than one year because of a nonservice connected disability (Civil Service Law, § 73), and the private interest affected by the governmental action, i.e., petitioner's job, does not mandate a hearing under circumstances where it would be an exercise in futility, there existing no question of fact requiring determination.

Civil Service -- Dismissal -- Nonservice Related Disability

2. The interpretation of a provision in a collective bargaining agreement as entitling a petitioner to unlimited sick leave with pay is in direct conflict with decisional law and public policy, and, therefore, does not prevent his dismissal by a village pursuant to section 73 of the Civil Service Law, under circumstances where petitioner had been continuously absent from his position for a period in excess of 18 months as a result of a nonservice related disability.

 

1113 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Barrett v. Wojtowicz


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


66 A.D.2d 604; 414 N.Y.S.2d 350; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10059



March 12, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Kings County, dated May 17, 1978, affirmed, with $ 50 costs and disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant convict sought review of an order by the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which denied defendant's motion to dismiss an action filed by plaintiff victim alleging assault and false imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: An individual was one of several people who was held hostage. The perpetrator was subsequently arrested and convicted for armed bank robbery. The incident was made into a movie. Several years later the victim filed an action seeking damages for assault and false imprisonment and the convict moved to have the matter dismissed as time barred pursuant to N.Y.C.P.L.R. 215. The trial court denied the motion and the convict sought review. The court determined that the one year statute of limitations had been extended from one year from the date of the crime to five years from the date an escrow account was established under N.Y. Exec. Law § 632-A. Therefore although the action was filed five years and five months after the crime, it was filed only one month after payment was made to the convict for his rights to the movie into an escrow account, the action filed by the victim was timely as to funds in the account. The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the denial of defendant's motion to dismiss.


HEADNOTES

Limitation of Actions -- Distribution of Moneys Received as Result of Commission of Crime

1. Section 632-a of the Executive Law (L 1977, ch 823, eff Aug. 11, 1977), which provided that the State Crime Victims Compensation Board was to hold in an escrow account all moneys received or contracted for by anyone accused of a crime who sells to the media his memoirs or expression of thoughts for the purpose of dramatic re-enactment of the alleged crime, that the board must pay over such moneys to a victim of the crime in question provided that the perpetrator is eventually convicted and the victim brings a civil action within five years of the date of the crime and recovers a money judgment against the perpetrator, and that the five-year period would [***2] not begin to run until the escrow account had been established, and which was amended (L 1978, ch 417, eff Sept. 1, 1978) to provide that the victim must bring a civil action within five years of the date of the establishment of the escrow account, does not revive a civil cause of action for assault or false imprisonment otherwise barred by the one-year limitation period of CPLR 215, but rather creates a new and independent cause of action; accordingly, in an action for assault and false imprisonment brought by a hostage during a bank robbery subsequently dramatized in the movie "Dog Day Afternoon", in January, 1978, five years and five months after the date the crime was committed, which would otherwise be time-barred for not having been brought within the one-year limitation period specified in CPLR 215, a motion to dismiss was properly denied since assuming, arguendo, that section 632-a as originally enacted barred the action at the time of its inception, plaintiff should nevertheless be permitted to proceed because of the expanded limitation period provided by the amendment, which expansion is constitutional inasmuch as the circumstances are exceptional and are such as [***3] to satisfy the court that serious injustice would result to the plaintiff, not guilty of any fault, if the intention of the Legislature were not effectuated.

Civil Rights -- Distribution of Moneys Received as Result of Commission of Crime

2. In an action pursuant to section 632-a of the Executive Law, which provides that the State Crime Victims Compensation Board is to hold in an escrow account all moneys received or contracted for by anyone accused of a crime who sells to the media his memoirs or expression of thoughts for the purpose of dramatic re-enactment of the alleged crime and that the board must pay over such moneys to a victim of the crime in question provided that the perpetrator is eventually convicted and the victim brings a civil action within five years of the date of the establishment of the escrow account and recovers a money judgment against the perpetrator, any judgment that may be recovered by a plaintiff should be deemed one in rem and be limited to a recovery of the pro rata amount which is found to be payable to him from the escrow account held by the board for the benefit of all the victims of a particular crime and such judgment should not be [***4] deemed a judgment in personam against any other assets of the perpetrator of the crime.

 

1114 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Sarrds, Inc. v. White Plains


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


68 A.D.2d 905; 414 N.Y.S.2d 209; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11158



March 12, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to declare the sign ordinance of defendant City of White Plains invalid, the City appealed an order from the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), which denied the City's cross motion to dismiss the complaint.


OVERVIEW: The instant suit involved plaintiff's existing sign that had a permit for many years. Plaintiff citizen sued the City, claiming that the City's sign ordinance was an unreasonable exercise of the police power and served to confiscate its property without just compensation, in violation of constitutional strictures. In addition, plaintiff claimed that the establishment of a Civic Art Commission was an unconstitutional delegation of powers. The City filed a motion to dismiss the complaint, but the supreme court denied it. On appeal, the court modified, by adding an exception to plaintiff's fifth cause of action, and as so modified, affirmed. The court found that plaintiff's fifth cause of action asserted in the complaint had been raised prematurely. Plaintiff had not been called upon to submit an application for a permit to the Civic Art Commission, which was established pursuant to the sign ordinance in question. Because the amortization period of three years provided for in the ordinance could not be extended, the court found that plaintiff was entitled to an immediate hearing as to whether the amortization period provided in the ordinance was unreasonable as applied.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order, on the law, and as so modified, affirmed, without costs or disbursements.

 

1115 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Kupferman v. New York State Board of Social Welfare


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


66 A.D.2d 540; 414 N.Y.S.2d 757; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10053



March 8, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, insofar as it granted plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment to the extent of declaring so much of chapter 431 of the Laws of 1977 as restricts the use of income disregard funds to be invalid, reversed, on the law, without costs; defendants' cross motion for summary judgment granted, and judgment directed to be entered in favor of defendants declaring chapter 431 of the Laws of 1977 to be valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, New York State Board of Social Welfare, challenged a decision from the Supreme Court in Albany (New York), which granted summary judgment in favor of appellee, a private proprietary home for adults (PPHA) on its claim to declare a new section of the Social Services Law, N.Y. Soc. Serv. § 131-o, concerning Supplemental Security Income (SSI) benefits, to be invalid as it conflicted with federal law.


OVERVIEW: The contested statute established "personal allowance accounts" for SSI recipients receiving residential or family care. The purpose of the personal allowance was to enable residents of facilities such as PPHA's to pay for personal items such as clothing and incidentals not provided by the home. The State contended that there was no federal statute or regulation precluding the State from restricting the use of "income disregard" funds to personal allowance accounts. The court agreed. It found that under the federal regulation, 20 C.F.R. § 416.110(c), payments were made under conditions as protective of people's dignity as possible and no restrictions, implied or otherwise, were placed on how recipients spent the federal payments. It also found no federal enabling statute authorizing the state to allocate the funds was required. Finally, it found that the statute did not unconstitutionally impair the obligation of contracts between the PPHA and its residents as payment level was defined by the federal SSI statute and not the State statute.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision granting summary judgment to the PPHA. The court found the statute to be lawfully enacted and valid and granted the State's cross-motion for summary judgment.


HEADNOTES

Social Services -- Personal Allowance Accounts

1. Section 131-o of the Social Services Law, which provides personal allowance accounts for SSI recipients receiving family care or residential care (Social Services Law, § 209, subd 3) and sets forth the amount of the recipient's income to be disregarded in determining eligibility for SSI benefits (Social Services Law, § 209, subd 5; US Code, tit [***2] 42, § 1382a, subd [b]), does not unconstitutionally restrict the use of income disregard funds as between a private proprietary home for adults (PPHA) and the recipients of SSI benefits for whom the PPHA provides board, lodging and certain personal services, the recipients having contracted to pay their SSI payment level if unable to pay the private rate established by the home, in that there is no Federal statute or regulation precluding the State from restricting the use of income disregard funds to personal allowance accounts and section 131-o furthers the objective of maintaining a Federally established minimum standard of living and protecting people's dignity (20 CFR 416.110 [c]) by enabling residents of PPHA's to pay for personal items such as clothing, transportation, and other incidentals not provided by the home.

Social Services -- Personal Allowance Accounts

2. Section 131-o of the Social Services Law, which provides personal allowance accounts for SSI recipients receiving family care or residential care (Social Services Law, § 209, subd 3) and sets forth the amount of the recipient's income to be disregarded in determining eligibility for SSI benefits [***3] (Social Services Law, § 209, subd 5; US Code, tit 42, § 1382a, subd [b]), does not unconstitutionally impair the obligations of the contracts between a private proprietary home for adults (PPHA) and the recipients of SSI benefits for whom the PPHA provides board, lodging and certain personal services, the recipients having contracted to pay their SSI payment level if unable to pay the private rate established by the home, as the statute is a valid exercise of the police power of the State over the PPHA industry to secure the general welfare of the aged and the allocation of the income disregard of SSI recipients to their personal allowance furthers that goal by attempting to alleviate the plight of SSI recipients who in the past have indorsed their entire checks over to the proprietors of homes thereby precluding the recipients from having any money left over for personal expenditures; furthermore, the SSI payment level is not defined in PPHA's contracts with its residents but rather by Federal statute and since the State has the power to allocate the income disregard to a personal allowance account, the statute does not impair the PPHA's contracts.

 

1116 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Allcity Ins. Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


66 A.D.2d 531; 413 N.Y.S.2d 929; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10052



March 1, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order, Supreme Court, New York County, entered on May 23, 1978, unanimously affirmed, without costs and without disbursements.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants challenged an order from the Supreme Court New York County (New York) ,which granted the application of the Superintendent of Insurance, as the rehabilitator of respondent insurance company, to approve and confirm his recommendation for disallowance of appellants' claims to the extent of referring them to a referee.


OVERVIEW: Appellants filed claims against respondent insurer pursuant to the uninsured motorist endorsement of respondent's policy. The claims were disallowed by the New York Superintendent of Insurance who had been appointed as rehabilitator upon respondent's adjudication as insolvent. Appellants cross-moved for an order that directed the rehabilitator to proceed to arbitrate their claims as required by the uninsured motorist endorsement. A referee was directed to hear and report on the disallowed claims and appellants challenged the decision. The court affirmed the lower court's decision to send the disallowed claims to the referee instead of requesting the claims be placed before an arbitrator. The court held that the Legislature was entitled to replace the right of a forum, contractually derived, with a statutory remedy.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's decision when it found that the lower court had the power to require that the dispute between appellant insureds and respondent insolvent insurer were to be resolved by the court in rehabilitation proceedings instead of arbitration, as provided in an endorsement.


HEADNOTES

Insurance -- Rehabilitation of Insurer -- Power of Court to Resolve Disputes

1. A court has the power to require that all disputes between an insured and insurer under the New York Automobile Accident Indemnification Endorsement issued by an insurer, now insolvent, be resolved by the court in rehabilitation proceedings instead of arbitration, as provided in the endorsement, since during rehabilitation, which is a design of the Legislature permitting the Superintendent [***3] of Insurance to take possession of the property of a domestic insurer and to conduct its business when it becomes insolvent (Insurance Law, §§ 511, 512, subd 1), the superintendent must obtain permission from the court to perform such functions as are necessary for the exercise of his duties, and there is no indication in the statute that the Legislature intended to have rehabilitation effected in any forum but a court of law; it has been said that the provisions of the Insurance Law relating to liquidation, another delinquency program envisioned by article 16 of the Insurance Law, are exclusive in their operation and furnish a complete procedure for the protection of the rights of all parties interested. The fact that a substitute forum for the enforcement of claims under the uninsured motorist endorsement has been provided is constitutionally permissible since common-law actions may be replaced by statutory remedies.

Statutes -- Construction

2. When interpreting a statute, a court should look to the enactment as a whole, to discern the purpose and policy underlying the statute, and should give the words a meaning, which serves, rather than defeats, the ends intended [***4] by the Legislature.

Statutes -- Presumption of Constitutionality

3. Every legislative enactment is deemed constitutional until its challengers have satisfied a court to the contrary, and there is generally a strong presumption that the Legislature has investigated and found the existence of a situation showing or indicating the need for or desirability of the legislation.

Actions -- Common-Law Actions -- Replacement with Statutory Remedies

4. Common-law actions may be replaced by statutory remedies.

 

1117 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Briggins


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


67 A.D.2d 1004; 413 N.Y.S.2d 741; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10807



February 26, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the County Court, Suffolk County (New York), which convicted him of two counts of criminal possession of a forged instrument in the second degree.


OVERVIEW: After a jury trial, defendant was convicted of two counts of criminal possession of a forged instrument in the second degree. On appeal, he claimed that he was denied a fair trial because his jury selection procedure was unconstitutional. But the court disagreed holding that the local jury selection procedure that excluded persons not possessing a driver's license from the panel was not unconstitutional. The court further held that the Sixth and Fourteenth Amendments to the Federal Constitution did not preclude the states from prescribing relevant qualifications for their jurors. The court also held that defendant failed to show that the exclusion of non-driving citizens disproportionately affected members of a particular class violating the "fair-cross-section" requirement.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed an order from the trial court, which convicted defendant of two counts of criminal possession of a forged instrument in the second degree.

 

1118 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Boynton


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


67 A.D.2d 982; 413 N.Y.S.2d 431; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10777



February 20, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The state appealed an order of the Supreme Court of Queens County (New York), which, after accepting a verdict of guilty on one count of an indictment, dismissed the remaining count against defendant because the jury was hopelessly deadlocked.


OVERVIEW: After deliberating, the jury returned a guilty verdict on the count of endangering a child, but was hopelessly deadlocked on the charge of rape. The court accepted the guilty verdict and dismissed the remaining charge stating on the record that it was loath to subject the state to the expense of another trial. On appeal by the state, the court reversed the dismissal, reinstated the charge, and ordered a new trial. The court held that the trial court was permitted to dismiss the charge only if it found that the state did not prove its case, but it could not decide to save the state the expense of a new trial. Further, the court held that the trial court should have declared a mistrial rather than dismissing the charge. Finally, the court determined that reinstatement and retrial would not have violated the Double Jeopardy Clause because there was no acquittal or a termination based on a the state's legally insufficient case.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order dismissing two counts of an indictment against defendant, reinstated the charges, and remanded the case for new trial.

 

1119 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Young v. Toia


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


66 A.D.2d 377; 413 N.Y.S.2d 530; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10023



January 25, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment unanimously modified, on the law, and, as modified, affirmed, with costs to petitioners, and matter remitted to Supreme Court, Orleans County, for further proceedings in accordance with opinion by Witmer, J.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff home relief recipients sought review of the decision of the Supreme Court at Special Term, Orleans County (New York), which denied their application for counsel fees pursuant to 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 in their 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 action against defendant Commissioner of the New York State Department of Social Services (commissioner).


OVERVIEW: The home relief recipients brought an action under § 1983 seeking declaratory judgment that a state law was invalid as violative of the minimum wage provisions of N.Y. Const. art. I, § 17 because it required employable home relief recipients to work an average of three full working days per week regardless of the monthly benefits which they received, and that it was violative of the equal protection and due process clauses of the United States Constitution. In addition they sought counsel fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The trial court granted their requested relief but denied their request for counsel fees. On appeal, the court modified the judgment and remitted the cause. The court held that pursuant to the Civil Rights Attorney's Fees Awards Act of 1976, which amended § 1988, in any action to enforce a provision of 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983, a trial court, in its discretion, could allow the prevailing party reasonable counsel fees. The court reversed the paragraph in the order which denied counsel fees on the grounds that 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 did not apply to the action.


OUTCOME: The court modified the order and remitted the matter for the trial court to exercise its discretion with respect to the application for counsel fees by the home relief recipients.


HEADNOTES

Civil Rights -- Counsel Fees

In order to facilitate the enforcement of the rights of citizens under section 1983 of title 42 of the United States Code, counsel fees incurred in such enforcement may be recovered from the defendant in the sound discretion of the court pursuant to section 1988 of title 42 of the United States Code and it is immaterial, with respect to the issue of attorney's fees, whether the court bases its decision on a finding that a State law was violated as opposed to a violation of the Federal statute which grants substantially the same rights.

 

1120 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. Shang


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


66 A.D.2d 6; 412 N.Y.S.2d 629; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9984



January 22, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment of the Supreme Court, Nassau County, entered March 23, 1978, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, and proceeding remitted to Special Term for further proceedings in accordance herewith.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, an employable home relief recipient, challenged the judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which, in a proceeding pursuant to N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78, dismissed the recipient's petition to compel respondents, the state and the county department of social services, to reduce a mortgage lien on the recipient's mortgage. The recipient had filed an action under N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 164.


OVERVIEW: The recipient's wife received Supplemental Security Income. Under N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 106, the county agency obtained a mortgage lien on their home, and they agreed to pay for the amount expended to relieve the mortgage. The recipient began to work on public works projects assigned by the county agency under N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 164 for the number of days necessary to earn the amount of the debt. Then, he applied for a reduction of the lien by the amount of payment credits earned on the projects. The county agency refused a reduction despite the state agency's advice to make a reduction. The recipient filed an action under N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 to compel the state and the county agencies to make the reduction. On appeal, the court reversed the trial court's judgment of dismissal, remitted to the trial court, and held that: (1) N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 106 was intended to preserve the nonliquid asset of a public assistance recipient and to provide relief advantageous to the public welfare; (2) N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 164 was intended to require such recipient to perform public works projects for earnings; and (3) the county agency was required to credit the recipient's earnings.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's judgment of dismissal of the homeowner's action against the state and the county agencies and remitted to the trial court to determine the amount earned by the recipient on the public works project and to direct the state and the county agencies to reduce the lien on recipient's home by that amount.


HEADNOTES

Social Services -- Work Relief -- Credit against Mortgage Lien

Petitioner, who was assigned to work on a public works project as an employable recipient of home relief in accordance with the provisions of section 164 of the Social Services Law, is entitled to a reduction of the mortgage lien held on his house by the County Department of Social Services in the amount of the payment credits he earned through his employment on the public works project, as it was the intent of the Legislature that an employable person receiving home relief would be required to perform work assigned [***2] to him by the social services agency furnishing such relief, but that the amount he received for his work should be treated as his earnings or wages; the failure to credit such earnings against the home relief received by petitioner allows the county to receive not only what it paid in home relief, but also the value of petitioner's labors gratis.

 

1121 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rinefierd v. Blum


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


66 A.D.2d 351; 412 N.Y.S.2d 526; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10019



January 19, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Determination unanimously confirmed without costs and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant applicant for medical assistance for his elderly father sought review of a determination by appellee state department of social services (New York) to affirm the denial of the application. The state claimed that the father transferred assets at a time when he had a medical need in order to qualify for medical assistance.


OVERVIEW: A son applied for medical benefits on behalf of his elderly father. The local social services agency denied the application, and the state department of social services affirmed the denial. The application was denied because the state believed that the applicant's father transferred assets when he had a medical need in order to qualify for medical assistance. The applicant sought judicial review. On review, the court found sufficient proof to substantiate that the applicant's father did transfer assets in order to qualify for medical assistance. The court also considered but rejected the applicant's claim that the applicable statute. N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 366 (1)(e) violated the Supremacy Clause and was unconstitutional. The court found that § 366 (1)(e) did not conflict with federal statutes and regulations. The court noted that the state statute denied assistance only when a transfer of funds or property was made with sham or spurious intent. The court recognized the interest of the state in protecting its resources from fraudulent utilization.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed that determination by the state to deny the application for medical assistance.


HEADNOTES

Social Services -- Transfer of Property to Qualify for Assistance

An application for medical assistance on behalf of petitioner's 87-year-old father was properly denied on the ground that the latter had transferred assets at a time when he had a medical need in order to qualify for medical assistance where the application was made over one year after petitioner's father sold his home and distributed the proceeds to his sons, the sale having taken place nine months after petitioner's father entered a nursing home, since section 366 (subd 1, par [e]) of the [***2] Social Services Law provided, at the time the application for assistance was made, that medical assistance shall be given to a person requiring it and who has not made a voluntary transfer of property for the purpose of qualifying for such assistance, a voluntary transfer within one year of the date of the application being presumed to have been made for the purpose of qualifying for assistance; although the one-year presumption could not be relied upon in this case because there was no proof that the transfer was made less than one year prior to the application for assistance, there was sufficient proof that the transfer was made for the purpose of qualifying for assistance. There is no violation of Federal law, since although Federal rules provide that only those resources actually available to an applicant are to be considered in determining eligibility, and State transfer-of-assets statutes which assume assets are available to recipients when in fact such assets are not available are unconstitutional, the New York statute denies assistance only where the transfer is made for the purpose of qualifying for medical assistance, i.e., a sham or spurious transfer or one made with fraudulent [***3] intent, unlike statutes of other States which have been held invalid since they disqualified an applicant solely because of a transfer.

 

1122 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


John R. Dudley Constr., Inc. v. Drott Mfg. Co.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


66 A.D.2d 368; 412 N.Y.S.2d 512; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10022



January 19, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Order unanimously affirmed, with costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff consumer sought damages in negligence and strict products liability against defendants, a manufacturer, seller, and servicer. The consumer alleged that the bolts on his used crane suddenly fractured heavily damaging the crane alone. The manufacturer, seller, and servicer appealed an order from the Supreme Court of Onondaga County (New York), which denied their motions for summary judgment.


OVERVIEW: The court held that the manufacturer and seller owed a duty to the consumer under the doctrine of strict products liability not to place into the stream of commerce a crane containing defective bolts the failure of which would create a danger of physical injury resulting to consumer's property extrinsic to the crane or to the crane itself. The damages were not in the loss of the benefit of the consumer's bargain but in the damages to the crane proximately caused by the defective bolts. Cases relied upon by the manufacturer, seller, and servicer were inapplicable because they did not involve physical damages resulting from a dangerous defect in a product. The disclaimer of warranty and "as is" clauses in the purchase contract did not benefit the manufacturer, seller, and servicer because it was conceded that there was no privity with the manufacturer or the servicer. Moreover, there was no showing that these clauses were intended to exclude a claim of physical damage to the product under the strict products liability theory. Therefore, summary judgment was properly denied.


OUTCOME: The order denying summary judgment to the manufacturer, seller, and servicer was affirmed.


HEADNOTES

Products Liability -- Injuries to Property

1. Strict products liability is a proper remedy for redress of injuries to property caused by defective manufacture.

Products Liability -- Damage to Product

2. A cause of action based on strict products liability against the manufacturer of a crane may stand where certain allegedly defective turntable bolts which [***3] connected the crane superstructure to the undercarriage broke while the crane was being operated and the only damage was to the crane itself, since there is no logical reason why recovery should be allowed for injuries to property beyond the limits of the crane, assuming there had been some, and disallowed for damages for the parts of the crane damaged or destroyed when it collapsed; in either case the damages could be said to have resulted from the same tortious conduct by defendant in supplying a defective crane, and said defendant, in manufacturing and marketing the crane, owed a duty to plaintiff, the purchaser of the crane, under the doctrine of strict products liability as defined in Codling v Paglia (32 NY2d 330), not to place into the stream of commerce a crane containing defective bolts, the failure of which would create a danger of physical injury resulting to plaintiff's property whether it be injury to property extrinsic to the crane or to portions of the crane itself consequentially damaged as a result of the bolts' failure.

Products Liability -- Nature of Action

3. An action for strict products liability seeks to provide a remedy for an individual injured [***4] because of another's violation of an obligation imposed not by contract, but by law, and the legal duty stems from an awareness that in today's advanced technological society it is in the public interest that an increased responsibility be cast upon the manufacturer, who stands in a superior position to recognize and cure defects, for improper conduct in the placement of finished products into the channels of commerce.

Products Liability -- Nature of Action

4. For causes of action arising prior to the effective date of CPLR 1411, which adopted the doctrine of comparative negligence in New York, i.e., prior to September 1, 1975, a manufacturer is liable for placing a defective product into the stream of commerce to any person injured or damaged if the defect was a substantial factor in bringing about his injury or damages, provided: (1) that at the time of the occurrence the product is being used for the purpose and in the manner normally intended, (2) that if the person injured or damaged is himself the user of the product he would not by the exercise of reasonable care have both discovered the defect and perceived its danger, and (3) that by the exercise of reasonable [***5] care the person injured or damaged would not otherwise have averted his injury or damages.

 

1123 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. King v. New York State Board of Parole


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


65 A.D.2d 465; 412 N.Y.S.2d 138; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 9980



January 9, 1979 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, Bronx County, entered on July 31, 1978, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the judgment of the Supreme Court in Bronx County, (New York), which found evidence concerning petitioner's heroin possession was properly admitted at his parole revocation hearing and sustained petitioner's application for a writ of habeas corpus only to the extent of vacating the hearing and ordering production of items for which petitioner sought discovery.


OVERVIEW: While on parole for another crime, defendant was arrested for possession of heroin. However, the charge was dismissed because the heroin had been illegally seized. Subsequently, defendant's parole was revoked based in part on his admission to his parole officer that he had been in possession of heroin at the time of his arrest. Defendant argued that his statement to his parole officer was erroneously admitted at the hearing because the heroin had been illegally seized. The court held that the statement was sufficiently distinguishable from the illegal seizure and, as such, was admissible in the parole revocation hearing under the doctrine of attenuation. Additionally, the court reasoned that because the parole revocation hearing was not considered a criminal proceeding, the exclusionary standards applicable in a criminal trial did not apply to defendant's case at issue.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court, which found evidence concerning petitioner's heroin possession was properly admitted at parole revocation hearing, was affirmed because petitioner's statement to his parole officer concerning his heroin possession was admissible at his parole revocation hearing.


HEADNOTES

Parole -- Parole Revocation Hearing -- Admission of Criminal Activity

1. A parolee's admission to his parole officer that he possessed heroin is admissible at a parole revocation hearing, where the criminal charges underlying the admission were ultimately dismissed since the heroin was illegally seized, because the evidence adduced by the parole officer was gained by means sufficiently distinguishable from the initial illegality, and it was purged of the primary taint and is therefore admissible against the parolee; additionally, there would be no deterrent against improper police conduct were the statement excluded from the parole revocation hearing, and the exclusionary rule was never intended to [***3] proscribe the use of illegally seized evidence in all proceedings or against all persons.

Parole -- Parole Revocation Hearing -- Nature of Hearing

2. A parole revocation hearing is not a stage of a criminal prosecution, and the standards applied to the former do not carry over to the latter; the revocation process involves a deprivation of a conditional liberty, and as such, the procedural protections afforded must be flexible in consonance with the demands of the particular situation.

Parole -- Parole Revocation Hearing -- Exclusionary Rule

3. Although the exclusionary rule has been applied to administrative hearings, it should not be applied to a parole revocation hearing where the evidence sought to be suppressed was not seized by the agents of, or for the purposes of, the agency conducting the administrative proceeding.

 

1124 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Harris


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


67 A.D.2d 665; 412 N.Y.S.2d 31; 1979 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10247



January 8, 1979 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which convicted defendant of attempted murder of a peace officer, robbery in the first degree and possession of a deadly weapon.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of attempted murder of a police officer, robbery in the first degree, and possession of a deadly weapon. He appealed his convictions. On appeal, the court considered defendant's claim that the lower court committed reversible error in refusing to instruct the jury that in order to convict the defendant of attempted murder as charged in the indictment, the People had to prove beyond a reasonable doubt that the defendant knew or had reason to know that his intended victim was a peace officer at the time that he attempted to kill him, as provided by N.Y. Penal Law §125.27 (1)(a)(i). The court noted that defense counsel preserved the issue for review. The court examined N.Y. Penal Law § 110.05, which provided in part that an attempt to commit a crime was a Class A-I felony when the crime attempted was the felony of murder of a peace officer in the course of performing his official duties. The court concluded that the deterrent purpose of the law would not be served by construing it as a strict liability statute. The statute required scienter on defendant's part and failure to charge the jury to that effect was reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the lower court on the law and ordered a new trial.

 

1125 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Bennett v. County of Nassau


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


66 A.D.2d 131; 411 N.Y.S.2d 912; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13909



December 29, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Order of the Supreme Court, Nassau County, dated February 16, 1978, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, and plaintiffs' motion for summary judgment denied; judgment is granted in favor of defendant (1) declaring (a) that persons employed by Nassau County as nonjudicial employees on March 31, 1977 were not terminated from service on that day and (b) that payment of accumulated vacation time and sick leave not transferred to the State did not become due and payable on April 1, 1977 and (2) otherwise dismissing the complaint.

Appeal from a further order of the same court, dated May 17, 1978, dismissed as academic, without costs or disbursements, in the light of the determination on the appeal from the order dated February 16, 1978.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county challenged an order of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which granted a motion by plaintiff court employees for summary judgment and an order which denied a motion by the county for renewal.


OVERVIEW: An act caused the nonjudicial employees to cease being county employees and to become state employees. The nonjudicial employees sought a judgment declaring that they had incurred a termination of service under certain county ordinances and collective bargaining agreements and were entitled to cash payment for accumulated time off that had not transferred. The lower court granted the nonjudicial employees' motion for summary judgment and held that the only issue to be determined was the amount of individual damages. The county appealed, and the court reversed the lower court's judgment, denied the motion for summary judgment, dismissed the complaint, and granted judgment in favor of the county. The court held that the annual transfer of boiler plate languages in various ordinances did not serendipitously furnish to the nonjudicial employees a legally viable claim to a windfall of entitlement to terminal benefits. No one could rationally have assumed that there was any circumstance that would trigger terminal leave payments, in which an employee could continue his services exactly as before and still claim that he was terminated for the purpose of collecting such payments.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the lower court's order on the law, without costs or disbursements, and denied the nonjudicial employees' motion for summary judgment. The court granted judgment in favor of the county, declaring that nonjudicial employees who became state employees were not terminated and that payment of vacation time and sick leave not transferred to the state did not become due and payable, and otherwise dismissing the complaint.


HEADNOTES

 [***2] Courts -- Unified Court System -- Transfer of Accumulated Leave

Plaintiffs, nonjudicial employees in the courts of Nassau County, are not entitled to receive terminal leave payments from the county for accumulated vacation and sick leave not transferred to the State when the unified court system (Judiciary Law, § 220, now § 39) went into effect, since there was only a partial shift in the source of payment from the county to the State, and the employees' service with the county could not rationally be considered to have terminated inasmuch as the employees performed exactly the same duties after unification as they did before; the employees did not incur a "termination of service" within the meaning of certain county ordinances and pursuant to parallel contracts between the county and the Civil Service Employees Association, and any claim that section 220 (subd 6, par [d]) of the Judiciary Law, by giving plaintiffs lesser terminal benefits than they would have had if court unification had not been enacted, has unconstitutionally deprived them of a vested right or has impermissibly impaired their contractual rights, must await determination at the time their services as [***3] court employees are in fact terminated, and not merely transferred from one governmental agency to another.

 

1126 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Bess v. Toia


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


66 A.D.2d 844; 411 N.Y.S.2d 651; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 14180



December 26, 1978 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother appealed a judgment of the Supreme Court, Westchester County (New York), which denied the mother's request for an attorney's fee under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 as the prevailing party in the mother's action seeking review of a determination of respondent Commissioner of the New York State Department of Social Services (commissioner) that affirmed a local agency's denial of a burial assistance grant to the mother for her deceased son.


OVERVIEW: After the commissioner affirmed a decision of a local agency to deny the mother a burial assistance grant for her deceased son, the mother filed an action seeking review of the commissioner's determination. The mother alleged violations of the Equal Protection Clause of the United States Constitution and sought damages under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1983 and an award of an attorney's fee under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988. The trial court entered judgment in favor of the mother, but denied the mother's request for damages and an attorney's fee. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying the mother's request for an attorney's fee. The court held that, although 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 allowed an award of attorney's fees to the prevailing party in a civil rights action, such an award was not appropriate in every case. The court held that the mother's action was merely an ordinary administrative proceeding under N.Y. C.P.L.R. 78, contained no bona fide civil rights claim, and was insufficient to create a substantial constitutional question. Thus, the court held that an award of attorney's fees under 42 U.S.C.S. § 1988 would have been inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that denied the mother's request for an attorney's fee as the prevailing party in the mother's action seeking review of the commissioner's determination that affirmed a local agency's denial of a burial assistance grant to the mother for her deceased son.

People v. Askew


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department

PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed from an order of the Supreme Court, Bronx County (New York), which denied its motion pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 440.40 to set aside the sentence of defendant on the ground that it was invalid as a matter of law.


OVERVIEW: Prior to defendant's sentencing, counsel requested that the sentence mandated by statute not be applied. The issue was fully briefed to the trial court, which ruled in favor of defendant. Well after the time to file a notice of appeal had passed, the State filed a motion to set aside the sentence on the ground that it was invalid as a matter of law. The court affirmed the trial court's determination. It held that the trial court could deny the State's motion because the matter was previously determined on the merits and counsel had full opportunity to present arguments germane to the issue. The court also held that the record did not indicate that the interests of justice warranted the trial court's exercising its discretion on the motion and setting aside the sentence. It held that the trial court's refusal to grant the motion to vacate the sentence was not an improvident exercise of discretion.

1128 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Rome v. New York State Health Dep't


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Fourth Department


65 A.D.2d 220; 411 N.Y.S.2d 61; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 13411



December 15, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Determination unanimously confirmed, without costs, and petition dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner city sought review of the determination of respondent Commissioner of New York State Health Department, ordering the city to submit plans for the construction of a complete water treatment facility pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 1107.


OVERVIEW: The commissioner investigated the city's water supply and determined that an outbreak of parasitic disease arose from the water supply. The commissioner held a full evidentiary hearing. He then ordered the city to submit plans for the construction of a complete water treatment facility pursuant to N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 1107. The city requested review of the determination. The court confirmed the determination and dismissed the city's petition. First, the court held that because the hearing held by the commissioner was not statutorily mandated, the court reviewed the determination under the arbitrary and capricious standard, rather than the substantial evidence test. While there was ample justification for a full evidentiary hearing, the fact that the hearing was held did not bring about the application of a different standard of review. The court further held that the commissioner clearly had a rational basis for his determination. Thus, the commissioner's order that a water treatment facility be constructed was not arbitrary or unreasonable.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the commissioner's determination to order the city to submit plans for the construction of a complete water treatment facility, following a severe outbreak of a parasitic disease caused by organisms in the city's water supply.


HEADNOTES

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- Applicable Test for Review of Administrative Order

1. The substantial evidence test is to be applied for the review of an administrative order where a hearing has been held and evidence taken "pursuant to direction by law" ( CPLR 7803, subd 4); however, where a full evidentiary hearing is conducted, but not mandated, the proper test is whether there is a rational basis for the order, i.e., the courts cannot interfere unless the action complained of is arbitrary and capricious. Accordingly, the rational basis test is the one applicable for review of an order issued by the Commissioner of Health pursuant to section 1107 of the Public Health Law, as despite the fact that the order is based upon facts adduced at a hearing, such hearing was not required by section 1107.

Proceeding against Body or Officer -- Scope of Review

2. It is well settled that the court is without power to upset the determination of an administrative tribunal [***3] on a question of fact and thus may not accord differing weight to conflicting evidence.

Health -- Unsafe Public Water Supplies

3. A determination by the Commissioner of Health, pursuant to section 1107 of the Public Health Law, ordering a city to submit plans for the construction of a complete water treatment facility has a rational basis where there is evidence that the water supply is unsafe and will continue to be so absent implementation of the measures ordered; the fact that implementation will obligate the city to expend large amounts of money does not necessitate a finding that the determination is not a reasonable improvement within the meaning of section 1107.

Health -- Unsafe Public Water Supplies

4. The conditions which could cause a municipal water supply to become a certifiable health hazard are infinite, requiring that the Commissioner of Health be given the widest flexibility, and although the powers conferred on the Commissioner by the Legislature pursuant to section 1107 of the Public Health Law are not precisely defined, drinking water standards promulgated by the Commissioner (10 NYCRR Part 72) provide a sufficient basis upon which to make [***4] a certification that a water supply is dangerous to the public health; accordingly, a determination by the Commissioner ordering a city to submit plans for the construction of a complete water treatment facility is both reasonable and lawful where there is evidence that the water supply is unsafe and will continue to be so absent implementation of the measures ordered.

Health -- Construction of Laws and Regulations Protecting Public Health

5. Laws and regulations enacted to protect the public health should be given an extremely liberal construction so as to further the accomplishment of their objectives.
