State v. Hudson Home for Aged


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


62 A.D.2d 1121; 405 N.Y.S.2d 319; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11225



April 27, 1978 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff State brought an action against defendant home, seeking injunctive relief. The home filed a counterclaim, seeking a determination of unconstitutionality. Both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The Supreme Court, Albany County (New York), entered judgment, granting the State's motion and denying the home's cross-motion. The home appealed.


OVERVIEW: The home was a private not-for-profit corporation which operated a facility for the aged. The home did not receive public funds. The State brought the action after the home refused to accept and conspicuously post an operating certificate forwarded to it by the board of social welfare as required by N.Y. Exec. Law § 759. In response, the home maintained § 759 and the rules and regulations promulgated thereunder authorizing the board of social welfare to regulate facilities for the aged not in receipt of public funds, were in violation of N.Y. Const. art. XVII, § 2. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment that granted the State's motion for summary judgment and denied the home's similar motion because the requirement for an operating certificate was justifiable pursuant to the police power of the State.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that granted the State's motion for summary judgment and denied the home's cross-motion for summary judgment, without costs.

 

1165 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People ex rel. Thorpe v. Clark


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


62 A.D.2d 216; 403 N.Y.S.2d 910; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10442



April 17, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Three judgments of the Supreme Court, Kings County, each entered October 24, 1977, reversed, on the law, without costs or disbursements, and applications granted to the extent of directing that the proceedings be remanded to the Family Court for further proceedings consistent with the opinion of Mr. Justice O'Connor. In the interim appellants are to remain in the custody of the respondent.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant law guardian on behalf of juvenile petitioners challenged judgments of the Supreme Court, Kings County (New York), which dismissed writs of habeas corpus and committed petitioners to the custody of respondent county hospital center pending transfer of custody to the commissioner of mental hygiene.


OVERVIEW: Appellant law guardian on behalf of juvenile petitioners challenged judgments dismissing writs of habeas corpus and committing juvenile petitioners to the custody of respondent county hospital center pending transfer of custody to the commissioner of mental hygiene. The court held that the Fam. Ct. Act § 231, which gives the family court jurisdiction to deal with a mentally retarded child, mandates that an involuntary commitment be in accordance with the Mental Hyg. Law § 33.27. The court held that petitioners received a full hearing with all the requisite due process guarantees on the issue of their competency to proceed to adjudication hearing. However, after they were found to be incompetent the court ordered, without any further proceeding, their involuntary commitment. Thus, because the required procedures were not followed, the court reversed and remanded accordingly.


OUTCOME: The judgments of the trial court committing petitioners to custody of respondent hospital were reversed and remanded because after petitioners were found to be incompetent, the family court ordered, without any further proceeding, their involuntary commitment to hospital, thus failing to follow the procedures as required by applicable law.


HEADNOTES

Infants -- Juvenile Delinquent -- Judicial Certification of Mentally Retarded Child

1. The Family Court has jurisdiction to commit a juvenile to the Department of Mental Hygiene if it is alleged [***3] that the juvenile is a delinquent in a situation where, prior to being adjudicated pursuant to article 7 of the Family Court Act, he is found to be incompetent to defend himself in such proceeding, provided such jurisdiction is exercised in a manner consistent with the juvenile's constitutional right to due process.

Statutes -- Effect of Subsequent Statute

2. Generally, a subsequent statutory provision prevails over a pre-existing and irreconcilably conflicting provision which is not expressly repealed.

Infants -- Judicial Certification of Mentally Retarded Child

3. Section 231 of the Family Court Act (L 1976, ch 853, § 4), providing for judicial certification of mentally retarded children, was not repealed by implication with the recodification of the Mental Hygiene Law in 1972, inconsistent in that it contains no such provision (Mental Hygiene Law, § 33.27), since although section 231 was re-enacted in 1976 in substantially the same language as its predecessor, it was enacted as an entirely separate statute and therefore will prevail over an inconsistent pre-existing statute.

Infants -- Judicial Certification of Mentally Retarded Child

4. A court-ordered [***4] involuntary juvenile commitment pursuant to section 231 of the Family Counrt Act must follow the procedures contained in section 33.27 of the Mental Hygiene Law.

Infants -- Juvenile Delinquent -- Judicial Certification of Mentally Retarded Child

5. Where a juvenile is found to be incompetent to proceed to an adjudication hearing, and the court finds that the youth is a threat to society as well as to himself, the Family Court can consider the request by the Law Guardian for a competency examination pursuant to CPL article 730 as an application sufficient to satisfy the requirements of section 33.27 of the Mental Hygiene Law.

Infants -- Judicial Certification of Mentally Retarded Child

6. In the absence of compliance with the procedures of section 33.27 of the Mental Hygiene Law, the use of sections 255 and 231 of the Family Court Act alone to authorize a commitment fails to guarantee a uniform procedure so that juveniles, subject to being committed involuntarily to the Department of Mental Hygiene, will be subject to the same procedures and the same due process and equal protection of the law.

 

1166 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Hochberg


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


62 A.D.2d 239; 404 N.Y.S.2d 161; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10444



April 13, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant public official sought review of a decision of the Supreme Court in Albany County (New York), which upon a jury verdict entered judgment convicting defendant of the crimes of corrupt use of position or authority in violation of N.Y. Elec. Law § 448, unlawful fees and payments in violation of N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 77, and attempted fraudulent and wrongful affecting of the result of a primary election N.Y. Elec. Law, § 421(5).


OVERVIEW: Defendant assemblyman allegedly sought to obtain a promise from an opponent not to run in an election against defendant. Plaintiff State of New York contended that defendant offered his opponent money and other incentives in exchange for his promise not to run against defendant. Defendant was charged with the crimes of corrupt use of position or authority in violation of N.Y. Elec. Law § 448, unlawful fees and payments in violation of N.Y. Pub. Off. Law § 77, and attempted fraudulent affecting of the result of a primary election N.Y. Elec. Law, § 421(5). The trial court entered a judgment convicting defendant and sentenced him accordingly. Defendant appealed his convictions and sentences. On appeal, the court affirmed, finding there was sufficient evidence to support the jury's findings that defendant accepted a thing of value, that he acted with corrupt intent, and that defendant deliberately attempted to cause his opponent to refrain from entering the primary in exchange for job offers and money. The appellate court further determined that based upon the facts and all other relevant information considered by the trial court, defendant's sentence was not excessive.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of elections offenses was affirmed. The statutes under which defendant was convicted were not unconstitutional, the jury properly found defendant failed to meet his burden of proving the affirmative defense of entrapment, and alleged prosecutorial misconduct did not rise to the level of reversible error.


HEADNOTES

Elections -- Fraudulently Affecting Result of Primary Election -- Corrupt Use of Position or Authority -- Unlawful Fees and Payments

1. There was sufficient evidence from which a jury might find that a legislator made offers of staff jobs and a campaign contribution to another which were contingent upon the latter's promise not to run against him in a primary election; that he accepted a "thing of value or of personal advantage", i.e., the other's promise not to run, in violation of section 77 of the Public Officers Law, which makes it a felony for a member of the Legislature to ask, receive, or consent or agree to receive any money, property or thing of value or of personal advantage for performing any discretionary act which he may exercise by virtue of his office; that he used or promised to use his authority as a legislator to secure the staff jobs with the intent and purpose of obtaining the other person's promise to refrain from entering the primary, in violation of section 448 of the [***4] Election Law, which prohibits any person, while holding public office, from corruptly using or promising to use his official authority to secure public employment upon consideration that the person so to be benefited or any other person will give or use their political influence or action in behalf of any candidate, or upon any other corrupt condition or consideration, and that he deliberately attempted to cause the other person to refrain from entering the primary in exchange for the said offers, in violation of section 421 (subd 5) of the Election Law, which prohibits the fraudulent or wrongful doing of any act tending to affect the result of a primary election.

Crimes -- Unlawful Fees and Payments

2. Under section 77 of the Public Officers Law, which makes it a felony for a member of the legislature to ask, receive, or consent or agree to receive "any money, property or thing of value or of personal advantage" for performing any discretionary act which he may exercise by virtue of his office, the benefit accruing to the public official need not be tangible or monetary to constitute a bribe.

Elections -- Fraudulently Affecting Result of Primary Election -- Corrupt  [***5] Use of Position or Authority -- Unlawful Fees and Payments

3. Statutes under which a legislator, charged with offering staff jobs to another in exchange for the latter's promise not to run against him in a primary election, was convicted of corrupt use of position or authority (Election Law, § 448), unlawful fees and payments (Public Officers Law, § 77), and attempted fraudulent and wrongful affecting of the result of a primary election (Election Law, § 421, subd 5), place reasonable restrictions on the use of official position and authority which is corruptive of a free elective process, and are sufficiently definite to give a reasonable person notice of the nature of the acts prohibited; they are not unconstitutionally overbroad or inhibitive of First Amendment activities relative to free political discussion, nor are they unconstitutionally vague.

Crimes -- Affirmative Defense of Entrapment

4. Under section 40.05 of the Penal Law, the affirmative defense of entrapment can be made out only when the active inducement or encouragement of a public servant or of a person acting in co-operation with a public servant creates a substantial risk that the offense would [***6] be committed by a person not otherwise disposed to commit it, and the defendant has the burden of proving such defense by a preponderance of the evidence.

Crimes -- Evidence Secured Through Unauthorized Investigation of Special Prosecutor

5. Participants in conversations with a defendant had a legal right to record those conversations, and violated no rights of the defendant in doing so, and the evidence thus obtained against him was not rendered inadmissible because it was secured during an investigation improperly being conducted by a Special Prosecutor prior to the issuance of an executive order authorizing him to do so.

Crimes -- Indictment

6. Where allegations in an indictment were not elements of the crime charged but were mere surplusage, the deletion of which did not alter the theory of the indictment, their deletion by the trial court did not constitute reversible error.

Crimes -- Sentence

7. Sentencing is a matter resting within the sound discretion of the trial court, and the sentence imposed should not be reduced on appeal unless there is an abuse of that discretion.

 

1167 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Gold v. Shapiro


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Second Department


62 A.D.2d 62; 403 N.Y.S.2d 906; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10418



April 7, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Petition granted, without costs or disbursements, and the respondent Justice is prohibited from signing an order effectuating his determination to grant bail to respondent Gonzalez following the latter's conviction of, and sentence for, a class A-III felony (see People v Gonzalez, decided Feb. 17, 1978).


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed a proceeding, pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law art. 78, requesting a petition to prohibit respondent from signing an order effectuating his decision to grant defendant's application for a stay of execution of judgment and for bail pending appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of criminal sale of a controlled substance and received a class A felony sentence. Defendant filed a notice of appeal and applied to respondent Justice for a stay of execution and bail. Respondent Justice declared that N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 530.50, which provided that bail pending appeal was not available to a defendant who had received a class A felony sentence, was an unconstitutional violation of defendant's right to equal protection of the laws. Respondent granted defendant's application, but withheld signing the order to afford petitioner district attorney the opportunity, pursuant to N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law art. 78, to request a petition prohibiting him from signing the order. On appeal, the court granted the petition, holding that N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 530.50 was constitutional and that respondent was without power to consider defendant's application. Defendant had no constitutional right to bail after conviction. N.Y. Crim. Proc. Law § 530.50 was rationally related to the legislature's determination that drug offenders constituted an insular class who posed a peculiar threat to society and required especially severe punishment.


OUTCOME: The court granted petitioner's request and held that respondent had no power to consider defendant's application for bail pending appeal because defendant had received a class A felony sentence and, pursuant to the applicable statute, was not entitled to bail pending appeal.


HEADNOTES

Bail -- Prohibition of Bail

1. CPL 530.50, which provides that bail, pending appeal, is not available to a defendant who has received a class A felony sentence, is rationally related to a legitimate State interest and is, therefore, constitutional.

Bail -- Prohibition of Bail -- Constitutional Law

2. There is no constitutional right to bail after conviction.

Bail -- Right to Bail

3. Although a State may afford an appellant the opportunity for bail, traditionally and acceptedly, there are offenses of a nature as to which a State properly may refuse to make provision for a right to bail.

Crimes -- Sentence

4. In determining [***3] the relative harshness of a sentencing scheme it is inappropriate to look only at the minimum period of incarceration; courts necessarily review the full scope of the available punishment and the primary component must be the potential maximum punishment.

Bail -- Prohibition of Bail

5. The recognized rational basis of isolating convicted drug offenders and deterring potential offenders, which supports the severe penal sanctions applied to class A-III felons, necessarily supports the constitutionality of a statute precluding the entitlement of postconviction bail to class A-III felons ( CPL 530.50).

Crimes -- Right to Bail

6. The determination of which offenses shall be bailable is primarily a question for the Legislature and exists independently of whether the particular offender is a serious absconding risk.

Bail -- Prohibition of Bail

7. A Judge is without power to consider an application for bail after a conviction and sentence for a class A-III felony. ( CPL 530.50.)

 

1168 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Long Island Home, Ltd. v. Whalen


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


62 A.D.2d 23; 404 N.Y.S.2d 53; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10413



April 6, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, on the law, without costs, plaintiff's motion for summary judgment denied, defendants' motion for summary judgment granted and paragraph (b) of subdivision 4 of section 2801-a of the Public Health Law declared to be applicable to plaintiff and its stock and constitutional as so applied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Department of Health challenged an order of the Supreme Court in Albany County (New York) denying its motion for summary judgment and granting summary judgment in favor of plaintiff nursing home in the nursing home's action seeking an injunction against the enforcement of N.Y. Pub. Health Law § 2801-a(4)(b).


OVERVIEW: A stockholder in the nursing home died and the Department notified the nursing home that the transfer of her stock was subject to the approval of the Public Health Council under § 2801-a(4)(b) because the decedent owned more than ten percent of stock. The nursing home sought to enjoin the enforcement of § 2801-a(4)(b), and both parties filed motions for summary judgment. The trial court denied the Department's motion for summary judgment and granted the nursing home's motion. The Department sought review, and the court reversed. The court held that the application of § 2801-a(4)(b) was not unconstitutional because the regulation of who owned healthcare facilities in order to protect the public was a permissive state objective. Assuming that stock could be transferred freely would have rendered the state's police power ineffective. The court granted the Department's motion for summary judgment and denied the nursing home's motion. The court declared § 2801-a(4)(b) applicable to the nursing home.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the order granting summary judgment in favor of the nursing home and denying summary judgment in favor of the Department. The court granted the Department's motion for summary judgment and denied the nursing home's motion.


HEADNOTES

Health -- Corporations Operating Hospitals -- Approval of Stock Transfers

1. Paragraph (b) of subdivision 4 of section 2801-a of the Public Health Law, which requires approval by the Public Health Council if there is a transfer of 10% or more of the stock of a corporation [***2] operating a hospital, defined as including nursing homes, or if any transfer results in control of more than 10% of the corporation's stock by any person, and which provides that, in the absence of such approval, the operating certificate of such hospital shall be subject to revocation or suspension, relates only to stock transfers in the future, and does not retroactively impair any vested right of a corporation which was operating a hospital prior to its effective date or of such a corporation's stockholders; it is applicable to such a corporation and its stock, and is constitutional as so applied.

Health -- Corporations Operating Hospitals -- Approval of Stock Transfers

2. The regulation of who may own hospitals and nursing homes in order to protect the public is a permissible State objective, and a statute ( Public Health Law, § 2801-a, subd 4, par [b]), which is applicable to corporations operating hospitals both prior to and after its effective date, and which requires approval by the Public Health Council if there is a transfer of 10% or more of the stock of such a corporation, or if any transfer results in control of more than 10% of such a corporation's stock [***3] by any person, and subjects the operating certificate of such hospital to revocation or suspension if the approval is not obtained, is reasonably related to that objective.

 

1169 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


In re Everett S.


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


62 A.D.2d 1069; 403 N.Y.S.2d 802; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11166



April 6, 1978 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner mother appealed an order of the Family Court of St. Lawrence County (New York), which granted petitions by respondent, the department of social services, for the guardianship and custody of two of her children and extended the placement with the department of two other children of the mother.


OVERVIEW: The mother contended that the former N.Y. Soc. Serv. Law § 384(7) was unconstitutional and that the record did not support the disposition of the trial court. She claimed that a finding of mental retardation under the statute violated her right to a trial by jury; denied her due process rights; the statute was vague; and required a finding by the trial court that the department had made diligent efforts to strengthen the parental relationship or shown that such efforts would have been detrimental to the children. The court held that state had never recognized a right to a jury trial on the issue of mental competence; the procedures of the former § 384 fully afforded the mother her due process rights; the statute was not vague; and the requirement that the department make diligent efforts to strengthen the parental relationship was not applicable to proceedings under § 384. Further, the court concluded that the findings of the trial court were amply supported by the record, and the disposition of the trial court was in the best interest of the children.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the family court.

 

1170 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


New York Public Interest Research Groups, Inc. v. Levitt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


62 A.D.2d 1074; 404 N.Y.S.2d 55; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 11171



April 6, 1978 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a citizen taxpayers' group and others, appealed from a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York) that granted a motion filed by defendants, the state comptroller and others, to dismiss their complaint seeking declaratory and injunctive relief to declare void an agreement for bond financing of the construction of a state office complex.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs commenced the action to declare void an agreement for the construction of a state office complex. Plaintiffs asserted that the agreement was invalid in that it was made in violation of the constitutional prohibition barring the state from incurring debts in the absence of a law authorizing the debt that had been submitted to the voters at a general election. Plaintiffs also sought to permanently restrain the state comptroller from disbursing state tax funds to the county. The trial court granted defendants' motion to dismiss the complaint. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment of the trial court. The trial court properly held that the action was time-barred because the cause of action arose when the allegedly unconstitutional contract was executed, and plaintiffs had the right to file an action as citizen taxpayers under N.Y. Gen. Mun. Law § 51 at any time after the execution of the contract. The action was also barred by laches because plaintiffs did not act diligently in asserting their rights in prosecuting this action for declaratory and injunctive relief, and their delay prejudiced defendants by increasing construction costs and other financial obligations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial decision granting defendants' motion to dismiss plaintiffs' complaint seeking declaratory and injunctive relief to declare void an agreement for bond financing of the construction of state office buildings.

 

1171 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Ellenbogen v. Levitt


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


61 A.D.2d 559; 403 N.Y.S.2d 566; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10099



March 30, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Determination confirmed, and petition dismissed, without costs.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner retiree brought a N.Y. C.P.L.R. art. 78 proceeding to review a determination of respondent State Comptroller (New York), which, after a hearing, denied the retiree's application for a recalculation of his retirement allowance.


OVERVIEW: When the retiree first became a member of the New York State Employees' Retirement System, the retirement plan was based on an age of 60. He later elected to become a member of the age 55 retirement plan and, later still, elected to become a member of the Legislative and Executive Retirement Plan. When he applied for retirement, the retiree requested that his retirement allowance be based on his final average salary for the immediately preceding three-year period. The retirement system calculated the retirement allowance based on the retiree's last three calendar years during which he received his highest compensation, subjected to N.Y. Retire. & Soc. Sec. Law § 80-a(d)(3), which provided that the total pension paid was not to exceed 75 percent of the retiree's final average salary. The retiree argued that the pension limitation provision was unconstitutional as applied because, when he became vested in his retirement benefits, the benefit plan did not contain any limitation. The court disagreed, holding that the retiree's election to become a member of the Legislative and Executive Retirement Plan was a waiver of his vested pension rights.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed the comptroller's decision and dismissed the retiree's petition.


HEADNOTES

Civil Service -- Retirement -- Legislative and Executive Retirement Plan

1. Paragraph 3 of subdivision d of section 80-a of the Retirement and Social Security Law which limits the pension paid to a member of the Legislative and Executive Retirement Plan (LERP) to 75% of a member's final average salary is not unconstitutional (NY Const, art V, § 7) as applied to a retiree who had become a member of the New York State Employees' Retirement System (system) in 1931, the benefits of which system did not contain any limitation, and thereafter had elected to become a member of the LERP in 1968. His waiver of vested pension rights was not against public policy.

Civil Service -- Retirement -- Final Average Salary

2. If a retiree, who was a member [***2] of the New York State Employees' Retirement System, had a vested right under that system to select the period determinative of his "final average salary", he waived that benefit by electing membership in the Legislative and Executive Retirement Plan (LERP) and it is not unreasonable or irrational to conclude that a computation of "final average salary" under the LERP is limited to three consecutive calendar years.

 

1172 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


Saxton v. Carey


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, Third Department


61 A.D.2d 645; 403 N.Y.S.2d 779; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10106



March 29, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Order modified, on the law, without costs; complaint reinstated, and judgment directed to be entered in favor of the defendants declaring that the 1978-1979 State budget and accompanying appropriation bills as submitted by the Governor to the Legislature are constitutional, and, as so modified, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizen-taxpayers sought review of a judgment of the Supreme Court at Special Term (New York), which converted the motion to dismiss filed by defendants, governor and others, to a motion for summary judgment and held the citizen-taxpayers' cause of action was premature and that the state budget was sufficiently itemized to show what money was expended for what purpose.


OVERVIEW: The citizen-taxpayers alleged that the 1978-1979 state budget and accompanying appropriation bills as submitted by the governor to the legislature was unconstitutional on the ground that it did not comply with N.Y. Const. art. VII, §§ 1-4. The court affirmed the lower court's decision that the cause of action was premature because the probability of a budget being enacted, which did not correct the alleged defects of the submitted bills, was great. Considering the size of the present work force of the State of New York and the fact that the executive budget was in excess of 11.5 billion dollars, the court concluded that the appropriation bills accompanying the budget were not sufficiently itemized to show what money was to be expended and for what purpose. The court also stated that the transfer provisions in the current appropriation bill was not unconstitutional where the present appropriation bill only permitted intra-program transfers and not interprogram transfers and intra-program transfers were necessary for the purpose of department management of funds. The court modified the lower court's judgment and converted the motion to dismiss to a motion for summary judgment.


OUTCOME: The court modified the lower court's judgment and reinstated the citizen-taxpayers' complaint. The court then ordered that judgment be directed in favor of defendants declaring that the 1978-1979 state budget and accompanying appropriation bills as submitted by the governor to the legislature was constitutional. The court then affirmed the lower court's judgment as modified.


HEADNOTES

State -- State Budget -- Constitutional Law

1. If budget bills as submitted by the Governor are not sufficiently itemized, and thereby repugnant to article VII of the State Constitution, the Legislature is not empowered to correct the deficiencies; although the Legislature may add its own itemized appropriations to the submitted [***3] bills, it is constitutionally prevented from striking out items from the submitted appropriation bills and substituting more detailed appropriations. (NY Const, art VII, § 4.)

Actions -- Premature Action

2. Where budget bills submitted by the Governor are allegedly not sufficiently itemized, and where there is a probability that a State budget will be enacted which does not correct these alleged defects, since the Legislature is not empowered to correct such deficiencies, an action brought by citizen-taxpayers contesting the constitutionality of the State budget and accompanying appropriation bills is not premature.

Actions -- Premature Action

3. The provisions of subdivision 1 of section 123-b of the State Finance Law which confer standing upon a citizen-taxpayer to maintain an action for declaratory and injunctive relief against a State officer who is causing or is "about to cause a wrongful expenditure, misappropriation, misapplication, or any other illegal or unconstitutional disbursement of state funds" is supportive of the conclusion than an action brought by citizen-taxpayers to contest the constitutionality of budget and appropriation bills submitted [***4] by the Governor as being insufficiently itemized, is not premature.

State -- State Budget -- Constitutional Law

4. Although the specifics or lack thereof in appropriation bills supportive of a proposed State budget are essentially the concern of the Governor and Legislature, where a citizen-taxpayer raises an issue regarding the constitutionality of the appropriation bill, as submitted, judicial intervention is compelled at least to the extent of resolving the constitutional issue.

Constitutional Law -- State Budget

5. An appropriation bill containing a transfer provision which provides that "[notwithstanding] the provisions of the state finance law, appropriations shall be controlled by the total of the amount provided for each program and within each program by the total of the amount provided for personal service expenses and by the total of the amount provided for maintenance and operation expenses" only permits intraprogram transfer and not interprogram transfer and, therefore, is not unconstitutional.

 

1173 of 2465 DOCUMENTS


People v. Robertson


[NO NUMBER IN ORIGINAL]


Supreme Court of New York, Appellate Division, First Department


61 A.D.2d 600; 403 N.Y.S.2d 234; 1978 N.Y. App. Div. LEXIS 10103



March 27, 1978 



DISPOSITION: Judgment, Supreme Court, Bronx County, rendered on January 16, 1976, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the Supreme Court-Bronx County (New York) on drug charges. At the suppression hearing, the trial court denied suppression of evidence and found that there was probable cause for a search warrant.


OVERVIEW: The landlord entered the premises after receiving complaints from the neighbors and found a box with suspicious contents. He called the police and showed them the box. The premises were secured, the box was taken for contents testing, and a search warrant was obtained. During the execution of the warrant, a substantial quantity of drugs and drug paraphernalia was found. The court held that: (1) the landlord's warrantless entry and identification of a box with suspicious contents was proper; (2) there was probable cause for a search warrant even without an affidavit from the landlord; (3) the defendant's key to, and familiarity with, the apartment, along with other circumstantial evidence, conclusively linked the defendant's exercise of dominion and control over the apartment to justify the jury's finding that the defendant had constructive possession of the drugs found there; (4) no reasonable theory, other than the defendant's guilt, accounted for defendant's actions; and (5) the strength of the links in the chain of circumstantial evidence mandated affirmance of the defendant's conviction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the defendant's conviction on drug charges.


HEADNOTES

 [***2] Crimes -- Unlawful Search and Seizure -- Seizure of Narcotics by Police Based upon Landlord's Entry into Apartment

1. The warrantless removal of a box containing suspected narcotics and drug paraphernalia by the police from a virtually vacant upstairs apartment of a two-family residence at the instigation of the landlord, who entered the premises and discovered the box after receiving complaints about the occupants of the second-floor apartment from the downstairs tenant, was proper, justifying the issuance of a search warrant based on the affidavit of a police officer which led to the discovery of additional narcotics in the upstairs apartment. The landlord, in notifying the police after discovering the narcotics, properly acted both as a citizen mindful of his duty and as a landlord mindful of his own self-interest in reporting the possible use of the premises "for any illegal trade, manufacture or other business" (Real Property Law, § 231). Even assuming that the removal of the box and its contents by the police for field tests was improper, the fact that the landlord intended to disclose the presence of suspected narcotics to the police and to cause an inspection to [***3] be made, coupled with the observation by the police of the contents of the box, amply justified the issuance of the search warrant.

Crimes -- Controlled Substances -- Constructive Possession of Drugs

2. The circumstantial evidence of defendant's guilt, including the fact that he possessed the keys to the apartment in which narcotics were found, rent receipts and a business card from the realty agent who rented the apartment, justifies defendant's conviction for possession of drugs and use of drug paraphernalia beyond a reasonable doubt. Where narcotics are found on premises under the "control" of defendant, it may properly be inferred that defendant had both knowledge and "control" of the narcotics sufficient to sustain a conviction for unlawful possession of narcotics. Control of the premises is not necessarily limited to the tenant of rented premises since control can be delegated or shared. The circumstantial evidence conclusively linked defendant with the exercise of dominion and control over the apartment and as such justified the jury's finding that defendant had constructive possession of the drugs discovered therein.

Crimes -- Circumstantial Evidence

 [***4] 3. An appellate court reviewing a verdict based largely on circumstantial evidence need not be convinced to an absolute certainty that there exists no possible hypothesis consistent with defendant's innocence in order to sustain the conviction thereon. It is sufficient if the circumstantial evidence is "direct, substantial and unequivocal" and the inferences to be drawn from the circumstances are "logically compelling". It is for the jury to determine if the circumstances exclude, to a moral certainty, every other "reasonable" hypothesis consistent with defendant's innocence beyond a reasonable doubt. If there is a fair conflict in the evidence such that different inferences can properly be drawn from it, the determination of the jury will not be set aside unless it is clearly against the weight of the evidence or appears to have been influenced by passion, prejudice, mistake or corruption.
